1001 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Association of Pennsylvania State College & University Faculties v. Kline


No. 1284 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


58 Pa. Commw. 164; 427 A.2d 684; 1981 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1367


December 10, 1980, Argued  
April 1, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Association of Pennsylvania State College and University Faculties v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and Caryl M. Kline, Secretary of Education of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Motion of petitioner for summary judgment granted. Arbitration award confirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner college and university faculty filed a motion for summary judgment to confirm an arbitration award made after petitioner and respondents, commonwealth and Secretary of Education, failed to negotiate a salary increase for faculty members. Respondents' cross motion for summary judgment argued that the award was advisory under the Public Employee Relations Act.


OVERVIEW: Under the court's original jurisdiction, petitioner college and university faculty and respondents, commonwealth and Secretary of Education, filed cross motions for summary judgment to determine whether an arbitration award was enforceable against respondents or merely advisory, awaiting the appropriation of funds from the legislature. The Public Employee Relations Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 1101.804, stated that parties submitted to binding arbitration were bound by the award, but that decisions that required legislative enactment to be valid were considered advisory only. The court found that an award did not become advisory until the public employer had demonstrated that the legislature had met, considered, and expressly rejected an arbitration award. Respondents' citation to a recent appropriations act that had denied funds for negotiated compensation increases was not a legislative rejection of an arbitration award. The court distinguished an arbitrated compensation increase from a negotiated increase. The court confirmed the award.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner college and university faculty's motion for summary judgment and confirmed the arbitration award. Under the Public Employee Relations Act, an award did not become advisory until the legislature met, considered, and expressly rejected to fund the arbitration award. The award was not rejected by an appropriations bill that banned the use of funds for negotiated salary increases, not arbitration awards.

 

1002 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Wilderness Industries of Maryland, Inc. v. Commonwealth, State Bd. of Motor Vehicle Mfrs., Dealers & Salesmen


No. 593 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


58 Pa. Commw. 127; 427 A.2d 1235; 1981 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1323


February 6, 1981, Argued  
March 30, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the State Board of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers, Dealers and Salesmen in case of Dean Fountain Camper Sales v. Wilderness Industries of Maryland, No. 78-MV-21.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a motor vehicle manufacturer, challenged an order of respondent State Board of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers, Dealers, and Salesmen (Pennsylvania), which suspended petitioner's license when petitioner terminated the franchise of respondent a motor vehicle dealer without giving 60 days advance notice as required by § 4(2)(xi) of the Motor Vehicle Manufacturer's, Dealer's, and Salesmen's License Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 63, § 805(2)(xi).


OVERVIEW: Respondent State Board of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers, Dealers, and Salesmen (board) ordered the suspension of the license of petitioner, a motor vehicle manufacturer, after petitioner terminated the franchise of respondent motor vehicle dealer (dealer). Section 4(2)(xi) of the Motor Vehicle Manufacturer's, Dealer's, and Salesmen's License Act (Act), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 63, § 805(2)(xi), required that franchised dealers receive 60 days notice before the termination of a franchise. Petitioner argued that the statute was not applicable because the parties did not have a written franchise agreement, but that if it was, a letter sent to respondent dealer nine months before the termination complied with the notice requirement. The court noted that a written agreement was not necessary to impose the requirements of the Act; instead, it looked to the business relationship of the parties and found a franchise existed. The letter placed respondent dealer "on probation" for a number of reasons and warned respondent dealer to make changes, but did not comply with the 60 day notice requirement of the Act. Respondent board's suspension of petitioner's license was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent State Board of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers, Dealers, and Salesmen suspending the license of petitioner, a motor vehicle manufacturer. Although they did not have a written franchise agreement, the business relationship between petitioner and respondent motor vehicle dealer (dealer) indicated that a franchise existed, and petitioner's only letter to respondent dealer was not a notice of termination.

 

1003 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Cianfrani v. Commonwealth, State Employees Retirement Bd.


No. 2722 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


57 Pa. Commw. 143; 426 A.2d 1260; 1981 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1258


June 5, 1980, Argued  
March 18, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued March 3, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original jurisdiction in case of Henry J. Cianfrani v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, State Employees' Retirement Board.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied. Judgment entered for respondents and against petitioner.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state employee sought reargument of his motion for summary judgment on the issue of whether § 5953 of the State Employees' Retirement Code, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5953, unconstitutionally impaired petitioner's retirement contract.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner state employee filed a motion for summary judgment, which challenged the constitutionality of § 5953 of the State Employees' Retirement Code, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5953; petitioner claimed the statute impaired his retirement contract with the state. The court initially denied petitioner's motion, and petitioner filed a motion for reargument and filed a new stipulation which established that he had been a member of the State Employees' Retirement Fund for a period of 16 years prior to October 7, 1975. The court again denied petitioner's summary judgment motion, and entered judgment for respondent retirement board. The court found that § 5953 did not unconstitutionally impair petitioner's retirement contract. The court found that the state could exercise such powers as were necessary for the general good of the public, though contracts previously entered into between individuals might be negatively affected by the state's actions.


OUTCOME: On reargument, the court denied petitioner state employee's motion for summary judgment because § 5953 of the State Employees' Retirement Code was enacted by the state for the general good of the public, the state had the power to make such enactments, and the statute was not unconstitutional even if it had the effect of changing petitioner's prior retirement rights.

 

1004 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvania Retailers' Assos., Reliable, Inc. v. Lazin


No. 1001 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


57 Pa. Commw. 232; 426 A.2d 712; 1981 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1203


December 9, 1980, Argued  
March 3, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Pennsylvania Retailers' Association et al. v. Terry Lazin, Director, Bureau of Consumer Protection et al.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained in part and overruled in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, director and attorney general, submitted a preliminary objection in the nature of a demurrer to the petition for review of a number of debt collectors' associations, and of others interested in the field, challenging regulations of debt collectors. The petition for review submitted by petitioner associations sought injunctive and declaratory relief from the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law, 73 P.S. § 201-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The court sustained respondents', director and attorney general, preliminary objection to the petition for review submitted by petitioners debt collector's associations and of others interested in the field, challenging regulations of debt collectors. The court held that the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law Act (UTPCPL), 73 P.S. § 201-1 et seq. particularly 73 P.S. § 201-3, empowered respondent attorney general to reasonably define and establish by regulation unfair or deceptive acts or practices or unfair method of competition in addition to those expressly defined in 73 P.S. § 201-2(4). The court held that respondent attorney general could delegate this power to the Bureau of Consumer Protection as a part of the Department of Justice pursuant to 73 P.S. § 201-3.1. The court overruled respondent's demurrer, holding that debt collection was a trade or commerce within the meaning of the UTPCPL and the facts would determine whether compliance with particular regulations was so expensive that petitioners' property interest in their accounts had been taken.


OUTCOME: The court overruled respondents', director and attorney general, preliminary objection to the petition for review holding that debt collection was a trade or commerce. The court sustained respondents' objection to petitioners debt collector's associations challenge to regulations of debt collectors holding that respondent attorney general was empowered to reasonably define and establish unfair or deceptive acts or unfair method of competition.

 

1005 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Villa, Inc. v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 199 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


57 Pa. Commw. 221; 426 A.2d 1209; 1981 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1207


October 9, 1980, Argued  
March 3, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County in case of The Villa, Inc. v. The Zoning Hearing Board of Old Forge Borough, No. 118 March Term, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the determination of the municipal zoning hearing board to deny appellant's challenge to the validity of an ordinance that rezoned appellant's property, preventing the development of the property into mobile home courts. Appellant claimed that the ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of the trial court's order affirming municipal zoning hearing board's (board) denial of appellant's challenge to the validity of an ordinance rezoning appellant's property. On appeal, appellant claimed that improper procedures were followed in the adoption of the ordinance and that the ordinance was unconstitutional in that it constituted a de facto exclusion of mobile home parks and it was arbitrary, unreasonable, and confiscatory in application because it was directed at appellant's property. The court affirmed the lower court's order, finding no abuse of discretion or error of law by the board. The court determined that the amount of land available for mobile home park use did not indicate a de facto exclusion, and concluded that the ordinance in question was not exclusionary in effect. The court held that the prior owners of appellant's property did not preserve for review the issue of the propriety of procedures in enactment of the ordinance. Finally, the court found that there was no evidence of discriminatory special legislation directed at appellant and that the rezoning bore a substantial relationship to the general welfare of the community.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, finding that the zoning ordinance preventing the development of appellant's property into mobile home courts was constitutional in that it was not a de facto exclusion of mobile home parks and the rezoning was not directed specifically at appellant and bore a substantial relationship to general community welfare.

 

1006 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Beckert v. American Federation of State, County & Municipal Employees


No. 2362 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


56 Pa. Commw. 572; 425 A.2d 859; 1981 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1161; 113 L.R.R.M. 2937


June 4, 1980, Argued  
February 11, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in the case of The Honorable Paul R. Beckert, individually and on behalf of the Judges of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County v. American Federation of State, County and Municipal Employees, District Council 88, AFL-CIO and Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections overruled; motion for summary relief granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judges of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County sought original jurisdiction in their motion for summary relief to enjoin Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board from assuming jurisdiction over an unfair labor practice charge made by respondent employees union.


OVERVIEW: A clerk of the district justice filed a grievance for her discharge from her employment. Respondent employees union adopted her cause, charging petitioner judges of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County with violations of the Public Employee Relations Act (PERA) and seeking to have the grievance heard by the Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board. Under the court's original jurisdiction, petitioners filed a motion for summary relief, asking for the board to be enjoined from reviewing the claim of unfair labor practices. The court granted the injunction, finding that to allow the board's review would violate the doctrine of separation of powers. Because the court was responsible for all aspects of its employees, the only proper forum for review of employee grievances was within the judicial branch of government. Although the court found that PERA granted some rights to judicial employees, it did not immunize such employees from the inherent judicial power of discharge.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board could not exercise jurisdiction over the underlying employee discharge matter brought by respondent employees union. The board was enjoined from hearing the matter because the doctrine of separation of powers dictated that grievances with the courts should only be resolved by the courts.

 

1007 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Ballou v. State Ethics Com.


No. 1013 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


56 Pa. Commw. 240; 424 A.2d 983; 1981 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1071


September 9, 1980, Argued  
January 22, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued December 10, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original jurisdiction in case of Richard Ballou v. State Ethics Commission, et al.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney filed a petition for review seeking injunctive and declaratory relief from respondent ethics commission's requirement that petitioner file a statement of his financial interests. Respondent filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer.


OVERVIEW: Respondent ethics commission, via statute, required public officers and employees to file statements of their financial interests. Petitioner attorney, counsel for certain municipal officers and the like, filed a petition for review seeking injunctive and declaratory relief from this requirement which respondent declared applied to municipal solicitors like petitioner. Respondent filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer. The court overruled respondent's preliminary objections because a portion of the regulation infringed upon the Pennsylvania Supreme Court's inherent and exclusive power to regulate the conduct of attorneys and violated the State Constitution. The court did not agree with petitioner that the regulation did not apply to him because he was an independent contractor. Nor did the court agree with petitioner that the regulation violated his right of privacy.


OUTCOME: The court overruled respondent ethics commission's preliminary objections to petitioner attorney's complaint because respondent's regulation requiring public officers and employees to file statements of their financial interests infringed on the Pennsylvania Supreme Court's exclusive power to govern the conduct of persons privileged to practice law in Pennsylvania and violated the state's constitution.

 

1008 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Kremer v. State Ethics Com.


No. 721 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


56 Pa. Commw. 160; 424 A.2d 968; 1981 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1080; 22 A.L.R.4th 230


September 9, 1980, Argued  
January 20, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued December 10, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original jurisdiction in the case of I. Raymond Kremer v. State Ethics Commission, et al.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objection overruled; respondent directed to file answer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judge sought injunctive and declaratory relief to prevent respondents, the ethics commission, the attorney general, and a county district attorney, from enforcing the financial disclosure provisions of the Ethics Act (Act), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 65, § 401 et seq., and which would declare the Act, particularly as it required judges to file statements of financial interests, unconstitutional. Respondent ethics commission filed a demurrer.


OVERVIEW: The legislature passed the Ethics Act (Act), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 65, § 401 et seq., which applied to public officials. Under §§ 4(d), (5) of the Act, public officials were required to make certain financial disclosures. Pursuant to the Act, respondent state ethics commission (commission) distributed to judges for completion and filing forms of statements of financial interests. Petitioner judge brought an action in the court's original jurisdiction to enjoin respondents from enforcing the financial disclosure provisions of the Act as against judges, and to declared the provisions unconstitutional. Respondent commission filed a demurrer. Agreeing with petitioner, the court overruled the preliminary objections of respondent commission and directed the commission to file an answer to petitioner's action within 30 days. The court found that the financial disclosure provisions could not be constitutionally applied to judges because under Pa. Const. art. V, § 10(a), only the supreme court could govern the conduct of judges in the performance of their work.


OUTCOME: The court held the financial disclosure provisions of the ethics law could not be constitutionally applied to judges because the state supreme court had the inherent and exclusive power to regulate judge conduct.

 

1009 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Klesh v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 2064 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


55 Pa. Commw. 587; 423 A.2d 1348; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1944


October 9, 1980, Argued  
December 24, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of Public Welfare in the case of Appeal of Frank Klesh, dated August 22, 1979.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner welfare recipient appealed from an order of the Department of Public Welfare (Pennsylvania) which affirmed an amended order of the department's hearing and appeals unit denying a request for the replacement of food stamps not received by petitioner and finding petitioner ineligible for food stamps.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner welfare recipient participated in the food stamp program with eligibility being due, in large part, to high monthly medical expenses which were deductible in computing income under the then applicable law. An authorization to purchase (ATP) food coupons for February, 1979 was mailed but, according to petitioner, was never received. Petitioner did not report them lost but requested a hearing in May 1979 to determine if he was entitled to a replacement. Under a new law effective March 1979, the deduction for high medical expenses was replaced with a standard deduction. Petitioner was found to be ineligible as a result of this change in the law. The court agreed with an administrative finding that because petitioner did not report that the ATP was lost until May 1979, he was not entitled to a replacement. The court also concluded that the law was neutral on its face and found no evidence of purposeful discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the administrative finding that petitioner welfare recipient was not entitled to a replacement authorization to purchase (ATP) food coupons and that he was ineligible for such a program. The court concluded that the medical expense deduction in computing income for food stamp eligibility purposes was constitutional.

 

1010 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Christian School Asso. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Labor & Industry


Nos. 925 C.D. 1979, 926 C.D. 1979, 932 C.D. 1979, 939 C.D. 1979, 940 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


55 Pa. Commw. 555; 423 A.2d 1340; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1946


September 9, 1980, Argued  
December 23, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Bureau of Employment Security in the case of In Re: Christian School Association of Greater Harrisburg, Account No. 22-19991; In Re: Christian School of Grace Baptist Church, Account No. 21-10783; In Re: Northumberland Christian School, Account No. 49-9289; Frankford Friends School, Account No. 71-94840; and In Re: Germantown Friends School, Account No. 71-94847.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed from the decision of the Pennsylvania Department of Labor and Industry (Pennsylvania) that they were subject to the provisions of the Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Law and, therefore, should be assessed unemployment contributions.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were five private religious schools. Respondent determined that each school was subject to the provisions of the Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Law and that each school should therefore be assessed unemployment contributions. Petitioners argued that they fell within the language of an exemption in the unemployment compensation law for certain religious organizations. The court held that each of the five schools satisfied the first part of a two part test because they operated primarily for a religious purpose, even though the organizational distinctions were offensive to the free exercise clause of the first amendment. The first part of the test remained operative despite the infirmity of the second part, i.e., that of being operated, supervised, controlled or principally supported by a church or convention or association of churches.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the determination that petitioners should be assessed unemployment contributions because they were operated primarily for a religious purpose, even though certain organizational distinctions were offensive to the free exercise clause of the first amendment.

 

1011 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Myers v. Commonwealth


No. 668 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


55 Pa. Commw. 509; 423 A.2d 1101; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1975


September 11, 1980, Argued  
December 22, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Dan Maurice Myers and Barbara Jean Myers v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Revenue.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter was before the court to rule on the preliminary objections filed by respondent Department of Revenue to petitioner's suit which sought a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of § 339 of the Tax Reform Code of 1971 (Tax Code), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 7339.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners sought a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 7339. Petitioners also requested the court to enjoin respondent Department of Revenue (Department) from assessing taxes against petitioners. The department filed preliminary objections challenging the subject matter jurisdiction of the court because the exclusive jurisdiction of the matter lied within the department's administrative tribunals. The court agreed with the department. The tax code provided an appeal procedure for petitioners to challenge sales and personal income tax assessments through the department's Board of Appeals and Finance and Revenue. Thus, the initial phases of tax assessment appeals were within the exclusive jurisdiction of the department's boards. Petitioners' constitutional challenge to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 7339 was not one that went to the basic validity of the tax statute. Instead, petitioners alleged certain procedural defects in the statute which administrative tribunals were competent to adjudicate. Thus, the matter was within the exclusive jurisdiction of the department's administrative tribunals.


OUTCOME: The court sustained respondent Department of Revenue's preliminary objection because the constitutional challenge presented in petitioners' suit was within the exclusive jurisdiction of respondent Department of Revenue's administrative tribunals. The court dismissed petitioners' petition.

 

1012 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Zemprelli v. Thornburgh


No. 973 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


55 Pa. Commw. 330; 423 A.2d 1072; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1936


September 10, 1980, Argued  
December 16, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Edward P. Zemprelli, State Senator v. Richard L. Thornburgh, Governor.



DISPOSITION: Respondent's motion dismissed. Petitioner's motion granted as outlined.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a motion for summary judgment arguing that respondent was required to fill vacancies in offices within 90 days of the first day of the vacancy under Pa. Const. art. IV, § 8(b), without an option of inaction.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was a member of the state senate. Respondent was the governor of the state. Petitioner argued that respondent was required to fill vacancies in offices within 90 days of the first day of the vacancy, without an option of inaction. The court held that the 90-day time limit of Pa. Const. art. IV, § 8(b), was mandatory in relation to respondent when he exercises his power to fill vacancies. However, the 90-day time limit is not applicable where the existence of a vacancy is precluded by an incumbent lawfully holding over. Moreover, the constitutional provision is mandatory only with respect to time. The court also held that judicial estoppel and the doctrine of laches were not effective defenses in the case. Accordingly, the court dismissed respondent's motion for summary judgment, and granted petitioner's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner's motion for summary judgment because respondent was required to abide by the 90-day constitutional time limit when he exercised his power to fill vacancies in office, absent the preclusion of a vacancy by an incumbent lawfully holding over.

Quirk v. Schuylkill County Municipal Authority


No. 15 T.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


54 Pa. Commw. 619; 422 A.2d 904; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1831


September 8, 1980, Argued  
November 20, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Robert T. Quirk, Leonard Hoak, General Association to Stop Pollution, Inc., Sierra Club -- Pennsylvania Chapter and Lancaster Environmental Action Force v. Schuykill County Municipal Authority, Crown American Corporation and Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, No. S-339-1979.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objection in the nature of a motion to dismiss sustained. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Municipal Authority, corporation and the commonwealth filed a preliminary objection and sought dismissal of plaintiffs' case, asserting that plaintiff could not challenge a land transfer between Municipal Authority and corporation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an amended complaint in equity against defendant Municipal Authority, corporation and the commonwealth, challenging the transfer of a tract of land. The state legislature approved the transfer of the tract from Municipal Authority to corporation in exchange for a parcel of land containing a dam. The amended complaint alleged that the legislature's action violated certain provisions of the Pa Const. art. I, § 27, and requested the court to declare void the deed from Municipal Authority to corporation and to order corporation to reconvey the tract to Municipal Authority, to enjoin Municipal Authority from conveying the tract to any third parties, to declare the legislature's action unconstitutional, and to enforce the penalties and equitable remedies set forth in 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3946.20, against Municipal Authority. Defendants raised a preliminary objection asserting lack of standing and lack of an adequate remedy at law. The court sustained the objection and dismissed the case finding that the legislature acted within its rights and noting that the commonwealth was the only party authorized to enforce the statute at issue.


OUTCOME: The court sustained defendant Municipal Authority, corporation, and the commonwealth's preliminary objection to plaintiff's suit to declare a transfer of land from Municipal Authority to corporation void and dismissed the suit, holding that plaintiffs did not have standing to object to said land transfer.

 

1014 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


McKenna v. Commonwealth, State Employees' Retirement Board


No. 2626 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


54 Pa. Commw. 338; 421 A.2d 1236; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1787


April 8, 1980, Argued  
October 23, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of J. Frank McKenna, Jr., an individual, on behalf of himself and all others similarly situated and Frederick G. Weir, an individual, on behalf of himself and all others similarly situated v. The State Employees' Retirement Board and Richard L. Witmer, in his capacity as Executive Secretary of the State Employees' Retirement Board and Robert E. Casey, in his capacity as Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Summary judgment for plaintiffs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retired judges filed a class action suit against defendant Pennsylvania State Employees' Retirement Board requesting the court to determine the validity of certain legislative modifications of the state employees' retirement program or the validity of the administrative application of those modifications insofar as they related to the retirement pensions of the named plaintiffs and others similarly situated.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff retired judges were adversely affected by certain legislative modifications of the state employees' retirement program. Plaintiffs disputed the modifications and the validity of the administrative application of those modifications. Plaintiffs filed a class action against defendant Pennsylvania State Employees' Retirement Board as well as motions for summary judgment to declare unconstitutional code provisions which purported to reduce the multiples by which benefits were calculated. Plaintiffs argued that the provisions impaired their pension rights in violation of their property and contractual rights as protected the state and federal constitutions. Plaintiffs also asserted that defendants misinterpreted the code. On review, the court focused on whether the Pennsylvania legislature had the legal power to reduce plaintiffs' retirement benefits. The court found that plaintiffs gained a vested right to have their retirement allowances as ascertained prior to the applicable legislation. The court concluded that the legislative provisions at issue violated Pa. Const. art. I, § 17 by impairing the obligation of contracts. The motion for summary judgment was granted.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff retired judges' motion for summary judgment against defendant Pennsylvania State Employees' Retirement Board was granted because plaintiffs had a vested right to have their retirement allowances as ascertained prior to the applicable legislation. The legislative provisions at issue violated the state constitution by impairing the obligation of contracts.

 

1015 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Picariello v. Commonwealth


No. 21 T.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


54 Pa. Commw. 252; 421 A.2d 477; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1780


September 8, 1980, Argued  
October 15, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Samuel O. Picariello v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Department of Revenue of Pennsylvania, and Milton Lopus, former Secretary of Revenue of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Department of Justice of Pennsylvania, and "The Guide" and Fry Communications, Action in trespass in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County.



DISPOSITION: Certain preliminary objections sustained; certain preliminary objections overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff media subject filed an action in trespass against defendant, commonwealth, Departments of Revenue and Justice, former Secretary of Revenue, and two media companies, that alleged defamation, invasion of privacy, and intentional inflicting of emotional distress. Defendant commonwealth entities and officer's preliminary objections of sovereign immunity under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5110(a) and demurrer were before the court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff media subject filed a complaint that alleged defamation, invasion of privacy, and intentional infliction of emotional distress against defendants, commonwealth, Departments of Revenue and Justice, former Secretary of Revenue, and two media companies, in regard to a letter that was transferred from defendants, commonwealth entities and officer, to defendant newspaper company that, in turn, published it. Defendants, commonwealth entities and officer, filed preliminary objections in the nature of claim of absolute immunity and demurrers. The preliminary objections of absolute immunity were overruled of defendant officer due to his position as a commonwealth officer because no party's pleading addressed whether public policy was or was not served by release of the letter to the press. Defendant commonwealth entities' preliminary objections were sustained as plaintiff's complaint failed to allege a cause of action within any of the eight exceptions to the bar of sovereign immunity provided by 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5110(a). The actions against defendant commonwealth entities were barred. Plaintiff failed to show § 5110(a) denied him U.S. Const. XIV protection.


OUTCOME: The court sustained preliminary objections that asserted sovereign immunity as to causes of action against defendant commonwealth government entities. Preliminary objections as to defendant former Secretary of Revenue that asserted absolutely immunity as a commonwealth officer were overruled because no party's pleadings had addressed whether public policy was or was not served by the release of the information to the media.

 

1016 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Widoff v. Disciplinary Board of Supreme Court


No. 881 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


54 Pa. Commw. 124; 420 A.2d 41; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1748


June 4, 1980, Argued  
October 2, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Mark P. Widoff, Consumer Advocate, et al. v. The Disciplinary Board of the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania and Charles V. Henry, III, Chairman, John C. Anderson, Vice-Chairman, Dennis C. Harrington, Herbert J. Johnson, Jr., Raymond Pearlstine, Pasco L. Schiavo, Frank J. McDonnell, Mary Bell Hammerman, and Robert C. Daniels, Members, Individually and in their official capacity.



DISPOSITION: Motion for declaratory judgment denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an attorney who formerly headed the Office of Consumer Advocate, sought a declaratory judgment that Pa. Code of Professional Responsibility DR 7-107(H), limiting the right of lawyers during the pendency of administrative proceedings to make certain public statements, was unduly vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The court ruled that an "actual controversy" existed so as to justify its consideration of the declaratory judgment requested by petitioner, the attorney who headed the Office of Consumer Advocate, as to the constitutional validity of Pa. Code of Professional Responsibility DR 7-107(H), which limited the right of lawyers during the pendency of administrative proceedings to make certain public statements. Explaining, the court acknowledged the conflict that existed between petitioner's free speech rights and the threat he received of disciplinary action. These rights could be restricted when necessary to ensure the due process rights of parties involved in proceedings in which petitioner was acting as counsel, the court said. Rejecting an assertion of overbroadness, the court ruled that the rule's limitation on comments "reasonably likely" to interfere with public hearings was properly restricted in time and person to ensure fairness. Nor was the proscription on out-of-court statements "on any other matter" affecting a hearing's fairness impermissibly vague, because when read in context with other barred conduct petitioner was placed on notice of statements viewed as prejudicial.


OUTCOME: Declaratory judgment sought by petitioner, an attorney who headed the consumer advocate's office, to have a disciplinary rule, which limited the right of lawyers during administrative proceedings to make certain public statements, declared unconstitutional denied, as petitioner's free speech rights must yield to litigants' due process rights when the rule was construed as being neither overbroad nor vague.

 

1017 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Robson v. Biester


No. 218 Misc. Dkt. No. 2


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


53 Pa. Commw. 587; 420 A.2d 9; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1715


September 19, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
September 3, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Ronald Robson v. Edward Biester, Attorney General of the State of Pennsylvania et al.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for review seeking to restrain respondents, attorney general, bureaus of corrections, and state prison, from transferring him to another prison, to expunge misconduct charges, and to restore his status as a good prisoner. Petitioner claimed he was denied due process and there was insufficient evidence to support the findings of the prison tribunal.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for review to restrain respondents, attorney general, bureau of corrections, and state prison, from transferring him to another prison, to expunge misconduct charges, and to restore his status as a good prisoner claiming he was denied due process and their was insufficient evidence to support the findings. A prisoner was not entitled to a hearing prior to transfer unless such transfer was punitive in nature and for disciplinary reasons. Because petitioner did not allege those factors, he failed to state a claim on the transfer issue. Due process was satisfied in prison disciplinary proceedings when the inmate was afforded written notice of the violation charged in advance of the hearing, a written statement by the factfinders to the evidence relied on, and the right to call witnesses on his own behalf. Because petitioner did not aver that he was denied those safeguards, due process was not violated. A decision by a prison tribunal was not a final adjudication within the court's jurisdiction absent an allegation that the action was arbitrarily or capriciously imposed and, because that was not alleged, the petition for review was dismissed.


OUTCOME: Petition for review by petitioner inmate of an order of respondents, attorney general, bureau of corrections, and state prison, was affirmed because petitioner's due process rights were not violated. The court found that the action of respondents was not arbitrarily or capriciously imposed and, absent that finding, a decision by a prison tribunal was not a final adjudication within the court's jurisdiction.

 

1018 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Kenney v. Keebler Co.


Nos. 1730 and 1821 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


53 Pa. Commw. 507; 419 A.2d 210; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1700


June 4, 1980, Argued  
August 21, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in cases of Keebler Company v. George T. Kenney et al., No. 1156 March Term, 1976; No. 861 March Term, 1977 and No. 2860 February Term, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Real estate owners in the City of Philadelphia who had objected to tax assessments of the Board of Revision of Taxes for 1975-1978 sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which rejected the method the taxpayers proffered for determining the ratio of assessed value to market value and accepted the board's method with some modifications. Both sides excepted to the trial court's order.


OVERVIEW: Taxpayers, owners of real estate, objected to the assessments imposed by the Board of Revision of Taxes. The taxpayers and the board proposed different methods for determining the proper ratio of assessed value to market value of properties. The trial court accepted the method proposed by the board, subject to some modifications. This method involved determining the actual ratio between assessed and fair market values by breaking the properties into six land use categories and then computing various ratios. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the novel method of calculation adopted by the trial court was too complex to be accepted by other than the most sophisticated property owners. Further, the methodology deviated substantially from the common and accepted methodology. The court ruled the trial court's exercise of equity jurisdiction was improper because the statutorily provided remedies had not been shown to be inadequate and no constitutional question had been demonstrated, as provided by 72 P.S. § 5341.1 et seq. The court thus reversed the trial court's order and remanded the matter for a determination of the appropriate ratios.


OUTCOME: Having determined that the method of calculation adopted by the trial court was too complex, the court entered an order reversing the orders of the court of common pleas and remanded the case to the lower court to determine the appropriate ratios consistent with the court's opinion.

Am. Fed'n of State v. Commonwealth


No. 1734 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


53 Pa. Commw. 415; 417 A.2d 1315; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1694; 110 L.R.R.M. 2303


June 6, 1980, Argued  
August 11, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of American Federation of State, County and Municipal Employees, AFL-CIO, by its Trustee ad Litem, Gerald W. McEntee v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania et al., and No. 1920 C.D. 1979, in case of Joint Bargaining Committee of the Pennsylvania Employment Security Employees' Association and The Pennsylvania Social Services Union, AFL-CIO, by its Trustee ad Litem, Andrew Stern v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania et al.



DISPOSITION: Respondents' motions denied. Petitioners' motions granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner unions sought summary judgment in their suit against respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania to enjoin respondent from enforcing the new 17-cent auto mileage reimbursement rate under 65 P.S. § 371. Respondent also sought summary judgment, asserting that the existing collective bargaining agreements with petitioners were superseded by § 371 due to the provisions of 43 P.S. § 1101.703.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner unions executed collective bargaining agreements with respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, allowing for an auto mileage reimbursement rate of 18.5 cents. The legislature later enacted a maximum 17-cent reimbursement rate under 65 P.S. § 371. Petitioners sought summary judgment to enjoin respondent from enforcing the new maximum, and respondent sought summary judgment, claiming that the existing agreements were superseded due to the provisions of 43 P.S. § 1101.703, which required that the agreements contain nothing which would violate statute. The court granted petitioners' summary judgment, and denied respondent's motion, finding that the existing agreements could not be affected by 65 P.S. § 371 because to do so would impair the obligation of contract under Pa. Const. art. 1, § 17, and U.S. Const. art. I, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner unions' summary judgment and denied respondent commonwealth summary judgment, holding that the existing collective bargaining agreements that contained a higher auto mileage reimbursement rate could not be impacted by the new statutory cap without impairing the obligation of contract.

 

1020 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Appeal of Harrisburg School Dist.


No. 797 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


53 Pa. Commw. 299; 417 A.2d 848; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1660


June 6, 1980, Argued  
July 30, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County in case of Appeal of the Redevelopment Authority of the City of Harrisburg From the Dauphin County Board of Assessment and Revision of Taxes, No. 5371 S 1978.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant local taxing authorities challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which found that property owned by the Redevelopment Authority of the City of Harrisburg was not subject to local taxation absent a specific delegation of taxing authority by the general assembly to appellants.


OVERVIEW: Appellant local taxing authorities sought review of the trial court's decision that property of the Redevelopment Authority of the City of Harrisburg was exempt from local taxation. The court first concluded that the Authority was an agency and instrumentality of the Commonwealth. The court noted that the Urban Redevelopment Law, 35 P.S. §§ 1701 et seq. (1945), contained no specific delegation of power to local authorities to tax property owned by entities created under the law. The court then stated the general rule that property owned by the Commonwealth was not generally subject to taxation unless the general assembly adopted statutes that specifically authorized local municipalities to do so. The court found that the public property owned by the Authority was not subject to taxation by appellants because the general assembly had not provided a specific delegation of the taxing powers to appellants. The decision of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was affirmed. Public property owned by an agency and instrumentality of the Commonwealth was not subject to taxation because of the absence of a specific statutory delegation of taxing power.

Nichols v. Corry


No. 1082 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


53 Pa. Commw. 248; 417 A.2d 836; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1633


May 5, 1980, Argued  
July 25, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County in case of G. Kenneth Nichols v. The City of Corry, No. 4261-A-1976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania), which determined that appellant was ineligible for retirement from appellee city's police force.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officer filed a petition for a declaratory judgment after appellee city's council refused to declare him eligible for pension benefits. Appellant sought to have a pension ordinance declared unconstitutional and an amending ordinance declared void. The trial court denied the petition. Appellant sought review of the trial court's decision, arguing principally that the trial court erred in excluding evidence of the city council's interpretation of the pension ordinances and evidence of the city council's intent in passing the ordinance amendment. The court affirmed, concluding that such evidence was inadmissible because members of a legislative body, such as a city council, were not subject to inquiry incident to any challenge of the body's legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which determined that appellant police officer was ineligible for retirement from appellee city's police force, because the trial court did not err in excluding evidence of the city council's interpretation of, or intent in passing, the pension ordinances appellant sought to challenge.

Cianfrani v. Commonwealth, State Employees' Retirement Bd.


No. 2722 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


57 Pa. Commw. 135; 417 A.2d 279; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1635


June 5, 1980, Argued  
July 24, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original jurisdiction in case of Henry J. Cianfrani v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, State Employees' Retirement Board.



DISPOSITION: Motion of petitioner denied. Judgment entered for respondents and against petitioner.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner retiree sought summary judgment in his declaratory judgment and mandamus action against respondent State Employees' Retirement Board (Pennsylvania) after respondent began assigning to petitioner's former employer, the Senate, setoff retirement funds under 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5953 (1975) to replace government funds wrongfully spent by petitioner during his term as a legislator.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner retiree served as a legislator in the Senate of the Commonwealth from 1966 to 1977, after which he began receiving retirement benefits. Petitioner later pled guilty to various crimes and the Senate found that $ 30,232 in Senate funds had been wrongfully spent by petitioner during his tenure by hiring "ghost" employees. The Senate directed respondent State Employees' Retirement Board under 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5953 (1975) to setoff the funds necessary to reimburse the commonwealth from the retirement benefits being paid to petitioner. The board complied and petitioner brought an action for declaratory judgment and a writ of mandamus, filing a motion for summary judgment. The court denied petitioner's motion, finding that petitioner had not qualified for retirement benefits before 1975 and was therefore subject to the setoff provisions of § 5953. The court further found that the procedures used to initiate the setoff complied with due process when balancing petitioner's interests against the commonwealth's need to conserve its fiscal and administrative resources. Finally, the court entered judgment in favor of respondent, although it had not moved for judgment.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner retiree summary judgment in his declaratory judgment action to prevent the setoff of funds from his retirement benefits necessary to reimburse the commonwealth for monies he wrongfully spent. The court entered judgment for respondent State Employees' Retirement Board, finding that petitioner had not qualified for retirement benefits before 1975 and was therefore subject to the statutory setoff provisions.

 

1023 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Gilbert Associates, Inc. v. Commonwealth


No. 2593 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


53 Pa. Commw. 142; 418 A.2d 783; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1970


June 4, 1980, Argued  
July 21, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in case of Gilbert Associates, Inc. v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Docket No. C-5236.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer appealed an order of the Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which computed petitioner's franchise tax in accordance with the requirements for foreign corporations in the Tax Reform Code, 72 P.S. §§ 7101 et seq. Petitioner asserted that the requirements violated the uniformity clause of Pa. Const. art. 8, § 1 and the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner taxpayer was a Delaware Corporation in Pennsylvania. Petitioner appealed the settlement by the Board of Finance and Revenue of its franchise tax. Petitioner asserted that the Tax Reform Code, 72 P.S. § 7602(a) violated the uniformity clause of Pa. Const. art. 8, § 1 and the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, by allowing domestic corporations to calculate their capital stock tax by either the three-factor formula or the single factor formula, while limiting foreign corporations to the three factor formula in calculating their franchise tax. The court affirmed, holding that the foreign franchise tax was not unconstitutional. The court found that the fact of the option given domestic corporations to calculate their capital stock tax by the three-factor method and that different rates of the same tax could not be imposed on domestic and foreign corporations, was not unconstitutional. The court noted that the capital stock tax was a tax on property, while the franchise tax was on the privilege of doing business in Pennsylvania.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the settlement of the Board of Finance and Revenue of petitioner's franchise tax because it was reasonable to impose different taxes on, respectively, domestic and foreign corporations and to require each to calculate its tax by the method required in the applicable statute.

Weaver v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Transp., etc.


No. 398 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


52 Pa. Commw. 625; 416 A.2d 628; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1612


June 6, 1980, Argued  
July 11, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Edwin Martin Weaver, Trust Book No. 44, Page 350.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania) affirming the action of respondent Department of Transportation revoking his operator's license for six years. Respondent sanctioned petitioner under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 1550 after petitioner was convicted of three vehicle related offenses.


OVERVIEW: The trial court affirmed an order revoking petitioner driver's operating privileges for six years. Respondent department of transportation revoked petitioner's operator's license after three vehicle code convictions. The convictions were for driving under the influence of alcohol or controlled substance under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3731; fleeing or attempting to elude a police officer under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3733; and leaving the scene of an accident involving damage to an attended vehicle or property under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3743. Petitioner contended that the statute imposing the suspension, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 1550, was unconstitutional; imposing consecutive suspensions for a single offense was improper; and that he should not have been sanctioned as an habitual offender. The appellate court affirmed the revocation, and held that petitioner's due process rights were fulfilled at a full hearing, that respondent had the authority to impose consecutive suspensions, and that petitioner could be designated as a habitual offender for an offense occurring within ten minutes of a previous offense.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order sustaining the revocation of petitioner driver's operating privileges. Petitioner had a full hearing that fulfilled due process requirements. Respondent department of transportation had the authority to impose consecutive suspensions. Finally, petitioner could be designated as a habitual offender for an offense occurring within ten minutes of a previous offense.

Commonwealth, Dep't of Health v. De Marco


No. 587 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


53 Pa. Commw. 1; 416 A.2d 623; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1615


June 2, 1980, Argued  
July 11, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Health, by its Secretary, Gordon K. MacLeod, M.D. v. Peter T. DeMarco, M.D.



DISPOSITION: Exceptions dismissed. Final decree entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor and intervenor company filed exceptions to a decree order that enjoined defendant from administering the drug Procaine-PVP to humans. Defendant and intervenor objected to the findings as unsupported by the evidence and that 35 Pa. Stat. § 780-111(d)(iii) was unconstitutionally vague and an unconstitutional delegation of authority by the legislature.


OVERVIEW: Defendant doctor and intervenor company challenged the issuance of an order, enjoining defendant from administering the drug procaine-pvp to humans. Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the findings as being unsupported by the evidence. Defendant also challenged the constitutionally of the statute as being vague and also as an unconstitutional delegation of authority by the legislature. The court reviewed the record and noted that there was sufficient evidence to support the court's order. The court also noted that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because defendant doctor did not have any statutory right to treat patients wholly in accordance with his personal beliefs as the state had power to regulate the practice of medicine. The court also found that the Medical Practice Act of 1974, 63 Pa. Stat. § 421.1 et seq., did not divest the court of its jurisdiction under the Controlled Substance Act, 35 Pa. Stat. § 780-125 to grant temporary or permanent injunctions restraining continued violations of that act.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed all of the exceptions of defendant doctor and intervenor company and directed the clerk to enter the chancellor's decree as a final decree of the court. The court held that the pertinent statute was not unconstitutionally vague and that there was sufficient evidence to support the order.

Ferris, Louise A. Kirner and Clara Kirner, individually and trading as Frank H. Kirner v. PPG Industries, Inc., Urban Redevelopment Authority of Pittsburgh and City of Pittsburgh, No. G.D. 79-14341.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners challenged the lack of notice and hearing on the determination by defendant, development authority, and city, which certified appellants' property as blighted pursuant to the Urban Redevelopment Law, 35 P.S. § 1701 et seq., and sought review of the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), that sustained preliminary objections to, and dismissed, plaintiffs' amended complaint in equity.


OVERVIEW: In equity proceedings, plaintiff property owners challenged the lack of notice and hearing on the determination by defendant, development authority and city, which certified plaintiffs' property as blighted pursuant to the Urban Redevelopment Law, 35 P.S. § 1701 et seq., and sought review of the trial court's order that sustained preliminary objections to, and dismissed, plaintiffs' complaint. OUTCOME: Although the appellate court found that plaintiff property owners' complaint averred sufficient facts that their properties were not located in an area that was blighted, the appellate court granted defendants' motion to dismiss the appeal because the fact that declarations of taking were filed and preliminary objections were lodged, the issues raised by plaintiffs' were to be disposed of in eminent domain proceedings.

Parise v. Commonwealth, State Board of Funeral Directors


No. 1184 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


52 Pa. Commw. 80; 415 A.2d 153; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1466


March 13, 1980, Argued  
June 6, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Board of Funeral Directors in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Carmine J. Parise and Son Funeral Home, No. 76-FU-454.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner director appealed an order of the State Board of Funeral Directors (Pennsylvania), which denied petitioner's application for approval of a new preparation room across the street from the main funeral home building.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed respondent board's denial of petitioner directors' application to construct a new preparation room across the street from the main building of the funeral home. The court held that it was not error for respondent to apply a statute amended after the date of an application for a permit, which was the basis for the denial, because the statute was a codified long-standing interpretation by respondent, 63 P.S. § 479.1 et seq., which was in effect prior to petitioner's initial application for approval. The court held that the denial of the application was not an unconstitutional taking of his property without compensation because the regulation was reasonably related to the public health and welfare of the community. The court found that respondent was properly concerned about alleviating the trauma and disconcertment that would result if the public was continually subjected to the sight of human remains being transported across a public street on a stretcher. The court found that the regulation would reduce the likelihood of traffic congestion and avoid potential accidents involving dead bodies.


OUTCOME: The court held that it was not error for the lower court to affirm respondent board's denial of petitioner director's application to construct a preparation room across the street from the funeral home because it was not an unconstitutional taking of his property when it was reasonably related to the public health and welfare, and reduced the potential trauma sustained by citizens being involved in accidents with dead bodies.

Board of Comm'rs v. Lukens

51 Pa. Commw. 576; 415 A.2d 118; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1441

May 29, 1980, Decided

Cyrus, individually and as bargaining representatives of Montgomery County Detectives, and Montgomery County Detectives, in their own right v. Board of Commissioners of Montgomery County, No. 78-13295.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Commissioners of Montgomery County sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), directing appellant to enter into collective bargaining with appellee detectives, pursuant to Act 111, 43 P.S. § 217.1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellee detectives, through their representatives, requested that appellant Board of Commissioners of Montgomery County enter into collective bargaining with them. Appellant refused, and appellees filed a complaint in mandamus in which they alleged that Act 111, 43 P.S. § 217.1 et seq. required appellant to bargain. Appellant filed an answer challenging inter alia the constitutionality of Act 111. At the conclusion of trial court proceedings, a final order was entered directing appellant to enter into collective bargaining with appellees' representatives. The court affirmed, ruling first that the trial court did not err in entering a peremptory judgment following a hearing on the pleadings. The court held that Pa. R. Civ. P. 1098 authorized the trial court's action. The court held that appellees were policemen within the meaning of Act 111 and that mandamus was the proper remedy to compel bargaining where their right to bargaining was clear. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, directing appellant Board of Commissioners of Montgomery County to enter into collective bargaining with appellee detectives. The court held that mandamus was the proper remedy to compel bargaining where appellees' right to bargaining was clear, and that appellant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of statutory provisions concerning the rights of its employees.

 

1030 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. Commonwealth


No. 654 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


51 Pa. Commw. 404; 414 A.2d 743; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1412


March 10, 1980, Argued  
May 16, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Edward H. Fisher, No. 77-11,173.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of violating the Lycoming County, Pa., Subdivision and Land Development Ordinance and ordered that he pay a $ 650 fine and the costs of prosecution.


OVERVIEW: The Lycoming County, Pa., Subdivision and Land Development Ordinance prohibited the sale of land before a final plat was approved by the county. Before the approval of a final plat, defendant sold several acres of land to a corporation, and he was subsequently convicted of violating the ordinance. On appeal, defendant claimed that because he did not subdivide his land with reference to or by other use of a plat, he did not violate the ordinance. He also alleged that the ordinance was an unconstitutional restraint on his freedom to use his land, and that his right to a speedy trial was denied. The court affirmed, holding that the ordinance applied to defendant's conduct, as it not only prohibited subdividing land "with reference to a plat" but contained the all-inclusive words "or otherwise." The court found that the ordinance was a reasonable exercise of the government's police power to ensure that land was not developed in a way adverse to the environment or the public. The court found no speedy trial violation, as defendant's case was called and a jury selected within the 180-day period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for violating a land use ordinance, because defendant violated the ordinance by selling property before the approval of a final plat, he failed to meet his burden of showing that the ordinance was unconstitutional, and he was not denied his right to a speedy trial.

American Family Life Assurance Co. v. Insurance Dep't of Commonwealth


No. 1552 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


51 Pa. Commw. 247; 414 A.2d 166; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1389


April 8, 1980, Argued  
May 8, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of American Family Life Assurance Company of Columbus v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Insurance Department and Harvey Bartle, III, Insurance Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents commonwealth, insurance department, and insurance commissioner filed preliminary objections in the trial court (Pennsylvania) to petitioner insurance company's suit to enjoin enforcement of regulations establishing minimum standards for individual accident and sickness insurance policies.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner insurance company filed suit against respondents commonwealth, insurance department, and insurance commissioner to enjoin enforcement of regulations establishing minimum standards for individual accident and sickness insurance policies and to declare portions of the Individual Accident and Sickness Insurance Minimum Standards Act (Act), 40 P. S. § 776.1 et seq. unconstitutional because they delegated legislative power to respondent commissioner. Respondent commissioner filed preliminary objections seeking to have the complaint dismissed on the ground that the court's original jurisdiction in equity was not appropriate because an adequate statutory remedy was available and had not been pursued. The court sustained the objections and held that petitioner had an adequate administrative remedy. The court found that agency review of the constitutional attack would be meaningful because examination of the regulations in the context of an actual case would provide application of the regulations to specific policies.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the preliminary objections of respondents commonwealth, insurance department, and insurance commissioner to petitioner insurance company's suit to enjoin enforcement of insurance regulations because an adequate administrative remedy was available and had not been pursued.

 

1032 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


In re Appeal by Mark-Garner Associates, Inc.


Nos. 1210 C.D. 1978, 1394 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


50 Pa. Commw. 354; 413 A.2d 1142; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1301


October 4, 1979, Argued  
April 8, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County in case of In Re: Appeal by Mark-Garner Associates, Inc., from the Decision of Bensalem Township Zoning Hearing Board Sustaining Decision of Zoning Officer of Bensalem Township, No. 77-0718-09-5.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania) directing the issuance of building permits to appellee landowner pursuant to 53 P.S. § 10508(4) and directing that appellant bear the cost of the original transcript of the record under 53 P.S. § 11008(2).


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the trial court's order directing the issuance of building permits to appellee landowner, whose final plan for a condominium was approved by appellant township before appellant reduced the allowable density of condominium units. Stating that once the three-year period of 53 P.S. § 10508(4) expired, appellee stood in the same position as any other landowner as to zoning requirements, it held that appellee had no vested right to complete its project in violation of applicable ordinances because it had not acted in reliance upon permits already issued. It rejected appellee's argument that § 10508(4) was unconstitutional, noting that the statute did not require a development's completion within three years, merely that if any of the governing ordinances were changed, they could be applied only after the three-year period. In the absence of permits and without a vested right to the issuance of additional permits, it stated, it did not see how appellee's constitutional rights were violated by the time limitation. It affirmed the trial court's decision that appellant should bear the cost of the original transcript of the record under 53 P.S. § 11008(2).


OUTCOME: Finding that appellee landowner had no vested right to complete its project in violation of applicable ordinances after appellant township reduced the allowable density of condominium units, the court reversed the trial court's order directing the issuance of building permits to appellee. It affirmed the trial court's order holding appellant responsible for the cost of the original transcript of the record.

 

1033 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Midway Coal Co. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources


No. 2797 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


50 Pa. Commw. 326; 413 A.2d 1139; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1270


December 5, 1979, Argued  
April 2, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County in case of Department of Environmental Resources, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Midway Coal Company, No. 1099 of 1977.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant coal company challenged a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County (Pennsylvania), which found it guilty of discharge of airborne dust from its property in violation of the Air Pollution Control Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Department of Environmental Resources filed a criminal complaint against appellant coal company charging it with violating the Air Pollution Control Act, 35 P.S. § 4008. It alleged appellant caused the discharge of airborne dust from its property. Appellant challenged its conviction and argued the conviction could not rest on subjective testimony of the witnesses. The court found that appellee was required to use a scientific test, if one was available. However, appellee showed that no accepted scientific test existed for measuring emissions from an open area. The court also found sufficient subjective evidence there were discharges of dust that could have been avoided. On appellant's challenge that the statute was unconstitutionally vague, the court held that the specific enumeration of contaminants in the statute was sufficient to put appellant on notice that its actions caused air pollution. Thus, the decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision because it found the statute to be constitution and that subjective evidence was properly introduced to show that the contaminants released by appellant coal company caused air pollution in violation of the statute.

 

1034 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Millcreek


No. 413 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


50 Pa. Commw. 249; 413 A.2d 764; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1257


February 8, 1980, Argued  
March 28, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lebanon County in case of Ivan W. Martin v. Township of Millcreek, No. 3271, 1977.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lebanon County (Pennsylvania) upholding appellee township's refusal to adopt a curative amendment overturning its 10-acre-minimum one-family lot size. He argued that the requirement was exclusionary and unduly restrictive.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the lower court's order upholding appellee township's refusal to adopt the curative amendment overturning its 10-acre-minimum one-family lot size proposed by appellant landowner, who sought to subdivide his tract. It agreed with the lower court that appellant had not shown that the 10-acre minimum excluded any portion of the population entirely from the township, noting that the minimum applied to only a third of the township's area and that the other residential districts were subject to a one-acre lot area minimum. It found, however, that the minimum requirement did not have the required substantial relationship to the public welfare and therefore had an unduly restrictive impact, rejecting appellee's argument that the minimum was necessary to avoid pollution caused by on-site septic systems. Noting that previous cases had struck down requirements of two, three, or four acres, it concluded that as a means to protect the public interest, the 10-acre minimum here was no more reasonable than these.


OUTCOME: Finding that appellee township's requirement that one-family lots be a minimum of 10 acres was unduly restrictive, though not exclusionary, the court reversed the lower court's order upholding appellee's refusal to adopt the curative amendment overturning the 10-acre-minimum proposed by appellant landowner, who sought to subdivide his tract.

 

1035 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Ritz v. Commonwealth


No. 1108 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


50 Pa. Commw. 155; 412 A.2d 1114; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1966


February 5, 1980, Argued  
March 20, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in case of John E. Ritz and Catharine M. Ritz v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Docket No. CPIS 680.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer challenged the order of respondent Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which denied his claim for deduction of union dues and home office expenses. Petitioner contended that the union dues and home office expenses should be excluded from his taxable income because he was required to pay them as a condition of continued employment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from respondent Board of Finance and Revenue's order, petitioner taxpayer contended that his union dues and home office expenses should be excluded from his taxable income. The court disagreed and affirmed the order. The union dues were not deductible because petitioner's employment did not include an agreement by him that he would pay union dues; the dues were not expenses incurred in pursuit of petitioner's employment; and it could not realistically be said that petitioner and his employer contemplated that petitioner would use a certain portion of his salaries for the dues. Further, the home office expenses were not deductible because although petitioner's work for the union required a suitable working area, the union did not recognize that petitioner would incur any expenses in the pursuit of his union chores. Moreover, the expenses were items which petitioner would have incurred regardless of whether petitioner used the den of his home to do his union paper work.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent Board of Finance and Revenue and denied petitioner's claim for deduction of union dues and home office expenses. Neither of these expenses were contemplated in the employment agreements between petitioner and his employers as expenses that petitioner would incur in pursuit of his employment that were required to be paid with a certain portion of petitioner's salary.
