Pennsylvania State Asso. of Township Supervisors v. Commonwealth, Ins. Dep't


No. 2954 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


50 Pa. Commw. 204; 412 A.2d 675; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1251


February 6, 1980, Argued  
March 19, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Insurance Commissioner in case of In Re: Workmen's Compensation Insurance Rate Filing of the Pennsylvania Compensation Rating Bureau, Proposal C-241, Docket No. R78-7-5.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Pennsylvania State Association of Township Supervisors appealed from the order of respondent Insurance Commissioner (Pennsylvania), granting a Workmen's Compensation Insurance Premium Rate Proposal filed by intervenor Pennsylvania Compensation Rating Bureau.


OVERVIEW: The Pennsylvania Compensation Rating Bureau filed proposed rates, requesting an increase for workmen's compensation premiums with respondent Insurance Department of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. The Pennsylvania State Association of Township Supervisors filed a petition for intervention before the final order. In affirming the Insurance Commissioner's grant of the Pennsylvania Compensation Rating Bureau's workmen's compensation insurance premium rate proposal, the court held that the action was not a proper case for considering a commingling issue. The court concluded that the Insurance Commissioner's review of the proposed rate filing was adequate and sufficient under § 654 of The Insurance Company Law of 1921, 40 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 814, and Pa. Const. art II, § 1, where there was relevant evidence, as a reasonable mind might accept as adequate, to support the conclusion and where the procedures, by which the Pennsylvania Compensation Rating Bureau's proposed insurance premium rates, did not violate the constitutional prohibition against the non-delegation of the legislative function.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Insurance Commissioner's order because the Insurance Commissioner's review of the proposed rate filing was adequate and sufficient where there was sufficient evidence and where the procedures, by which the Pennsylvania Compensation Rating Bureau proposed insurance premium rates, did not violate the constitutional prohibition against the nondelegation of the legislative function.

Miller v. Commonwealth, State Employees' Retirement Board


No. 2606 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


50 Pa. Commw. 74; 411 A.2d 1300; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1228


February 5, 1980, Argued  
March 12, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Edward R. Miller v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, State Employes' Retirement Board.



DISPOSITION: Restoration of pension benefits ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a retired state employee, sought review of the order of respondent State Employees Retirement Board (Pennsylvania), which discontinued pension benefits which petitioner had been receiving in retirement. Respondent entered the order pursuant to the Public Employee Pension Forfeiture Act, 43 P.S. § 1311 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a retired state employee, was receiving state pension benefits when he pled guilty to charges of theft by extortion, arising from conduct which occurred while he was an employee of the commonwealth. Thereafter, the Public Employee Pension Forfeiture Act (Act), 43 P.S. § 1311 et seq., became effective. Respondent Public Employees Retirement Board entered an order discontinuing petitioner's pension benefits. Petitioner sought review of the order. The court reversed and ordered petitioner's pension benefits reinstated. The court held that the Act was unconstitutional because it provided retroactively that pension benefits being received by a retired state employee would be forfeited if the employee was convicted or pled guilty or no defense to a crime related to public office or public employment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of respondent State Employees Retirement Board, which discontinued pension benefits to petitioner, a retired state employee. The court reinstated petitioner's pension, holding that the law under which petitioner's pension was forfeited was unconstitutional because it provided for retroactive applicability.

Wiker v. Roux


No. 66 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


49 Pa. Commw. 513; 412 A.2d 176; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1216


February 4, 1980, Argued  
February 29, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County in case of Esther E. Wiker v. Henry J. Roux, Gerald T. Horn, Jere W. Schuler, David M. Huber and Township of West Lampeter, Equity Docket No. 18, Page 206.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee township's motion for judgment on the pleadings. Appellant had brought an action, under 53 P.S. § 65702, to restrain appellee from collecting a street light assessment and for a judgment for assessments paid. Appellee counterclaimed for unpaid light assessments.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowner brought an action to restrain appellee township from collecting a street light assessment and for a judgment for assessments paid, pursuant to the Second Class Township Code, 53 P.S. § 65702. Appellee counterclaimed for unpaid assessments and successfully moved for judgment on the pleadings. The court affirmed. First, the court rejected appellant's assertion that § 65702 imposed a 10-year limitation upon the power of appellee's supervisors to assess properties for the cost and expense of maintaining lights. The court held that the statute imposed no limitation on the number of successive 10-year contracts which may have been entered into, nor did it remotely suggest that there was a 10-year or any other limitation on the time during which properties should have been assessed for the continuing expense of the maintenance of lights. Second, appellant asserted that the supervisors did not make a consistent application of assessments. The court held that appellant's averments of her amended complaint fell far short of showing a deliberate, purposeful discrimination in the administration of light assessments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting appellee township's motion for judgment on the pleadings. The court held that the Second Class Township Code did not impose a limitation on assessment for the expense of maintaining street lights. The court also held that appellant landowner did not demonstrate discrimination in appellee's administration of its light assessments.

Burello v. Commonwealth, State Employes' Retirement System


No. 2480 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


49 Pa. Commw. 364; 411 A.2d 852; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1155


December 4, 1979, Argued  
February 20, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Employes' Retirement Board in case of Rocco A. Burello, dated September 6, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee challenged the action of respondent State Employee's Retirement Board (Pennsylvania), when it discontinued petitioner's pension benefits. Petitioner argued the Public Employee Pension Forfeiture Act, 43 P.S. § 1311 et seq., violated constitutional prohibitions against impairment of contract obligation where it provided for forfeiture of accrued pension benefits for conviction of a crime related to public employment.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee had qualified for, and was receiving, state pension benefits when he entered a plea of nolo contendere and was convicted in the federal district court of four counts of federal extortion under 18 U.S.C. S. § 1951. Thereafter, respondent State Employees' Retirement Board informed petitioner by letter that it had discontinued pension benefit payments to him effective immediately, pursuant to the Employee Pension Forfeiture Act (Act), 43 P.S. § 1311 et seq. The proceedings before the court attacked that action and the law on which it was based. Respondent's order was reversed and the matter was remanded with a direction that all pension benefits be restored retroactively. The court determined that respondent's order was an adjudication in that it was a final order by an agency that affected personal or property rights, duties, liabilities, or obligations of the parties, so that an appeal was available under 2 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 702. The court found that the Act was an unconstitutional impairment of obligation of contract because petitioner's pension benefits vested prior to the enactment of the statute and the crime committed.


OUTCOME: The order of respondent State Employees' Retirement Board was reversed and the matter was remanded with a direction that all petitioner employee's pension benefits be restored retroactively. The court held that the Public Employee Pension Forfeiture Act did, as to petitioner, effect an unconstitutional impairment of the obligation of contract.

Mosholder v. Greene County Industrial Development Corp.


No. 407 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


49 Pa. Commw. 340; 411 A.2d 1262; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1143


December 6, 1979, Argued  
February 15, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Greene County in case of William H. Mosholder and Delores McMinn, as Administratrix of the Estate of Daniel W. Mosholder v. Sherwood Builders and Greene County Industrial Development Corporation, No. 206 May Term, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Greene County (Pennsylvania) sustaining appellee/third-party defendant employer's demurrer, which alleged that it could not be joined as a third-party defendant, in appellee estate representative's trespass suit for the accident that killed its employee, based on 99 P.S. §481(b).


OVERVIEW: Decedent was killed in a job-related accident while employed by appellee/third-party defendant employer. Appellee personal representatives brought an action in trespass against appellants, owners and general contractors. Appellants then joined appellee employer as a third-party defendant, alleging that the accident site was under its direction and control. Appellee employer demurred, arguing that, as the decedent's employer, it was immune from suit under 77 P.S. § 481(b). The lower court sustained the demurrer and dismissed appellee employer. On appeal, the court affirmed, noting that adjudication of the liability of appellee employer had been foreclosed by statute. Accordingly, appellee employer could not properly be joined in the trespass action. Further, the court found that the statute was constitutional as it had been upheld on appeal.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court sustaining appellee/third-party defendant employer's demurrer to appellee estate representative's action in trespass against appellants, owners and general contractors, was affirmed because it could not be joined to a suit, based on the controlling statute from the Workmen's Compensation Laws.

Johnston v. Commonwealth, State Board of Medical Education & Licensure


No. 2692 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


49 Pa. Commw. 9; 410 A.2d 103; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1088


December 7, 1979, Argued  
January 22, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Board of Medical Education and Licensure in case of James C. Johnston, Jr., M.D., dated November 8, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner medical doctor challenged the order of respondent State Board of Medical Education and Licensure (Pennsylvania) revoking his license to practice medicine pursuant to the Medical Practice Act of 1974, 63 P.S. § 421.1 et seq., following the revocation of his license to practice in the State of Washington. Petitioner contended that 63 P.S. § 421.15(a)(4), under which the license was revoked, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner medical doctor's license to practice in the State of Washington was revoked by that state's medical licensing authority, upon charges of gross incompetence resulting in patient deaths and aiding and abetting an unlicensed person to practice medicine. Under 63 P.S. § 421.15(a)(4), respondent state board of medical education and licensure revoked petitioner's license, on the basis that his license in Washington had been revoked. Petitioner claimed the statute was unconstitutional and challenged respondent's order. The court held that the legislature's authorization of suspension or revocation following disciplinary action taken by another state against a holder of a Pennsylvania license was neither unreasonable nor arbitrary and constituted a valid exercise of the state's police power. Because respondent had no real independent ability to monitor the performance of physicians who conducted their practices out-of-state, the court viewed respondent's authority to act swiftly upon official verification of disciplinary action in another state as most salutary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent state board of medical education and licensure which revoked petitioner medical doctor's license. Respondent's authority to revoke the license based upon revocation in another state was neither unreasonable nor arbitrary and constituted a valid exercise of the state's police power.

Kremer v. Barbieri


No. 1019 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


48 Pa. Commw. 557; 411 A.2d 558; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1038


November 14, 1979, Argued  
January 18, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of I. Raymond Kremer, Charles P. Mirarchi, Jr., and Eugene Gelfand, Judges of the First Judicial District and Francis J. Catania (President Judge) and Joseph T. Labrum, Jr., Judges of the Thirty-second Judicial District and John W. O'Brien, Judge of the Fifth Judicial District and Milton O. Moss and Horace A. Davenport, Judges of the Thirty-eighth Judicial District on behalf of themselves and all other Judges similarly situated, Petitioners v. Alexander F. Barbieri, Court Administrator of Pennsylvania and Robert E. Casey, State Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Respondents.



DISPOSITION: Summary judgment for respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, individual trial judges and judges' association, and respondents, court administrator and state treasurer, filed cross motions for summary judgment on petitioners' complaint seeking a writ of mandamus directing respondents to increase trial judge salaries to the level recommended by the Commonwealth Compensation Commission, at 9 Pa. Bull. 1029.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, individual trial judges and judges' association, filed a complaint in mandamus, (in the court's jurisdiction under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 761) seeking to compel respondents, court administrator and state treasurer, to adopt the recommendations of the Commonwealth Compensation Commission published at 9 Pa. Bull. 1029 for salary increases. On cross-motions for summary judgment, the court dismissed petitioners' motion, holding that the legislature's rejection of the bill was not invalid due to conflict of interest. Pa. Const. art III, § 13 required legislators with a personal interest in any measure to disclose it, and none had done so. Also, Pa. Const. art. II, § 8 prohibited salary increases during the legislative terms on which they were voted. The court further held that the failure to increase salaries did not violate separation of powers, because the power of judicial compensation was constitutionally fixed in the legislature. Finally, the court held that mandamus was inappropriate, because respondents had no power to increase petitioners' compensation, but only administered legislative appropriations.


OUTCOME: The court denied judgment for petitioners, individual trial judges and judges' association, and entered judgment for respondents, court administrator and state treasurer, holding that the legislators had no conflict of interest, that the failure of the bill did not violate separation of powers, and that mandamus was inappropriate, because respondents could not set judicial salaries.

Bray v. Zoning Board of Adjustment


No. 175 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


48 Pa. Commw. 523; 410 A.2d 909; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1049


October 5, 1979, Argued  
January 17, 1980, Decided

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) which reversed the zoning board's denial of respondent applicants' request to establish a roller-skating rink in a shopping center district under the Philadelphia Zoning Code, § 14-309(2)(j).


OVERVIEW: Respondent applicants sought to establish a roller-skating rink in a shopping center district under Philadelphia Zoning Code § 14-309(2)(j), which allowed, by board certificate, a use of the same general character as the uses absolutely permitted in that district. Appellant city objected to the application. The court affirmed the trial court's approval of the application, finding that respondent applicants satisfied their burden of presentation and persuasion, showing their compliance with the criteria set forth in § 14-1803(1), including only a minimal increase in traffic, and finding that appellant city failed to set forth evidence of detriment sufficient to support the zoning board's denial of the requested use certificate. The board in its decision to the contrary displayed a capricious disregard of the testimony and evidence offered.


OUTCOME: Order granting respondent applicants' request to establish a roller-skating rink in a shopping center district was affirmed because respondent applicants satisfied their burden, showing compliance with the zoning code, but appellant city failed to set forth evidence of detriment sufficient to support the zoning board's denial of the requested use certificate.

Atlantic-Inland, Inc. v. Board of Supervisors


No. 29 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


48 Pa. Commw. 397; 410 A.2d 380; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1010


October 5, 1979, Argued  
January 10, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County in the case of Atlantic-Inland, Inc. v. The Board of Supervisors of West Goshen Township and Township of West Goshen, No. 300 January Term, 1975.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania) dismissing its complaint against appellee township seeking equitable relief from the ordinance of West Goshen Township, Pa. Electrical Code §§ 3(b), 6(b), on the basis that it was unconstitutional and requesting a writ of mandamus requiring appellees, township and board of supervisors, to approve appellant as an electrical inspector.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation brought complaint against appellee township requesting equitable relief from the ordinance of West Goshen Township, Pa. Electrical Code §§ 3(b), 6(b), by alleging that it was unconstitutional and seeking a writ of mandamus requiring appellees, township and board of supervisors, to approve appellant as an electrical inspector. The court found the standards for approval in § 6(d) to be not so vague as to render them unconstitutional because appellees could inquire to determine the competency of a potential inspector. The ordinance was sufficiently specific to prevent appellees from exercising their power in an arbitrary and discriminatory manner by following § 6(d). The trial court correctly refused to issue mandamus because the record contained substantial evidence of appellant making improper inspections and reports for appellees to correctly refuse to approve appellant as an inspector. The trial court correctly declined to be bound by appellees' letter denying appellant's application because the evidence was legally sufficient to support appellees' decision. The court declined to address the constitutionality of § 3(b) because this inquiry was unnecessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that dismissed appellant corporation's complaint against appellee township, which sought equitable relief from the ordinance because it was unconstitutional and that requested a writ of mandamus requiring the approval of appellees, township and board of supervisors, of appellant as an electrical inspector. The ordinance was constitutional. The trial court's denial of mandamus was based on substantial evidence.

Nagle v. Commonwealth


No. 1829 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


48 Pa. Commw. 295; 409 A.2d 525; 1980 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 995


October 2, 1979, Argued  
January 4, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Insurance Commissioner in case of In Re: Petition for Review filed August 4, 1976, on behalf of John Nagle et al. regarding Objections to Workmen's Compensation Rate Classification, Docket No. WC76-8-3.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This was an appeal from the order of the Insurance Commissioner (Pennsylvania), which failed to grant part of the relief sought by petitioners who successfully challenged a prior approved insurance premium rate classification for black lung coverage of non-mining truck drivers.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners sought review of an order of respondent insurance commissioner, which failed to grant refunds for some premiums paid before petitioners successfully challenged the insurance premium rate classification for black lung coverage of non-mining truck drivers. The reviewing court affirmed, holding that the scope of judicial review was limited to the determination of whether there was a manifest and flagrant abuse of discretion or a purely arbitrary execution of respondent's administrative duties or functions. Furthermore, the Insurance Company Law, 40 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 814, provided that respondent could withdraw his approval whenever, in his judgment, the rate was inadequate or discriminated unfairly between risks of essentially the same hazard, and was silent as to any requirement that premiums, even where based on a rate that discriminated unfairly, must be ordered refunded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Upper Moreland v. Commonwealth, Pennsylvania Dep't of Transp.


No. 2407 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


48 Pa. Commw. 27; 409 A.2d 118; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2245


September 10, 1979, Argued  
December 14, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Township of Upper Moreland and Brian Mook v. Pennsylvania Department of Transportation and James B. Wilson, Secretary of the Department of Transportation.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections partially sustained and partially dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, township and taxpayer, sought to enjoin respondent department of transportation and its secretary from using public funds for the construction of a left-hand standby turning lane.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, township and taxpayer, sought to enjoin respondent department of transportation and its secretary from using public funds for the construction of a left-hand standby turning lane on a certain road. Petitioners alleged that the proposed construction was for the sole benefit of an adjacent landowner, and was, therefore, an unlawful abuse of discretion by respondent department of transportation and was contrary to Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 11, which provided that revenue derived from taxes on gasoline sales, motor vehicle licensing, and other specified forms of taxes on transportation, be used for the public benefit. Respondent raised preliminary objections asserting a lack of capacity to sue, a demurrer, and laches. The court granted respondent's preliminary objections and dismissed petitioner township as a party because it would not have been directly harmed by the expenditure. However, the court held that petitioner taxpayer had standing to contest public spending. Thus, the court dismissed respondent's preliminary objection as to petitioner taxpayer as petitioner taxpayer fell within the rule that taxpayers had standing to contest public spending.


OUTCOME: The court held that petitioner township had standing to enjoin respondent department of transportation and its secretary from using public funds for the construction of a left-hand standby turning lane because it would not have been directly harmed by the expenditure. However, petitioner taxpayer did have standing as petitioner taxpayer fell within the rule that taxpayers had standing to contest public spending.

De Marco v. Commonwealth, State Bd. of Medical Education & Licensure


No. 1278 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


47 Pa. Commw. 500; 408 A.2d 572; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2238


April 5, 1979, Argued  
December 4, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Board of Medical Education and Licensure in case of In the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of the License to Practice Medicine, License No. MD-26088, issued August 29, 1958, to Peter Thomas DeMarco, M.D., dated May 24, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner physician appealed the decision from respondent, State Board of Medical Education and Licensure (Pennsylvania), which revoked his license to practice medicine pursuant to 63 P.S. § 421.15(a)(4) of the Medical Practice Act (1974). This was after his license had been revoked in New Jersey.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner physician was licensed in New Jersey and Pennsylvania. Petitioner's New Jersey license was revoked. Respondent State Board of Medical Education and Licensure then revoked petitioner's Pennsylvania license pursuant to 63 P.S. § 421.15(a)(4) of the Medical Practice Act (1974). That section gave respondent the authority to revoke a license of a physician who lost a license in another state. The appellate court affirmed. The court held that respondent could revoke a license on the basis of actions which occurred in another state. There was no evidence that petitioner committed acts of malpractice or violated any rules in Pennsylvania. However, a physician in Pennsylvania was under a duty to remain in good standing in another state where he was licensed in that state. If petitioner had committed the same acts in Pennsylvania, he would have lost his license. Geographical distinctions were irrelevant in determining professional conduct.


OUTCOME: The order from respondent State Board of Medical Education and Licensure suspending petitioner physician's license to practice medicine was affirmed. Petitioner's Pennsylvania license could be revoked solely on the basis that his New Jersey license had been already revoked because he was under a duty in Pennsylvania to remain in good standing in any state in which he was licensed.

Colonial Park for Mobile Homes, Inc. v. New Britain Township


No. 507 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


47 Pa. Commw. 459; 408 A.2d 1160; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2212


April 6, 1979, Argued  
November 30, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued September 12, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County in case of Colonial Park for Mobile Homes, Inc. v. New Britain Township, No. 77-1580-04-5.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mobile home park sought review of the order from the Court of Common Pleas, Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which upheld the constitutionality of the New Britain Township, Pa., Zoning Ordinance of 1974, and refused appellant's request for curative amendment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mobile home park submitted a request for curative amendment to the Board of Supervisors (Board), challenging the New Britain Township, Pa., Zoning Ordinance as unconstitutionally exclusive because it made no provision for mobile home parks within its township. The Board rejected appellant's request, and the trial court affirmed the judgment. On appeal, the court held that while it was true that the ordinance did not explicitly declare that the use of land for trailer parks was permitted, it did not explicitly prohibit such use, and appellant failed to carry its burden of proving that the ordinance excluded the establishment of mobile home parks. The court held that the ordinance did permit the establishment of a park on appellant's land, and affirmed the order from the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court that upheld the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance, and refused appellant mobile home park's request for curative amendment. The court held that appellant failed to prove its burden of proving that the ordinance excluded the establishment of mobile parks as the ordinance did not explicitly declare that the use of land for trailer parks was permitted.

 

1049 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 1968 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


47 Pa. Commw. 441; 408 A.2d 216; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2220


February 5, 1979, Argued  
November 28, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued October 2, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Department of Public Welfare in case of Appeal of Herman Foster, dated September 9, 1977.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, welfare recipient, appealed the decision from respondent, Department of Public Welfare (Pennsylvania), which upheld the ruling by the hearing examiner that petitioner and his wife were ineligible for general assistance.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner welfare recipient and his wife were on public aid. Sixty-two P.S. § 432.12(a) of the Public Welfare Code and 55 Pa. Code, § 183.64(e)(1) were adopted which required that respondent Department of Public Welfare reduce from income expenses of up to only $ 25 in determining eligibility for aid. The effect of this was that petitioner could no longer deduct the expenses of employing someone to care for his sick wife in determining their eligibility. The hearing examiner affirmed the discontinuance of aid, and respondent affirmed. The appellate court reversed and remanded. Government had the authority to discontinue welfare benefits, but it could not do so in an arbitrary fashion. The record was unclear as to why a limit was placed at $ 25. The cause would have to be remanded for a determination on the relationship between the legitimate governmental interest to the limitation. This did not necessarily mean that the new regulations were unconstitutional as petitioner contended if respondent could establish the purpose for the regulations.


OUTCOME: The order of respondent Department of Public Welfare affirming the decision by the hearing examiner to eliminate general assistance benefits to petitioner welfare recipient and his wife was reversed and remanded. Whether a rational relationship existed between new regulations setting the amount of deductible expenses in determining eligibility for aid at $ 25 and some governmental objective could not be determined from the record.

S. § 403, stated a cause of action upon its pleaded facts. Accordingly, the court overruled respondent's preliminary objections.

Pierce v. Commonwealth, Pennsylvania Bd. of Probation & Parole


No. 147 Misc. Dkt. No. 2


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


46 Pa. Commw. 507; 406 A.2d 1186; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2091


June 26, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
October 17, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Thomas Pierce v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole.



DISPOSITION: Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parolee filed a petition for review of an order of respondent Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, which revoked his parole, and respondent filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings in response.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner parolee filed a petition for review of an order of respondent Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole that revoked petitioner's parole. Respondent filed an answer with new matter, and petitioner admitted that he had been convicted of aggravated robbery, burglary, larceny, conspiracy, and receiving stolen property, among other offenses. The court granted respondent's motion for judgment on the pleadings, and held that respondent showed that it considered evidence of petitioner's rehabilitation, and that petitioner's constitutional rights were not violated where three members of respondent board heard the case as provided by law, as a quorum of the board satisfied due process requirements. Further, petitioner's arguments failed to meet the heavy burden of showing that 61 P.S. § 331.4, which authorized a majority of respondent's board to revoke the parole of any person, violated the constitution. Finally, the court found no genuine issue of material fact in petitioner's denial of two allegations in respondent's new matter because the facts disputed by petitioner simply were not material to any of the critical issues raised in his petition.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion of respondent Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole for judgment on the pleadings, and held that the facts disputed by petitioner parolee simply were not material to any of the critical issues raised by petitioner in his petition for relief, and petitioner failed to show any violations of his constitutional rights.

 

1052 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Liquor


No. 344 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


46 Pa. Commw. 490; 407 A.2d 83; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2096


June 8, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
October 16, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Adams County in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Liquor (as per attached Exhibit A) Seized in: Route 15, Adams County; In Poss: Dorothy Straley, Miscellaneous Action No. MC-20-78, Sec. 13.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state liquor control board challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Adams County (Pennsylvania), which directed that liquor purchased by appellee owner in Maryland and transported into Pennsylvania that appellant sought to forfeit pursuant to 47 P.S. §§ 6-601 to -603 be returned to appellee upon payment of Pennsylvania taxes or, if taxes were not paid, be forfeited.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state liquor control board seized two cases of liquor purchased by appellee owner in Maryland and brought into Pennsylvania in violation of 47 P.S. § 4-491(2). After a hearing, the lower court ordered that the liquor be returned to appellee upon payment of Pennsylvania taxes, but be forfeited to appellant if the taxes were not paid. On appeal, the court reversed, and held that the portion of the liquor code which was found unconstitutional by the lower court in a prior ruling was severable, such that the remainder of § 4-491(2) was valid and enforceable for purposes of the forfeiture proceeding. Thus, if appellant proved that the liquor in question was possessed in violation of § 4-491(2), the court below erred in when it ordered its return to the owner. As the record convincingly demonstrated unlawful possession, § 4-491(2) clearly was violated and the liquor, therefore, was unlawfully possessed and was subject to forfeiture.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order that required return of liquor to appellee owner, subject to forfeiture to appellant state liquor control board if taxes on it were not paid because the findings showed that the liquor code was clearly violated by appellee's transport of the liquor into Pennsylvania. The matter was remanded for the entry of an order providing for the forfeiture of the liquor to appellant.

Escofil v. Commonwealth


Nos. 167 Misc. Dkt. 1976, 2136 C.D. 1977, 2564 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


46 Pa. Commw. 475; 406 A.2d 850; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2312


September 13, 1979, Argued  
October 15, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in case of Appeal of Noel Tancred Escofil, Nos. RPIT 966, RPIT 1867 and RPIT 1459.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer appealed an order of the Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania) sustaining respondent state's assessments for petitioner's income tax deficiencies.


OVERVIEW: In a consolidated action, petitioner taxpayer appealed the affirmation of respondent state's assessment of back income taxes petitioner owed. Petitioner contended that he was not required to pay the taxes because the federal social security system was unconstitutional and adverse to biblical law. The court affirmed and held that respondent properly disallowed certain deductions petitioner claimed because they either did not have supporting data or were not related to a business or occupation for which petitioner claimed them. The court found that petitioner did not produce evidence controverting respondent's position and held that it lacked jurisdiction to hear his claims regarding the constitutionality of the federal social security system as it applied to the validity of his tax assessment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order upholding respondent state's tax assessment against petitioner taxpayer because respondent's uncontroverted evidence showed that the identified deductions claimed by petitioner lacked supporting data or were not related to a business or occupation for which they were claimed. The court did not have jurisdiction to resolve petitioner's constitutional challenge to the federal social security system.

Kastner v. Commonwealth, Pennsylvania Dep't of Transp.


No. 1708 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


46 Pa. Commw. 97; 405 A.2d 1133; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1989


March 21, 1979, Argued  
September 19, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Richard Kastner v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Pennsylvania Department of Transportation.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual sought reconsideration of his action in trespass against defendants, the commonwealth of Pennsylvania and the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation, following remand from the Supreme Court (Pennsylvania).


OVERVIEW: The court dismissed plaintiff individual's action in trespass against defendants, the commonwealth of Pennsylvania and the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation, and held that case law had not provided him with a cause of action that could not be destroyed by legislation. Plaintiff contended that the Act of Sept. 28, 1978, Pa. Laws 788, Act No. 152 (act) was unconstitutional because it retroactively destroyed his vested right in his cause of action and provided no alternative remedy for redress. The court held that the act did not impair a contractual obligation or disturb a vested right of the parties and therefore it was not unconstitutional on those grounds. The court found that the act did not violate the ex post facto provision of Pa. Const. art. I, § 17 because the act was a civil law and the ex post facto provision of § 17 applied only to penal laws.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed plaintiff individual's action because case law did not vest him with a cause of action against defendant, the commonwealth of Pennsylvania and the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation, which could not be destroyed by legislative action, and legislation affecting his action was not unconstitutional because it did not retroactively destroy his vested rights in the cause of action and it was not an ex post facto law.

Brungard v. Hartman


No. 1100 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


46 Pa. Commw. 10; 405 A.2d 1089; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1970


March 21, 1979, Argued  
September 14, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Karen R. Brungard v. John A. Hartman and Mansfield State College.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections of Mansfield State College sustained. Complaint dismissed as to that defendant. Case transferred to the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from vacation of the court's dismissal based on sovereign immunity, plaintiff student filed a complaint in trespass against defendants, school and professor, in which she alleged that she was injured by an explosion in a classroom resulting from defendant professor's negligence.


OVERVIEW: The court sustained defendant school's preliminary objection in the nature of a demurrer of plaintiff student's negligence complaint against defendants, school and professor, alleging she was injured as a result of a chemistry explosion, and dismissed the action against defendant school. The court held that defendant school had sovereign immunity under 1978 Pa. Laws 788 from plaintiff's claim because her claim did not fall within any of the categories of claims in 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5101(b) as to which immunity had been waived. The court transferred plaintiff's claim against defendant professor to the court of common pleas for disposition of his preliminary objection on the ground that plaintiff's complaint by failing to allege that his negligent conduct was wanton, malicious, or reckless failed to state a cause of action. The court stated that defendant professor was clearly not an officer of the commonwealth for purposes of the court's jurisdiction of the complaint against him.


OUTCOME: The court transferred plaintiff student's claim of negligence against defendant professor to the court of common pleas because defendant professor was not an officer of the commonwealth for purposes of the court's jurisdiction. The court sustained defendant school's preliminary objection to plaintiff's claim because the claim did not fall within any of the categories of claims to which sovereign immunity had been waived.

Estate of Armstrong v. Pennsylvania Bd. of Probation & Parole


No. 44 T.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


46 Pa. Commw. 33; 405 A.2d 1099; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1976


March 21, 1979, Argued  
September 14, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of The Estate of Tanya Carlissa Armstrong, a/k/a Lisa Rodriguez, Deceased, a Minor, by her Parent and Natural Guardian and Personal Representative, Phyllis Rodriguez and Phyllis Rodriguez in her own right v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, William C. Boor, Chairman, and Board Members William F. Butler, Ernest R. Connelley and John Jefferson; and Irving Glazer, Parole Officer.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections of Commonwealth and Board sustained. Complaint dismissed as to those defendants. Preliminary objections of remaining defendants overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parent filed a complaint against defendants, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, the Board of Probation and Parole (board), and individual members of the board, which alleged negligence in the release of a convicted felon, and defendants filed preliminary objections asserting sovereign and absolute immunity.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff parent filed a complaint in trespass which alleged that defendants, Commonwealth, the board of probation and parole (board), and individual members of the board, were negligent in the release of a convicted felon, who, after his release, raped and murdered plaintiff's minor daughter. The court sustained the preliminary objections of defendants, Commonwealth and board, and dismissed plaintiff's complaint as to them on the ground of sovereign immunity. The doctrine applied to bar plaintiffs suit at the time the circumstances giving rise to the action occurred, and still barred the action when instituted. The subsequent passage of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5110(a), which set forth an applicable exception to the sovereign immunity doctrine, did not change this result. However, the preliminary objections of defendant individual members of the board, which asserted absolute immunity, were overruled and dismissed without prejudice to raise the defense of official immunity. The rules of absolute immunity had been judicially replaced by the doctrine of official immunity. The passage of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5110 did not affect the operation official immunity.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed plaintiff parent's complaint as to defendants, Commonwealth and the board of probation and parole (board). The doctrine of sovereign immunity still served as a defense to plaintiff's action despite the recent passage of an applicable statutory exclusion because the circumstances giving rise to plaintiff's claim, and the initiation of the action, occurred before the effective date of the exception.

Bluebell Assocs. v. Township Eng'r for Whitpain Township


Nos. 269 C.D. 1977, 334 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


45 Pa. Commw. 599; 405 A.2d 1070; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1955


April 3, 1979, Argued  
September 12, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County in cases of Bluebell Associates v. The Township Engineer for Whitpain Township, No. 76-12439; and Bluebell Associates v. Board of Supervisors of Whitpain Township and Manus McHugh, III and Deidre McHugh, his wife, No. 76-12692.



DISPOSITION: Order dismissing mandamus action affirmed. Order reversing curative amendment denial reversed. Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two appeals, consolidated for argument and consideration, were from orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), the first involving the trial court's refusal, in a mandamus action against the appellee township engineer, to compel the issuance of a grading permit for an airport extension, and the second concerning an order granting applicant approval of that same airport enlargement in a statutory zoning proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Two consolidated appeals were before the court. One involving the trial court's refusal in a mandamus action to compel the issuance of a grading permit for an airport extension, and the other concerning an order granting applicant approval of that same airport enlargement in a statutory zoning proceeding. Applicant, appellant in the first action and appellee in the second initiated an action with the township for a curative amendment, not a variance, under 53 P.S. § 11004. Appellee township supervisors denied the curative amendment, but its resolution purported to grant a variance. The court held that 53 P.S. §§ 10603, 10912 conferred the variance power exclusively upon the zoning hearing board and affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the mandamus complaint because the township supervisors lacked authority to grant the variance purported by their resolution. The court then reversed the trial court's order as to the zoning appeal that still remained and remanded with the direction it be denied holding that in a residential township, zoning provisions permitting airports could be omitted without placing upon the municipality the burden of demonstrating a justification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal by the trial court of the mandamus complaint because the curative amendment application had been denied and appellee township supervisors lacked authority to grant the variance purported by their resolution. The court remanded with the direction that the zoning appeal be denied and stated that appellant applicant could have a remedy for the expansion of its nonconforming use by way of a variance proceeding.

O'Donnell v. Casey


No. 2807 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


45 Pa. Commw. 394; 405 A.2d 1006; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1924


June 5, 1979, Argued  
September 5, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Thomas P. O'Donnell, Jr. and Eileen O'Donnell, his wife; Philip Shalanca and Ann Marie Shalanca, his wife; Kenneth Moules and Geraldine Moules, his wife; and Wilkes-Barre Area School District v. Robert E. Casey, State Treasurer, and Caryl M. Kline, Secretary of Education.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer sustained. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, school district and residents of school district, sought to enjoin respondents, state treasurer and secretary of education, from disbursing funds to any school district under the provisions of The Public School Code of 1949 (Code), 24 Pa. Stat. § 1-101 et seq., which established a formula for computation of the state subsidy. Petitioners challenged the constitutionality of the Code and respondents filed preliminary objections.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, school district and residents of school district, opposed the formula for computation of state education subsidies and sought an injunction against respondents, state treasurer and secretary of education, from disbursing funds under the provisions of The Public School Code of 1949, 24 Pa. OUTCOME: The court sustained respondents', state treasurer and secretary of education, preliminary objection in the form of a demurrer and dismissed the petition for review of the constitutionality of the state education subsidy laws for failure to state a cause of action.

 

1059 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Somma v. Commonwealth


No. 2056 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


45 Pa. Commw. 332; 405 A.2d 1323; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2311


June 5, 1979, Argued  
September 4, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in case of Appeal of: Leo and Elizabeth Somma, No. RPIT-1483.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers sought review of an order of the Pennsylvania Board of Finances and Revenue, which sustained respondent Pennsylvania Department of Revenue's assessment against petitioners but which declined to rule on a challenge to the constitutionality of 72 P.S. § 7314(a) (1971).


OVERVIEW: Under 72 P.S. § 7314 (a) (1971), Pennsylvania taxpayers receive a credit for income taxes paid to another state. Petitioner taxpayers argued that the provision violated Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1, which provided that all taxes had to be uniform. Petitioners argued that to grant taxpayers credits against Pennsylvania personal income tax for taxes paid to other states, while denying credits for taxes paid to local Pennsylvania taxing authorities, created unequal state tax burdens. The court affirmed and noted that taxpayers bore a heavy burden when contesting the constitutionality of a taxation statute and that the legislature had broad discretion in choosing acceptable classifications. The court asserted that it had no authority to rewrite the statutes as proposed by petitioners. The court concluded that when petitioners questioned the reasonableness of the scheme, they were questioning not uniformity of the taxing provisions, but rather the sense of fairness, which permitted the imposition of two separate and distinct taxes on one income. The court held that two separate taxing schemes that superimposed one upon the other did not create impermissible, unconstitutional inequalities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Pennsylvania Board of Finances and Revenue, which sustained a tax assessment against petitioner taxpayers. The court held that the tax statute that permitted Pennsylvania taxpayers a credit for taxes paid to other states but not to local jurisdictions was constitutional because it did not constitute non-uniform taxation. The court entered a judgment against petitioners for the amount of taxes owed.

Pennsylvania State Asso. of Township Supervisors v. Thornburgh


No. 417 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


45 Pa. Commw. 361; 405 A.2d 614; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1915


June 5, 1979, Argued  
August 31, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Pennsylvania State Association of Township Supervisors, Asa D. Burkholder, Leon Lankford and Vince Carpenter v. Richard L. Thornburgh, Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Robert E. Casey, Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Al Benedict, Auditor General of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Ethel D. Allen, Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer sustained. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, association of township supervisors and individual supervisors, filed a petition for review, pursuant to which petitioners asserted that the Public Officials Ethics Law, 65 P.S. § 401 et seq., violated various provisions of the Pennsylvania and United States constitutions and sought a decree declaring the Act unconstitutional, void, and unenforceable.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, association of township supervisors and individual supervisors, filed a petition for review, which asserted that the Public Officials Ethics Law (Act), 65 P.S. § 401 et seq., violated various constitutional provisions. Respondents, state officials, lodged preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer. The court sustained the objections and held that the Act did not deny petitioners due process or equal protection of the law, did not infringe on petitioners' rights to serve in public office, was not vague or overbroad, did not infringe on petitioners' rights of privacy and freedom from unreasonable searches, and did not provide for an unconstitutional exercise of the power of appointment. Furthermore, the Act did not violate Pa. Const. art. II, § 1, which vested the legislative power in the general assembly, because the rule of non-delegation of legislative power did not require that all details of administration be precisely enumerated in the statute. It was sufficient where the Act contained sufficient guidelines to limit the exercise of statutory power conferred by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court sustained respondents', state officials, objections in the nature of a demurrer and dismissed petitioners, association of township supervisors and individual supervisors', request for review as to whether the Public Officials Ethics Law (Act) violated constitution provisions. The court held that the Act did not violate any constitutional rights asserted by petitioners, and did not violate the rule of non-delegation of legislative power.

 

1061 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Snider v. Shapp


No. 55 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


45 Pa. Commw. 337; 405 A.2d 602; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1917


June 5, 1979, Argued  
August 31, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Obie Snider, Fred L. Hoffman, and Barbara V. Barker v. Milton J. Shapp, Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Robert E. Casey, Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Al Benedict, Auditor General of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Barton A. Fields, Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Centre County Board of Elections, the Bedford County Board of Elections, York County Board of Elections; and John Glatz, John T. Saylor, Grover Spearley, Alva Hostetler, Stanley Bollman, I. Stanley Claycomb and Carroll H. Leppo, Robert L. Bowers and William C. McKinley, Jr., as members of the Centre, Bedford and York County Boards of Elections.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, elected school officials, filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against respondent state officials in an action to prohibit implementation of the Public Officials Ethics Law, 65 P.S. § 401 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, elected school officials, challenged the Public Officials Ethics Law, 65 P.S. § 401 et seq. (law), which required them to disclose their financial affairs. The court dismissed the action in favor of respondent state officials, although petitioners had standing due to the law's potential effects. The court held that petitioners' privacy rights under the United States and Pennsylvania Constitutions were not violated because their interests were subject to the public's interests in public integrity. The law was not vague. There was no conflict with Pa. Const. art. IV, § 8 because there was no requirement that the Senate confirm gubernatorial appointments to the enforcing agencies. There was no violation of Pa. Const. art. I, § 28 where both genders were equally affected. There was no violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV because there was a reasonable basis for the law not to apply to appointed officials. There was no violation of Pa. Const. art. I, § 5 and art. III, § 27 because there was no effect on the ability of petitioners to serve or in the right of the public to elect them. 65 P.S. § 403(b) did not infringe upon a republican form of government.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the complaint against respondent state officials for declaratory and injunctive relief in an action to prevent the implementation of the Public Officials Ethics Law (law) because, even though petitioners, elected school officials, had standing to challenge the law, the law was not unconstitutional under the United States and Pennsylvania Constitutions.

Biles v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 58 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


44 Pa. Commw. 274; 403 A.2d 1341; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1799


March 7, 1979, Argued  
July 17, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Vincent Biles, Dorothy Birch, Harold Jackson, Gloria Morales, Valerie White, individually and all other persons similarly situated v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Public Welfare.



DISPOSITION: Motion for summary judgment denied. Motion for judgment on the pleadings granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, full-time university students considered ineligible for public assistance because of provision in Supplemental General Appropriations Act of 1977, 1977 Pa. Laws 512, moved for summary judgment in suit against respondent public welfare department, contending the provision violated Pennsylvania and U.S. Constitutions, and respondent moved for judgment on the pleadings.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, a class of people consisting of all full-time university students who were considered ineligible for public assistance as a result of a provision in the Supplemental General Appropriations Act of 1977 (Act 14A), 1977 Pa. Laws 512, sued respondent state department of public welfare, asserting that Act 14A violated the Pennsylvania and U.S. Constitutions. Petitioners moved for summary judgment and respondent moved for judgment on the pleadings. The court granted respondent's motion. The provision at issue did not violate Pa. Const. art. III, § 11, which required that a general appropriations bill embrace nothing but appropriations for the commonwealth's executive, legislative and judicial departments, and for the public debt and for public schools. The provision was germane to the appropriations, it did not conflict with existing law, and it did not extend beyond the life of the appropriations bill itself. Act 14A did not violate equal protection by distinguishing between general assistance recipients in different categories because the classification had some reasonable basis. The classification was not unconstitutional simply because it resulted in some inequality.


OUTCOME: Court granted respondent's motion for judgment on pleadings. Provision was not an unconstitutional rider to general appropriations bill because it was germane to the appropriations and did not extend beyond life of appropriations bill, and it did not violate equal protection because classification of assistance recipients had some reasonable basis.

 

1063 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Ashbourne School v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Education


No. 1004 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


43 Pa. Commw. 593; 403 A.2d 161; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1708


March 7, 1979, Argued  
June 28, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Secretary of Education in case of In the Matter of Ashbourne School et al. v. Department of Education, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, dated April 11, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, private schools previously approved by respondent Department of Education for the special education of state tuition reimbursable exceptional children, appealed the Secretary of Education order that granted reimbursement to the schools on a pro rata basis pursuant to the retroactive application of audit regulations, instead of from special education appropriations.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner private schools were approved for special education tuition reimbursement. They alleged that the Secretary of Education erred in allowing respondent Department of Education to pay monies owning to petitioners to be paid on a pro rata basis. Specifically, petitioners claimed they had been denied due process of law in that the criteria set forth in 22 Pa. Code § 171.19(e)(2) were too indefinite to provide a guide as to what charges were reimbursable. The court found that the criteria provided sufficient guidance for conducting audits and taking subsequent administrative actions regarding reasonable costs. Petitioners then argued that respondent was precluded from applying the reimbursement regulations retroactively. The court disagreed, reasoning that reimbursement for tuition rates was deemed conditional, not vested, so that new tuition rates could not have been fixed by any pre-school year contractual agreement. Finally, since the General Assembly allocated specific funds from which payments were to be made to the approved private schools, the Department of Education was powerless to use funds appropriated for other purposes to satisfy its debts to Petitioners.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Secretary of Education's adjudication, concluding that the statutory language provided a general description of a certain type of fund to be used rather than a command that special education appropriations were to be used for reimbursement, and that having previously concluded that a pro rata disbursement was an acceptable method, respondent Department of Education properly applied the audit regulations retroactively.

 

1064 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Simon v. Vitto


No. 1726 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


43 Pa. Commw. 402; 403 A.2d 1335; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1698


May 7, 1979, Argued  
June 19, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County in case of Paul Del Vitto v. Ted Simon, John W. Regoli and William R. Davis, County Commissioners for Westmoreland County, Pennsylvania, No. 2221 of 1975.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff deputy sheriff brought suit in the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania), to recover for days worked in 1975 and 1976 but not paid, while plaintiff was in forced retirement due to the county's retirement plan, 16 P.S. § 11651. The jury returned a verdict for plaintiff, and defendant county commissioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff deputy sheriff was hired in 1960. In 1972, the county set up a retirement system under 16 P.S. § 11651, et seq., pursuant to which plaintiff was forced into retirement in 1973. In 1975, an amending resolution allowed retired deputies to work a yearly maximum of 30 days, payable on a per diem basis. Plaintiff returned to work on a daily basis; however, he was only paid for 30 days' work in 1975 and 1976. In 1976, the county rescinded the 1972 plan, and plaintiff was rehired. Plaintiff filed suit to recover for days worked but not paid in 1975 and 1976, and the jury returned a verdict in his favor. Defendant commissioners appealed. The court reversed the jury's verdict, holding that a county sheriff does not possess independent authority to establish an employment relationship for which defendants were bound to pay. Further, 16 P.S. § 1205 did not allow the sheriff to appoint such deputies as he believed necessary, without going before the county salary board for its approval. Defendants had no duty to approve payment of compensation for someone occupying a position not authorized by the salary board.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for plaintiff deputy sheriff, holding that plaintiff was not authorized to work by the county salary board. The sheriff had no inherent, independent power to establish an employment relationship for which the county was required to pay. 16 P.S. § 1205 did not allow the sheriff to appoint deputies he believed necessary, without the approval of the county salary board.

Wirsing v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


43 Pa. Commw. 305; 402 A.2d 310; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1628

OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant requested and was granted a leave of absence to care for her grandchildren during her daughter's illness. Several days before she was to return to work, she requested and received an extension of her leave. Her employer advised her at that time that she would be granted no further extensions. Claimant failed to report to work on her scheduled return date, and was informed several days later that she was considered to have terminated her employment. An unemployment referee denied benefits under 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 802(b)(1), reasoning that petitioner voluntarily ceased work without necessitous and compelling reasons. The Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (board) affirmed the referee but modified the decision, holding petitioner ineligible under 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 402(b)(2)(II), the domestic quit section. The court reversed, remanding the matter to the board for a redetermination of eligibility. The statute upon which the board decision relied had been held unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order holding petitioner claimant ineligible for unemployment benefits and remanded the case for a redetermination of eligibility, holding that respondent agency erred in finding petitioner ineligible for benefits under the domestic quit section, which had been held unconstitutional.

Pennsylvania Power & Light Co. v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


No. 2466 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


43 Pa. Commw. 252; 401 A.2d 1255; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1640


February 7, 1979, Argued  
June 6, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission in case of Mapping of Retail Electric Service Territories, Special Order Docket No. 76-4.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner utility challenged the order of respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission, which required the filing of maps pursuant to the Retail Electric Supplier Unincorporated Area Certified Territory Act, 15 P.S. § 3280(c). Petitioner argued that respondent should have ordered that the maps show only those lines where a public utility adjoined an electric cooperative, or where two electric cooperatives adjoined.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission, pursuant to its authority in 15 P.S. §§ 3280(c), 3284, entered an order nisi requiring petitioner utility to file maps showing the location of distribution lines located entirely within the service territory of a single retail electric supplier. In addition, respondent ordered that the maps filed show only distribution lines located on the peripheries of service territories, where electric utilities adjoined other electric utilities, where electric utilities adjoined electric cooperative corporations, and where electric cooperative corporations adjoined other electric cooperatives. An administrative law judge affirmed the order nisi. Petitioner objected to the requirement that the maps show distribution lines where two public electric utilities adjoined. The court affirmed the lower tribunal's order. The court found that petitioner was attempting to have the court render an advisory opinion on the meaning and constitutionality of the statutory provisions. The court would not do so. The court stated that both parties ignored the clear mandate that all distribution lines be shown, regardless of their location.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission's order. The court found that petitioner utility was attempting to have an advisory opinion rendered on provisions of the Retail Electric Supplier Unincorporated Area Certified Territory Act. The court did affirm the mandate that all distribution lines were to be shown, not simply certain types of connections in certain locations.

Pennsylvania Gas & Water Co. v. Old Lycoming


No. 258 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


43 Pa. Commw. 188; 402 A.2d 1096; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1604


March 5, 1979, Argued  
June 1, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County in case of Pennsylvania Gas & Water Company v. Township of Old Lycoming, No. 76-2915.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility company challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant relief in its action in equity challenging the reasonableness of the permit issuance and inspection fees charged by appellee township, and set by appellee Department of Transportation (Pennsylvania), for installation and maintenance of gas pipes located under township's roads.


OVERVIEW: On review of an order denying appellant utility company relief, appellant utility company contended that appellee township's fees for the installation and maintenance of gas pipes located under township's roads were invalid because they were not based on the township's actual cost of processing the application and inspecting the work but rather on the cost of similar services provided by appellee Department of Transportation. The court disagreed and affirmed the order. First, the township had no discretion to fix the permit fees because pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 66156 the prescribed fees were determined by the department. Second, § 66156 did not prohibit the department from using its own cost studies and fee schedule in determining the fees to be charged by the township and, there were substantial similarities between the department and township procedures and salary schedules. And finally, the trial court did not err in determining that the fees were not excessive because even though the evidence was conflicting, there was testimony that warranted the trial court's findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying appellant utility company relief. The permit issuance and inspection fees charged by appellee township for installation and maintenance of gas pipes were properly determined by appellee Department of Transportation, the department properly relied on its own fee schedule in setting the fees, and the record supported the trial court's finding that the fees were not excessive.

Bresch v. Commonwealth, Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board

May 18, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County in case of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board v. Edward A. Bresch, Jr., and Patricia R. Bresch, License Docket No. 1, Page 115, Citation No. 1779, 1977.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner licensees appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the action of respondent state liquor control board that revoked petitioners' liquor license pursuant to § 471 of the Liquor Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 47, § 4-471.


OVERVIEW: Respondent state liquor control board revoked petitioner licensees' liquor license pursuant to § 471 of the Liquor Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 47, § 4-471, on the ground that petitioners sold alcoholic beverages between 2 a.m. and 7 a.m. The lower court sustained respondent's revocation. On further appeal, petitioners contended that § 471 was unconstitutionally vague and indefinite. The court rejected petitioners' contention and affirmed the lower court's order. The court held that any reasonable licensee would clearly have had sufficient notice that citations could have issued for violations of any of the liquor laws by any of the licensee's agents or employees. The court found that petitioners' argument that the statute was unclear was patently frivolous.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed an order that sustained respondent state liquor control board's revocation of petitioner licensees' liquor license. The court held that a challenged section of the Liquor Code was not unconstitutionally vague and indefinite.

Bievenour v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review


No. 1378 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


42 Pa. Commw. 616; 401 A.2d 594; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1563


December 8, 1978, Argued  
May 17, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of Lewis J. Bievenour, No. B-145757.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant appealed an order of respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which disallowed his appeal from a referee's denial of unemployment compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant worked as a carpenter in the hardware store owned by his son. He applied for unemployment compensation benefits, which were denied by a referee following a hearing. Respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review affirmed the referee's denial of benefits. Petitioner appealed, contending that 43 P.S. § 753(1)(4)(5) (Act), unconstitutionally discriminated against him on the basis of age and violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed respondent's denial of benefits. The court concluded that the Act, which excluded service by a parent that was performed for a son or daughter, was constitutional. The classification excluding parents of employers from unemployment compensation coverage was rationally related to a legitimate state interest. The right to receive unemployment compensation benefits in Pennsylvania was a statutory right, not a fundamental one. A classification based on age did not constitute a suspect classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review's denial of unemployment benefits to claimant. The Unemployment Compensation Law (Act) was constitutional. The Act's classification excluding parents of employers from coverage was rationally related to a legitimate state interest. Entitlement to unemployment benefits was not a fundamental right, and classification by age did not constitute a suspect classification.

In re Revocation of Restaurant Liquor License No. R-9606


No. 2406 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


42 Pa. Commw. 582; 401 A.2d 421; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1571


April 2, 1979, Argued  
May 15, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lehigh County in case of In Re: Revocation of Restaurant Liquor License No. R-9606 and Amusement Permit No. AP-23526 Issued to A-J-C, Inc., Andy's Tavern, 247 North 10th Street, Allentown, Pennsylvania, 18102, No. 68-M/1975.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lehigh County (Pennsylvania), which upheld an order of the liquor control board that revoked appellant's liquor license on the grounds that appellant's establishment was conducted in a noisy and disorderly manner, and that appellant's sole officer and shareholder pleaded nolo contendere to a charge of aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: The liquor control board revoked appellant corporation's restaurant liquor license on grounds that appellant's establishment was conducted in a noisy and disorderly manner under 47 P.S. § 4-471, after police were called to a domestic disturbance between appellant's sole officer and shareholder and his wife, which escalated to a fight with police officers. The revocation was also based on a second ground that appellant's sole officer and shareholder had on another occasion entered a plea of nolo contendere to a charge of aggravated assault. Appellant challenged the decision and the trial court affirmed. Appellant challenged the trial court's ruling and contended that an isolated instance of noisy and disorderly conduct was an insufficient ground upon which to base a revocation, and the that the trial court erred in admitting evidence of the prior nolo contendere plea. The court affirmed and held that the conduct in question involved not only a domestic quarrel but a fight with police officers. The court held that both grounds were proper because the agency was carrying out its duty to protect the citizens by regulating the conduct of its licensees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the trial court which upheld an order of the liquor control board that revoked appellant corporation's liquor license because operation of appellant's establishment in a noisy and disorderly conduct constituted a sufficient basis for revocation under the statute and trial court did not err in admitting evidence of appellant's sole officer and shareholder's plea of nolo contendere to aggravated assault.
