Bala v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Bd. of Review


No. 279 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


42 Pa. Commw. 487; 400 A.2d 1359; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1554


June 5, 1978, Argued  
May 8, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued December 5, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of Irwin Bale, No. B-139385.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of an order of respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which denied him unemployment compensation benefits on the basis that he was discharged from employment for willful misconduct. Petitioner argued that the activity resulting in his discharge was protected speech under the U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee worked as a hotel night watchman for 10 months prior to being discharged for willful misconduct. The hotel discharged petitioner on the basis that he wrote a note, on hotel stationary, to a hotel guest in order to voice his displeasure with the guest and a certain political campaign. Subsequently, petitioner was denied unemployment compensation benefits by respondent unemployment compensation board of review. Petitioner argued that his note to the hotel guest was protected speech under the U.S. Const. amend. I, therefore, the denial of unemployment benefits was an impermissible infringement of his rights. The court held that petitioner's note to a hotel guest voicing displeasure with the guest did not involve a matter of public concern or political expression, thus it was not a violation of petitioner's freedom of speech to deny unemployment compensation benefits where the hotel proved that petitioner's note constituted willful misconduct in that he ignored warnings that he was to cease interaction with hotel guests. As such, the court affirmed the order denying petitioner benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying petitioner employee unemployment compensation benefits, holding that it was not a violation of petitioner's freedom of speech to deny unemployment benefits where his employer proved that petitioner's note to a guest, which did not involve a matter of public concern or political expression, constituted willful misconduct in that he ignored warnings to cease interaction with hotel guests.

Appeal of Redo


Nos. 2469 C.D. 1977, 15 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


42 Pa. Commw. 468; 401 A.2d 394; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1556


September 29, 1978, Argued  
May 8, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County in case of In Re: Appeal of Phillip D. Redo from Suspension from Duty as a Police Officer and from Order of Termination as a Police Officer by the Supervisors of West Goshen Township, Misc. No. 40, 1977.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, township and police officer, sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Chester County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the adjudication of the Board of Supervisors that appellant police officer engaged in conduct unbecoming an officer, but which modified the Board's dismissal order to a one-year suspension.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officer engaged in an altercation with a hotel owner, whom he suspected of causing or exacerbating his marital problems. Subsequently, the board of supervisors dismissed appellant police officer. The lower court affirmed the board but modified the board's dismissal of appellant police officer to a one-year suspension. Appellants, township and police officer, sought review. The court held that the procedures employed by appellant township in affording appellant police officer a hearing on his dismissal did not deny him due process by improperly commingling prosecutorial and adjudicatory functions because although the board prepared the charges for disposition, the charges were actually filed by the police chief; furthermore, the board was advised by independent counsel during the hearing and decision. Finally, the court found that the lower court did not abuse its discretion in modifying the board's dismissal to a one-year suspension where it considered appellant police officer's past record, the effects of his conduct on the morale of the police force, and the citizenry's respect for the force. As such, the court affirmed the order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order modifying the board's dismissal of appellant police officer for conduct unbecoming an officer to a one-year suspension, holding that the procedures employed by appellant township in determining that appellant police officer engaged in conduct unbecoming an officer did improperly commingle prosecutorial and adjudicatory functions where the charges were actually filed by the police chief.

Biberman v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review


No. 64 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


42 Pa. Commw. 451; 401 A.2d 9; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1549


February 8, 1979, Argued  
May 7, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of Morris Biberman, No. B-151989.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee challenged the denial by respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), of benefits under 43 P.S. § 802(b)(2)(II), which denial was based upon the finding that petitioner voluntarily terminated his employment because of domestic obligations and circumstances. Petitioner contended that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee challenged the denial of unemployment compensation benefits under 43 P.S. § 802(b)(2). The denial was based upon the finding of respondent Unemployment Compensation Board that he voluntarily terminated his employment because of domestic obligations and circumstances. When petitioner applied for the benefits, he was found ineligible under 43 P.S. § 802(b)(1), because he had voluntarily quit his employment without cause of a necessitous and compelling nature. Respondent affirmed his ineligibility, but on the basis that he had voluntarily terminated his employment for a domestic reason and was, therefore, ineligible under 43 P.S. § 802(b)(2)(II). Section 802(b)(2)(II) had been held unconstitutional by the court. The statute improperly denied domestic claimants the opportunity to demonstrate that their termination was for a necessitous and compelling cause. Therefore, the court reversed the decision of respondent, which denied benefits to petitioner under § 802(b)(2), and remanded the case for a redetermination of eligibility under § 802(b)(1)-(2).


OUTCOME: The order of respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review was reversed and the case was remanded to respondent for a redetermination of petitioner employee's eligibility for unemployment compensation benefits under the applicable section of the Unemployment Compensation Law. The statute under which petitioner was deemed ineligible was unconstitutional, as it denied the opportunity to demonstrate cause.

1076 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Ruano v. Barbieri


No. 1229 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


42 Pa. Commw. 67; 400 A.2d 235; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1461


November 1, 1978, Argued  
April 18, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of William J. Ruano v. Alexander F. Barbieri, Judge, Court Administrator of Pennsylvania, and Gerald W. Spivack, Esquire, Deputy Court Administrator.



DISPOSITION: Petitioner's request for injunctive relief denied. Statutes declared to be constitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner retired district justice filed a petition for review in the nature of a complaint in equity and for declaratory judgment. Petitioner sought determination of the vitality and constitutionality of Section 205 of the Magisterial District Reform Act, 42 P.S. § 2205, to compel respondent court administrators to register him as a "qualified retired district justice" under the provisions of § 205.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner retired district justice sought to compel respondent court administrators to register him as a qualified retired district justice under § 205 of the Magisterial District Reform Act, 42 P.S. § 2205. Respondents contended that § 205 was repealed and replaced by the Judicial Code, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4122, which respondents challenged as unconstitutional under Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(c). The court held that the legislature intended to repeal absolutely all of the provisions of 42 P.S. § 2205, except for the compensation clause thereof, which remained in effect until a separate repealer date. The court also held that the applicable provisions governing assignment of senior district justices were those found in the Judicial Code, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4122(b). Because no registration procedure was established therein, petitioner's request for injunctive relief was denied. Next, the court held that Pa. Const. art. V, § 16, being silent regarding senior district justices, did not constitute a positive prohibition upon the power of the legislature to enact laws providing for their assignment. Thus, the legislature had the power to enact the provision.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Magisterial District Reform Act, under which petitioner retired district justice sought to be registered as a qualified retired district justice, had been repealed and replaced by the Judicial Code, which did not provide for registration. The court denied petitioner's request for injunctive relief and decreed that the applicable provisions of the Code did not violate the Pennsylvania Constitution.

1078 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Bardo v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 1784 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


40 Pa. Commw. 585; 397 A.2d 1305; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1304


March 3, 1978, Argued  
February 27, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued December 5, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Department of Public Welfare in case of Appeal of Edna Bardo, dated September 17, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner homeowner challenged a decision of respondent Department of Public Welfare (Pennsylvania), which denied her emergency assistance when her mobile home was destroyed by a windstorm. Respondent claimed that the action was barred by the doctrine of res judicata.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner homeowner applied for emergency assistance after she lost her mobile home in a wind storm. Respondent Department of Public Welfare denied petitioner's request for emergency assistance because there had been no civil disorder emergency order issued. The court reversed respondent's order, holding that the regulations under which petitioner was denied assistance had been previously declared unconstitutional and that the Social Security Act required emergency assistance to eligible recipients. The court also found that petitioner's action was not barred by the doctrine of res judicata because the prior forum did not have the authority to order the state treasury to make payment. The prior action, of which petitioner was a class member, was filed in federal court and the remedy available was limited to injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying petitioner homeowner emergency assistance, holding that the regulations under which petitioner was denied assistance were unconstitutional, emergency assistance to eligible recipients was required, and the doctrine of res judicata did not apply.

 

1079 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


East Suburban Press, Inc. v. Penn Hills


No. 1646 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


40 Pa. Commw. 438; 397 A.2d 1263; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1279; 4 Media L. Rep. 2333


October 30, 1978, Argued  
February 14, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in case of East Suburban Press, Inc., a corporation v. Township of Penn Hills, No. 2088 January Term, 1975.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant publisher challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), in a declaratory judgment proceeding against appellee township regarding the specifications of the Newspaper Advertising Act (Act), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 101 et seq. The trial court denied appellant relief after appellee refused to permit appellant to bid for legal advertising.


OVERVIEW: Appellant publisher printed a newspaper that was primarily distributed free of charge and lacked second class mailing privileges. Appellee township refused to permit appellant to bid for appellee's legal advertising. Appellant brought a declaratory judgment proceeding regarding the specifications of the Newspaper Advertising Act (Act), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 101 et seq., involving the requirements that a newspaper must meet in order to carry legal advertising. The trial court determined appellant did not comply with either the price or mailing privilege requirements of the Act. After considering the constitutionality of both those requirements, the trial court held that they were valid and refused to grant appellant relief. Appellant claimed compliance with the price requirement but, on appeal, pursued a constitutional attack upon the second class mail requirement. The court affirmed the judgment because appellant failed to comply with the statutory price and mailing requirements, and the legislature did not improperly delegate the formulation of rules on the subject of legal advertising to any external agency regarding the Act.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellant publisher relief against appellee township in a declaratory judgment proceeding was affirmed. Appellant was not treated as a newspaper distributed at a fixed price; thus appellant failed to meet statutory requirements, and the statute was valid because the legislature did not abdicate its control of legal advertising sphere.

 

1080 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Keystone Trucking Corp. v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board


No. 1605 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


40 Pa. Commw. 326; 397 A.2d 1256; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1255


December 8, 1978, Argued  
February 6, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board in case of Edward Wilson v. Keystone Trucking Corporation, Docket Misc. 3785.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, employer and insurer, appealed the decision from respondent, Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania), which denied petitioners' motion not to be proceed with a hearing. Respondent, Department of Labor and Industry, had ordered the hearing to determine if petitioner insurer had failed to timely make payments to respondent employee.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Department of Labor and Industry (department) ordered a hearing to determine if petitioners, employer and insurer, had failed to make timely payments to respondent employee and whether they should be penalized pursuant to 77 P.S. § 991 of the Workmen's Compensation Act. Petitioners challenged the order, which was denied by respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (board). The appellate court affirmed. The court rejected the argument that since 77 P.S. § 991 required respondent board to establish certain rules for departmental hearings, and because it had not established such rules, the hearing could not be held. Respondent department had the authority to impose penalties under § 991. Ceilings of 10 and 20% percent for penalties were a sufficient standard to meet petitioners' due process rights. The statute did not violate Pa. Const. art. III, § 18's requirement that workmen's compensation be reasonable. The fact that employers and insurers could be penalized as much as 20 percent whereas claimants could only lose interest for causing delay was not a denial of equal protection. The former were in a superior position whereas workers would gain nothing by delay.


OUTCOME: The order from respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (board) which denied petitioners', employer and insurer's, petition not to proceed with a hearing ordered by respondent Department of Labor and Industry to determine if petitioner insurer failed to timely pay respondent employee was affirmed. Respondent board had the authority to hold such a hearing. The penalty provisions of the statute were not unconstitutional.

 

1081 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Hargreaves v. Mid-Valley School Dist.


No. 2361 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


40 Pa. Commw. 110; 396 A.2d 894; 1979 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1218


September 29, 1978, Argued  
January 24, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County in case of Robert B. Hargreaves v. Mid-Valley School District, No. 435 September Term, 1977.



DISPOSITION: Decision granting motion of plaintiff affirmed. Decision granting motion of additional defendant reversed. Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania), which ordered appellant to pay to appellee elected tax collector commissions on certain returns for delinquent taxes which were subsequently collected by appellee county because the returns in question were made under 72 P.S. § 5971 et seq. (1931).


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered appellant school district to pay to appellee elected tax official commissions on returns for delinquent taxes which were subsequently collected by appellee county. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee elected tax official but reversed regarding appellee county. The court held that appellee elected tax official was entitled to the commissions because the returns in question were made under 72 P.S. § 5971a et seq. (1931) and appellee elected tax official had an unambiguously vested right in the commissions. However, the court held that appellee county was liable for their payment and appellant was not. The court determined that the statutory provisions in effect when the collections were made had to have been used because the action payment of the commissions were part of and dependent upon the collection process as governed by the Real Estate Tax Sale Law, 72 P.S. § 5860.101 et seq. (1947). The Real Estate Tax Sale Law had a catch-all section which established non-reimbursable and non-recoverable county liability and therefore the commissions should have been paid out as other expenses of appellee county.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order in favor of appellee county and affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee elected tax collector in the action on commissions on certain returns for delinquent taxes. The court held that appellee elected tax collector was entitled to the commissions but that appellee county was liable instead of appellant school district.

 

1082 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Lehigh Foundations, Inc. v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board


No. 1611 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


39 Pa. Commw. 416; 395 A.2d 576; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1550


September 15, 1978, Argued  
December 27, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board in case of Mildred B. Kelly and Bret Arthur Fegan, a minor, by Diane R. Fegan, parent and natural guardian; Rudy Arthur Kelly, deceased v. Lehigh Foundations, No. A-72575.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, employer and insurer, appealed a decision of respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a referee's award of compensation to respondent claimant, an illegitimate child who was the sole surviving dependent of the decedent, under the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act, 77 P.S. § 562.


OVERVIEW: Respondent claimant, an illegitimate child who was the sole surviving dependant of the decedent who died as a result of work-related injuries, was awarded compensation by a referee, and the award was affirmed by respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (board). Petitioners, employer and insurer, appealed respondent board's decision, and the court affirmed. The court held that respondent claimant was entitled to compensation under the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act (act), 77 P.S. § 562. The court construed the statute in accordance with the demands of the equal protection clauses in U.S. Const. amend. XIV and the prohibition of special laws in Pa. Const. art. III, § 32, and held that the grant of compensation under 77 P.S. § 562 to or on account of any child embraced illegitimate children within the meaning of the statute. The court found that the recognized purpose of the act was to compensate children of deceased employees as a result of the children's filial status, and that an inferior classification of illegitimate children under § 562 would have borne no significant relationship that statutory purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board's decision that awarded compensation to respondent claimant. The court held that the compensation statute was intended to apply to illegitimate children, and that an inferior classification of illegitimate children would not have borne any significant relationship to the statutory purpose of compensating children of deceased employees as a result of the children's filial status.

 

1083 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


K. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


Nos. 2120 and 2121 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


39 Pa. Commw. 343; 395 A.2d 653; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1532


December 9, 1977, Argued  
December 20, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued September 13, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Order of the Department of Public Welfare in cases of Appeal of Ms. Rebecca K. and Appeal of Mr. Edward L., dated October 4, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two members of a drug rehabilitation program, challenged an order of appellee, the Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare, which denied them food stamp benefits. Appellee's basis for denial of benefits was that county contributions for appellants' treatment exceeded the maximum allowable income for a single person household of $ 245 per month.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, two members of a drug rehabilitation program, were turned down when they applied to appellee, the Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare, for food stamps. To fund the drug program, various counties contributed a per capita sum, called vendor payments, which appellee assessed as income. For the purposes of food stamp eligibility, appellee concluded that appellants' income exceeded the eligibility requirements of the Food Stamp Act of 1964, 7 U.S.C.S. § 2011 et seq. Although the federal vendor payment provision had been held void, the court found that the commonwealth's vendor-payment regulation was not invalid. Nor did the payments fall within the exemption for medical benefits, absent an accounting that could show what amount of the per capita payment was used for medical purposes. Finally, although the vendor payments were considered income and block grant funds were not, this discrepancy did not violate the equal protection clause when there was a reasonable basis for it. The court affirmed the order to deny benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of appellee, the Department of Public Welfare, and denied benefits to appellants, two members of a drug rehabilitation program. Payments made by the counties for appellants' treatment were vendor payments, properly included in calculation of income to determine appellants' eligibility for food stamps. The payments did not fall within the income exemption for medical care.

Eboch v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review


No. 888 C.D.1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


39 Pa. Commw. 268; 395 A.2d 321; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1511


September 15, 1978, Argued  
December 15, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of Jane M. Eboch, No. B-141133.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant appealed an order of Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, which found claimant ineligible for the special unemployment assistance program under the Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 P.S. § 802(b)(2)(I), which barred compensation for unemployment due to leaving work to accompany or to join a spouse in a new locality.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant terminated her employment with her employer and moved with her husband to another state where her husband had enrolled at a university. Petitioner claimant filed an application for benefits under the special unemployment assistance program (SUA) instituted by the Emergency Jobs and Unemployment Assistance Act, 26 U.S.C.S. § 3304. The Bureau of Employment Security and, upon appeal, a referee and respondent Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Board of Review found petitioner ineligible for SUA benefits because she was disqualified under the Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 P.S. § 802(b)(2)(I). The referee had held that claimant did not meet her burden of proof on the issue of whether or not, during the six-month period prior to her leaving or filing an application for benefits, she was the sole or major support of her family. The court affirmed the board's denial of petitioner's application for compensation. The court held that because petitioner failed to sustain her burden of proof with respect to the exception to § 802 ineligibility provision, petitioner was disqualified in terms of state law and, therefore, was ineligible for SUA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and respondent Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Board of Review's decision that sustained the denial of petitioner claimant's application under the special unemployment assistance program (SUA). The court held that because petitioner failed to sustain her burden of proof with respect to exception to the ineligibility provision of the statute, she was disqualified under state law and, therefore, was ineligible for SUA.

Appeal of Cedarbrook Realty, Inc.


Nos. 2115 and 2116 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


39 Pa. Commw. 150; 395 A.2d 613; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1489


September 28, 1978, Argued  
December 11, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County in cases of Cedarbrook Realty, Inc. and Cedarbrook Joint Venture v. The Board of Assessment Appeals for Montgomery County, the School District of Cheltenham Township, The Township of Cheltenham, County of Montgomery and The Montgomery County Institution District, No. 76-16915; and Appeal of Cedarbrook Realty, Inc. from the Real Estate Assessments for the Tax Years 1970-1976, No. 76-16916.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the preliminary objections of appellees, board and taxing districts, pursuant to the Third Class County Assessment Law, 72 P.S. § 5342 et seq., and dismissed appellants' challenges to the tax assessments of their properties.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers challenged the tax assessments of their properties for the years 1970 through 1976. The lower court sustained the preliminary objections of appellees, board and taxing districts, and dismissed the actions seeking a refund and damages. The lower court held that it was without jurisdiction to entertain the action in equity because appellants failed to pursue the mandatory and exclusive statutory remedy. Appellants sought review. The court affirmed because appellants failed to file a timely challenge of the market value determination and assessment ratio with appellee board in accordance with the mandatory time limits of the Third Class County Assessment Law, 72 P.S. § 5342 et seq. The court held that even if an employee of appellee board made material representations about the county's assessment ratio, appellee did not induce appellants to forego the available statutorily prescribed remedy. The court found that appellants failed to allege the elements of fraud that would entitle them to equitable intervention.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order sustaining the preliminary objections of appellees, board and taxing districts to appellant taxpayers' action challenging tax assessments of their property because the lower court correctly found that it was without jurisdiction in equity to entertain the suit where appellants had failed to make a timely appeal to appellee board before filing suit.

 

1086 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Perma-Lite of Pennsylvania, Inc. v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board


No. 2169 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


38 Pa. Commw. 481; 393 A.2d 1082; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1427


September 29, 1978, Argued  
November 15, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board in case of Lawrence L. Schott v. Perma-Lite of Pennsylvania, Inc., No. A-72240.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged an order of appellee Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a referee's decision to award benefits to appellee subcontractor. Appellant argued that under § 203 of the Workmen's Compensation Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 77, § 52, it was not appellee subcontractor's employer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employer, a home remodeling business, hired a contractor to perform a job on a residence. Without appellant's knowledge, the contractor hired appellee subcontractor to do the work. Appellee subcontractor fell from a ladder and was injured. Appellee subcontractor's claim for worker's compensation benefits was granted by the referee and affirmed by appellee Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board. The court reversed. Section 203 of the Workmen's Compensation Act (Act), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 77, § 52, imposed employer liability for subcontractors only when the putative employer had actual control over the premises where the injury occurred. The court observed that the evidence in the record showed that appellant had no actual control over the premises where appellee subcontractor was working. Therefore, the court held that the language of the Act and its interpretation by the Pennsylvania Supreme Court required that the award of benefits be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of appellee Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board. The court held that the Workmen's Compensation Act imposed employer liability for appellee subcontractor only when the putative employer had actual control over the premises where the injury occurred. In this case, appellant employer had no control over the home on which remodeling work was performed.

 

1087 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Simco Sales Service, Inc. v. Lower Merion Board of Comm'rs


No. 52 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


38 Pa. Commw. 434; 394 A.2d 642; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1413


September 29, 1978, Argued  
November 8, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County in case of Simco Sales Service of Pennsylvania, Inc., t/a Jack & Jill Ice Cream Company v. Township of Lower Merion Board of Commissioners, Township of Lower Merion Department of Police and Township of Lower Merion Department of Health, No. 76-08466.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an ice cream truck business, challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which vacated appellant's preliminary injunction against enforcement of an ordinance of appellees, the Lower Merion Township, its Police Department, and its Department of Health. Lower Merion Township, Pa., Ordinance 1769 prohibited the sale of merchandise, including food, from motor vehicles.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an ice cream truck business, were prohibited from operating when appellees, Lower Merion Township, its Department of Police, and its Department of Health, enacted Lower Merion Township, Pa., Ordinance 1769, which banned the selling of food from motor vehicles parked in such a way as to induce purchasers to approach the seller. The ordinance was purportedly enacted to protect young children. The court, observing that local ordinances enjoyed the same presumption of constitutionality as statutes, noted that the First Class Township Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, §§ 56510, 56544, and 56552, gave appellees the authority to promulgate regulations under their exercise of the police power. However, the court also noted that police power was not absolute. In this case, appellees' regulation had put appellant out of business. Evidence in the record about appellant's required safety training for its drivers showed that appellant had dealt effectively with potential hazards raised by the business. The court reversed and permanently enjoined appellees from enforcing the ordinance, which was unreasonable and overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and permanently enjoined appellees, Lower Merion Township, its Department of Police, and its Department of Health, from enforcing the ordinance. The court held that although appellees had the power to enact regulations to promote health and safety under the police power, the ordinance was overbroad and unreasonable.

 

1088 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Wallace v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review


No. 1643 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


38 Pa. Commw. 342; 393 A.2d 43; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1393


October 7, 1977, Argued  
October 31, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued April 4, 1978. Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of Alice Wallace, No. B-134227.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of a decision by the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a referee's denial of benefits following petitioner's voluntary termination of her employment under 43 P.S. 802(b).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant was a nurse who quit work because she could not provide care for her two sons. Her petition for unemployment compensation was denied by the referee, pursuant to 43 P.S. § 802. The denial was affirmed by respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review. On further review, petitioner contended that by preventing persons who quit their jobs for domestic reasons from showing that their resignations were motivated by necessitous and compelling causes, in comparison to persons who quit their jobs for any other reason, the statute established a classification which bore no rational relationship to a legitimate state interest, and therefore, violated the guarantee of equal protection. The court reversed the decision of respondent, and remanded the case for a redetermination of eligibility for benefits. The court held that the absolute disqualification of all unemployment compensation claimants who voluntarily terminated their employment for martial, filial, or domestic reasons had no rational relationship to a legitimate legislative purpose, and violated the equal protection clause of the U.S. Constitution.


OUTCOME: The order of the Unemployment Compensation Board that disqualified appellant from unemployment benefits because she voluntarily resigned her employment because of domestic reasons was reversed. The absolute disqualification of employment benefits for domestic reasons was a violation of the equal protection clause of the U.S. Constitution.

 

1089 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Gaito v. Pennsylvania Board of Probation & Parole


No. 21 Misc. Dkt. No. 2


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


38 Pa. Commw. 199; 392 A.2d 343; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1354


July 7, 1978, Submitted on Briefs  
October 19, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Joseph Gaito, Jr. v. Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, et al.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parolee challenged a decision of respondent Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole (Board) and others, which had ordered his arrest and recommitment as a parole violator. Petitioner challenged his arrest and the crediting of detention and parole time to his sentences, and raised issues about the revocation hearing and his incarceration status. Respondent board filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was paroled from a previous sentence. Shortly thereafter he was questioned about two shooting deaths. When respondent parole board and others could not locate petitioner, he was arrested on a warrant and charged with a violation of the Uniform Firearms Act. He was thereafter confined in a restricted area of a state correctional institution. No credit was granted for street time while on parole, and detention time following arrest was applied to the previous sentence. In an original action, petitioner challenged his arrest, application of detention time, the revocation hearing process, and the conditions of his incarceration. Respondent filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer. The court sustained the preliminary objections and dismissed the petition for review because it had no jurisdiction over the arrest issues inasmuch as they had previously been decided on a motion to suppress. The denial of street time under 61 P.S. § 331.21a(a) was constitutional, and the application of detention time to the earlier sentence was proper. Petitioner had a timely revocation hearing and respondent had no responsibility for the conditions of petitioner's incarceration.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the preliminary objections filed by respondent parole board and others, and dismissed the petition for review. The court held that it had no jurisdiction over already decided arrest issues, manner of attributing street and detention time was proper, procedural safeguards such as a timely revocation hearing were complied with, and respondent had no authority over incarceration conditions.

 

1090 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


McCoy v. Lincoln Intermediate Unit No. 12


No. 441 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


38 Pa. Commw. 29; 391 A.2d 1119; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1325


June 5, 1978, Argued  
September 28, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Secretary of Education in case of Appeal of Harold D. McCoy, a Professional Employee, from a decision of the Board of School Directors of the Lincoln Intermediate Unit, No. 12, New Oxford, Pennsylvania, No. 273.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged an order of the Secretary of Education (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his appeal from his demotion by the board of directors of respondent employer, an intermediate unit of school districts, contending that he was not demoted on any valid basis and that his demotion should be set aside because he was denied substantive due process under the Public School Code of 1949, and under U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was demoted by the board of directors (board) of respondent employer, an intermediate unit of school districts, and his administrative appeal of the demotion was dismissed. On appeal, appellant claimed that he was demoted on an invalid basis, because his supervisor did not like him and that his demotion should be set aside because he was denied substantive due process under the Public School Code of 1949 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed the order of dismissal, finding that substantial evidence on the record supported the board's decision to demote appellant and that the board reasonably exercised its discretion without any violation of due process. The court believed appellant was well aware of the basis for his demotion, considering that his supervisor informed him numerous times that his insubordinate, disruptive and disloyal conduct was in question, and it therefore, rejected appellant's contention that an unconstitutionally vague standard was applied. The court held that the record clearly indicated that appellant was afforded notice of his unsatisfactory performance and that he was given ample notice of his opportunity for a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant employee's appeal of his demotion, finding that substantial evidence supported the decision of the board of directors (board) of respondent employer, an intermediate unit of school districts, to demote appellant, that the board reasonably exercised its discretion without a violation of due process, and that appellant had notice of his unsatisfactory performance and of his opportunity for a hearing.

 

1091 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


In re Controller's Annual Report, Year 1972


No. 129 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


37 Pa. Commw. 580; 390 A.2d 1368; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1310


August 3, 1978, Submitted on Briefs  
September 19, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County in case of In Re: Controller's Annual Report for year 1972 of Lackanna County, No. 139 September Term, 1973.



DISPOSITION: Motion to quash granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania), which found no fraud or concealment on the part of appellees, controller and commissioners, in appellee controller's report and dismissed the appeal because it was untimely filed.


OVERVIEW: A group of taxpayers filed an appeal from appellee controller's report. The statute that authorized such appeals, 16 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2805, required that such appeals be entered within 90 days after the filing of the report. Appellee commissioners moved to dismiss the appeal because it was filed after the deadline. Appellants sought leave to file the appeal nunc pro tunc. After a hearing, the lower court found no fraud or concealment and dismissed the appeal because it had been untimely filed. Appellants, two taxpayers who were not among the taxpayers that filed the original appeal, sought review and the court granted appellees' motion to quash the appeal because appellants did not have standing to appeal from the order of the lower court. The court concluded that appellants were not aggrieved parties. The court found that because appellants were not parties initially, the lower court's adjudication was not adverse as to them. The court held that the detriment to the appellants as individual taxpayers was too remote because there was no evidence that they would be specially or directly affected by the alleged loss to the county of the funds.


OUTCOME: The court granted appellees', commissioners and controller, motion to quash because the court did not believe appellants, two taxpayers, had standing to appeal from the order by the lower court. The court concluded that appellants were not aggrieved parties.

 

1092 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


McCoy v. Commonwealth, Bd. of Medical Education & Licensure


No. 881 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


37 Pa. Commw. 530; 391 A.2d 723; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1303


June 7, 1978, Argued  
September 14, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Board of Medical Education and Licensure in case of In the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of the License of Orlo G. McCoy, M.D., to Practice as a Physician, License No. E 1845.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician sought review of an order of respondent State Board of Medical Education and Licensure (Pennsylvania), that suspended his license pursuant to 40 P.S. § 1301.701(a), challenging the constitutionality of the mandatory insurance provisions of the Health Care Services Malpractice Act 40 P.S. § 1301.101 et seq. under the due process and equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Pa. Const. art. III, § 32.


OVERVIEW: Appellant physician's license to practice medicine was suspended for failure to comply with 40 P.S. § 1301.701(a), which required malpractice insurance or proof of self-insurance and contribution to a Medical Professional Liability Catastrophe Loss Fund. Appellant claimed that the mandatory insurance provisions of the Health Care Services Malpractice Act, 40 P.S. § 1301.101 et seq., were unconstitutional under the due process and equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Pa. Const. art. III, § 32. The court affirmed the order suspending appellant's license, finding § 1301.701(a) to be constitutional. The court held that § 1301.701(a) did not violate appellant's right to substantive due process, finding that a real and demonstrable relation existed between the requirement of insurance and the objects sought to be attained thereby, and the court rejected the contention that license suspension was too harsh a penalty. With respect to equal protection, the court found that appellant was not treated unfairly by the applicability of § 1301.701(a) only to certain health care providers, because those included were more affected by the crisis that prompted § 1301.701(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order suspending appellant physician's license for noncompliance with mandatory insurance provisions of the Health Care Services Malpractice Act (Act), finding that appellant was not denied his right to substantive due process or equal protection, because there was a real and substantial relation between the provisions and the object of the Act and the Act was aimed at those most affected by the crisis that inspired it.

 

1093 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvania Parent Assistance Authority v. Sloan


No. 983 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


37 Pa. Commw. 159; 389 A.2d 1208; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1241


January 31, 1978, Argued  
August 8, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Pennsylvania Parent Assistance Authority v. Grace Sloan, Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Pennsylvania Parent Assistance Authority, petitioned the court for an order directing defendant state treasurer to reimburse plaintiff for its administrative expenses.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, the Pennsylvania Parent Assistance Authority, was created to administer a plan created by the legislature to provide tuition reimbursement for children going to non-public schools. The tuition reimbursement plan was found to be unconstitutional, and plaintiff sought an equitable order directing defendant state treasurer to reimburse plaintiff for the payment of expenses incident to the closing of its offices. The court denied the equitable relief sought by plaintiff because, defendant, having already transferred the money in the reimbursement fund to the general fund, had no authority to do so. There was no legislative directive that funds were be paid on plaintiff's behalf following the declaration that tuition reimbursement plan was unconstitutional. The court ruled that, even though it was sitting in equity, it could not order defendant to perform an illegal act.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition of plaintiff, the Pennsylvania Parent Assistance Authority, for an order directing defendant state treasurer to reimburse plaintiff for its administrative expenses. The court held that because there was no legislative authority permitting the release of the funds by the state treasurer from the general fund, it could not order defendant to perform an illegal act, even though it was sitting in equity.

 

1094 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Di Ciacco v. Civil Service Com.


Nos. 1726, 1727, 1728 and 1729 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


37 Pa. Commw. 77; 389 A.2d 703; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1229


April 6, 1978, Argued  
July 31, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in cases of Nicholas DiCiacco v. Civil Service Commission of the City of Philadelphia, No. 533 December Term, 1972; Joseph Gottwald v. Civil Service Commission of the City of Philadelphia, No. 3321 December Term, 1972; John Gerace v. Civil Service Commission of the City of Philadelphia, No. 2175 February Term, 1973; and Francis Kieffer v. Civil Service Commission of the City of Philadelphia, No. 2174 February Term, 1973.



DISPOSITION: Order in 1729 C.D. 1976 reversed. Case remanded. Remaining orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officers sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which found for appellee, Civil Service Commission, in appellants' action that challenged the termination of their employment for conduct unbecoming a police officer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officers were dismissed from their employment by appellee, Civil Service Commission, for conduct unbecoming a police officer after each made incriminating statements during investigatory inquiries. The trial court affirmed the dismissals, and the court affirmed three dismissals and reversed and remanded the fourth dismissal. The court found that under Philadelphia, Pa., Home Rule Charter § 10-110, none of appellants should have been told that their failure to respond to the inquiries would have resulted in their dismissal because that was a violation of their privilege against self-incrimination under U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV. However, two appellants waived the issue by the failure to raise it in the lower court. The third appellant made the incriminating statements without his employment having been threatened. The court held that there was corpus delicti and sufficient evidence to support the three dismissals. The court reversed the fourth appellant's dismissal and remanded for another hearing because he made the incriminating statement under the threat of the loss of his employment, and the statements were improperly admitted into evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order for appellee, Civil Service Commission, in an action concerning the dismissal of three appellant police officers because their incriminating statements were properly admitted. The court reversed and remanded the dismissal of one appellant police officer because that appellant's incriminating statement was inadmissible because he was threatened with the loss of his employment if he did not respond.

 

1095 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Delaware Valley Apartment House Owner's Asso. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Revenue


No. 171 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


36 Pa. Commw. 615; 389 A.2d 234; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1566


February 1, 1978, Argued  
July 21, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Delaware Valley Apartment House Owners' Association, by Paul R. Trichon, Trustee Ad Litem, and Hopkinson Associates v. Department of Revenue of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Pennsylvania Department of Revenue, filed preliminary objections in the action of petitioners, apartment owners and owners' association, seeking a declaratory judgment on the constitutionality of Tax Reform Code of 1971 § 201(m), 72 P.S. § 7201(m).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, apartment owners and owners' association, sought a declaratory judgment on the constitutionality of Tax Reform Code (code) of 1971 § 201(m), 72 P.S. Respondent, the Pennsylvania Department of Revenue, filed preliminary objections. On review, the court dismissed the objections, and held that that petitioner owner's association claim that the taxpayer status of its members has been affected by § 7201(m) was sufficient to confer standing on the association under the Declaratory Judgments Act § 2, 12 P.S. § 832. The refund provisions of the code did not provide a sufficient statutory remedy such that a declaratory judgment should not be permitted. Because the parties, and possibly the issues, in other litigation challenging § 7201(m) were not identical to the instant case, dismissal of petitioners' action was not required. Because petitioners merely sought a declaration that § 7201(m) was unconstitutional, the action was not barred by sovereign immunity. Petitioners properly initiated the action by way of a petition for review pursuant to Pa. R. App. P. 1501(a)(3), 1502.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the preliminary objections of respondent, the Pennsylvania Department of Revenue, holding that petitioner owners' association had standing to challenge the constitutionality of a tax statute, based on the taxpayer status of its members. A declaratory judgment action was appropriate as disputed factual questions could be resolved in such an action, and sovereign immunity was not a bar to it.

 

1096 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Curtis Bldg. Co. v. Tunstall


No. 635 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


36 Pa. Commw. 233; 387 A.2d 1370; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1186


April 3, 1978, Argued  
July 12, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County in case of Curtis Building Co., Inc. v. Joseph L. Tunstall, Jr. and Mary E. Tunstall, No. 5320 of 1971.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant purchaser sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which declared invalid a treasurer's deed under which appellant claimed title to property owned by appellee property owners because appellees had not been served with proper notice.


OVERVIEW: Appellant purchaser challenged a decision of the trial court, which declared invalid a treasurer's deed under which appellant claimed title to property owned by appellee property owners. The property had been sold to appellant at a treasurer's sale for the nonpayment of real estate taxes. The trial court had declared the tax sale void, on the basis that notice by certified mail was constitutionally inadequate under the circumstances and in violation of appellees' due process rights. The court reversed the order of the trial court and held that the notice required by due process was that which is reasonably calculated, under all of the circumstances, to actually apprise interested parties and afford them an opportunity to present their objections. Certified mail addressed to appellant at its actual place of residence was reasonably calculated to give actual notice of the proceedings to appellant. Appellant's signature was on the return receipt card, which gave the taxing authorities strong reason to believe that actual notice had in fact been received. Therefore, appellant had received proper notice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which declared invalid a treasurer's deed under which appellant purchaser claimed title to property owned by appellee property owners because appellees had not been served with proper notice, and held that the trial court's invalidation of appellees' deed was inappropriate because appellant had been afforded an opportunity to present its objections and actual notice had in fact been received.

Salix State Bank v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Banking


No. 1657 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


36 Pa. Commw. 120; 387 A.2d 673; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1120


February 28, 1978, Argued  
June 16, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Salix State Bank v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvavania, Department of Banking.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Department of Banking filed preliminary objections to the petition for review of petitioner bank invoking the original jurisdiction of the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania under §§ 401 and 403 of the Appellate Court Jurisdiction Act, 17 P.S. §§ 211.401- 403. Respondent alleged that it was immune from suit, that petitioner had failed to plead a justiciable issue, and that petitioner had failed to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Department of Banking determined that certain insurance premium financing contracts entered into by petitioner bank were direct loans that exceeded the lawful maximum interest rate and directed petitioner to rebate excessive interest charges. The bank invoked the original jurisdiction of the Commonwealth Court under 17 P.S. §§ 211.401 - 403 by filing a petition for review in the nature of a complaint in equity questioning a governmental determination. Respondent filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer for failure to state a cause of action, and alleged that it was immune from suit and that the petition failed to plead a justiciable issue. The court dismissed the preliminary objections because it held that sovereign immunity did not bar a suit seeking to restrain government officials from performing affirmative acts and that petitioner was not required to await judicial enforcement proceedings before seeking judicial review. The demurrer was overruled because on the state of the record the court could not say that the petition failed to state a cause of action. The court directed the respondent to file an answer to the petition for review.


OUTCOME: Respondent's preliminary objections were dismissed because the assertion of immunity from suit was without merit and petitioner was not required to await enforcement action before seeking judicial review. The court overruled the demurrer because in light of the many uncertainties about the practice at issue it could not conclude that the petition for review did not state a cause of action.

 

1098 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Caserta v. Milford Township


No. 477 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


35 Pa. Commw. 598; 387 A.2d 495; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1088


April 5, 1978, Argued  
June 5, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County in case of Pasquale Caserta et al. v. Milford Township, et al.; Richland Township, et al., and Haycock Township, et al., No. 75-11241-08-5.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, landowners and agents, sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which sustained preliminary objections in the nature of demurrers to plaintiffs' complaint in equity and entered judgment in favor of defendant townships in plaintiffs' challenge of the validity of defendants' zoning ordinances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant townships recommended the adoption of a zoning ordinance to certain municipalities, which in turn adopted the ordinance. Plaintiffs, landowners and agents, alleged that the ordinances unconstitutionally restricted the use of their property and that they were entitled to equitable relief in that the legal remedies provided were inadequate. The court affirmed, holding that plaintiffs were afforded a complete and adequate legal remedy under the Pennsylvania Municipalities Planning Code, 53 P.S. §§ 10913.1-11004. Being owners or agents of owners, plaintiffs could have attacked the procedure followed in the enactment of the ordinances. The substantive validity of the ordinances could have been challenged. And finally, plaintiffs' challenge to the general validity of the ordinances could have been brought, either by way of the zoning hearing board or by a request for a curative amendment. The court held that because plaintiffs had an adequate remedy at law, equity did not have jurisdiction over the subject matter of the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order sustaining judgment in favor of defendant townships in plaintiff landowners and agents' complaint in equity challenging the validity of defendants' zoning ordinances because plaintiffs were not entitled to equitable relief where they had an adequate remedy at law.

Philadelphia Chewing Gum Corp. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources


Nos. 1389, 1390, 1395 and 1415 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


35 Pa. Commw. 443; 387 A.2d 142; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1063


October 4, 1977, Argued  
May 24, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Environmental Hearing Board in cases of In the Matter of: Philadelphia Chewing Gum Corporation, Docket No. 75-253-D; Shell Oil Company, Docket No. 73-256-S; National Wood Preservers, Inc., Docket No. 73-249-D; and Clifford and Virginia Rogers, Docket No. 73-346-D.



DISPOSITION: Appeals of Philadelphia Chewing Gum Corporation and Shell Oil Company sustained. Appeals of National Wood Preservers, Inc. and Clifford and Virginia Rogers denied. Orders reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, land owners and occupiers, sought review of the orders of the Environmental Hearing Board (Pennsylvania), which sustained in part and dismissed in part the appeals of appellants from orders issued by respondent, environmental department, for appellants to take corrective measures with regard to what respondent determined was a condition on the land of appellants.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, environmental department, issued orders requiring appellants, land owners and occupiers, to take corrective measures as to the pollution of the waters of their land. The hearing board sustained in part and dismissed in part appellants' appeals, and the court reversed as to two appellants, sustaining their appeals, and affirmed as to the remaining appellants, denying their appeals. The court held that requiring appellants who had not caused the pollution to spend the sums necessary to abate the condition, based solely upon their ownership or occupancy of land, was employing means unduly oppressive upon these individuals. The court held that the board's conclusion that 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 691.316 was a declaration of the strict liability of appellants to correct the condition was erroneous as a matter of law because such a construction of § 316 would permit the commonwealth to engage in regulation which constituted the taking of property without compensation, and hence, would be an unconstitutional exercise of police power. The court held that two appellants had never been associated with the condition, while the remaining appellants had at least adopted the condition.


OUTCOME: Orders of environmental board reversed as to two appellants, sustaining their appeals, and affirmed as to the remaining appellants, denying their appeals because requiring those appellants who did not cause the pollution to sustain the financial burden of correcting it was too onerous a burden and would constitute a taking under the state's police power.

McCracken v. Central Susquehanna Intermediate Unit


No. 190 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


34 Pa. Commw. 148; 382 A.2d 1293; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 899


February 3, 1978, Argued  
March 7, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Secretary of Education in case of Helen K. McCracken v. Central Susquehanna Intermediate Unit, No. 280, dated December 27, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee appealed an order of the Secretary of Education (Pennsylvania), which dismissed her appeal of respondent school district's decision terminating her employment on the grounds of lack of jurisdiction under § 1131 of the Public School Code of 1949, 24 P.S. § 11-1131.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee was dismissed from her positions as Coordinator of NonPublic School Services and Director of Adult Basic Education by respondent school district. The Secretary of Education dismissed her appeal pursuant to § 1131 of the Public School Code of 1949, 24 P.S. § 11-1131, on the grounds that petitioner was not a teacher and therefore not a professional employee entitled to an appeal to the Secretary. The court affirmed, holding that petitioner was not a teacher under 24 P.S. § 11-1141 because she did not show that at least 50 percent of her time was spent in "teaching or direct educational activities." Petitioner admitted that her duties did not include teaching, and the court found that her work, which included visits to nonpublic schools, determining what materials and services would be suitable for nonpublic schools, keeping the lines of communication open between nonpublic schools and respondent, and coordinating the funding and operations of the adult basic education program, were administrative, not direct educational activities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Secretary of Education that it did not have jurisdiction to hear the appeal of petitioner employee's dismissal by respondent school district because petitioner did not devote at least 50 percent of her time to teaching or other educational activities necessary to be a teacher so as to have a right to appeal.

Petitioner also filed a petition for review of the trial court's denial of petitioner's motion to amend its decree to include language required by 17 P.S. § 211.501(b).

Petitioner presented a motion to the trial court to amend the decree to provide a statement which allowed immediate appeal as required by 17 P.S. § 211.501(b), which was denied by the trial court. The court therefore transferred the matters to the supreme court.


OUTCOME: The court that it was without authority to grant petitioner education association's interlocutory appeal from an order of the trial court which entered a decree enjoining a work stoppage by petitioner because the trial court had refused to amend its decree to provide for immediate appeal, and since the trial court declared a portion of a statute unconstitutional, the court transferred a petition for review to the Supreme Court's jurisdiction.

Schneck v. Philadelphia


No. 1859 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


34 Pa. Commw. 96; 383 A.2d 227; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 882


October 5, 1977, Argued  
February 27, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in case of George W. Schneck, Howard M. Kuehner and The Pennsylvania Federation of Sportsmen's Clubs, Inc. v. City of Philadelphia and Frank Rizzo, Mayor, and Sheldon Albert, City Solicitor, and Hiller Levinson, City Managing Director, and Joseph O'Neill, Commissioner of Police and Dominic Sabatini, Commissioner of the Department of Licenses and Inspections and Colosimo's Gun Center, No. 6241 May Term, 1975.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Enforcement of ordinance enjoined.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant firearms purchasers challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) dismissing their action against appellees, city and city officials, and denying appellants a permanent injunction against appellees' enforcement of the city's gun ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant firearms purchasers were unable to purchase firearms in appellee city because, although they proffered compliance with the Uniform Firearms Act (Act), 18 P.S. § 6101 et seq., they refused to comply with the application and license requirements of appellee city's local ordinance, which regulated the acquisition and transfer of firearms in that city. Appellants argued that the ordinance regulated the lawful ownership, possession, or transportation of firearms and was therefore preempted by state legislation, which provided for the comprehensive regulation of the sale, licensing, transfer, and delivery of firearms throughout the state. On appeal, the court agreed, holding that the Act clearly preempted local governments from regulating the lawful ownership, possession, and transportation of firearms, and that appellee's ordinance attempted to regulate firearms in the manner indicated in the statute as prohibited. The court enjoined appellees, city and its officers, from enforcing the local ordinance and reversed the order of the court below.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing appellant firearms purchasers' complaint and denying them a permanent injunction of the enforcement of appellee city's gun ordinance was reversed. The local ordinance attempted to regulate the lawful ownership, possession, or transportation of firearms in a manner specifically prohibited by state statute.

Danson v. Casey


No. 781 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


33 Pa. Commw. 614; 382 A.2d 1238; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 857


October 4, 1977, Argued  
February 14, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of William Danson and Edith, his wife, et al. and The School District of Philadelphia v. Robert E. Casey, State Treasurer, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Caryl M. Kline, Secretary of Education, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents Pennsylvania Treasurer and Pennsylvania Secretary of Education filed preliminary objections to a suit filed by petitioners School District of Philadelphia and parents seeking to enjoin implementation of the state's system of school financing which allegedly violated the provisions of Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 14 and 32.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners School District of Philadelphia and parents claimed that the state's statutory system of school financing failed to provide adequate funds to petitioner school district for a thorough and efficient education of its public school children as mandated by Pa. Const. art. III, § 14, and that it denied these children equal educational opportunity solely because of their residence, in violation of Pa. Const. art. III, § 32. Petitioners sought a decree enjoining and restraining respondents Pennsylvania Treasurer and Pennsylvania Secretary of Education from making payments of state funds to any other school districts. The court sustained respondents' preliminary objections and dismissed the action. The court held that there was no discrimination, invidious or otherwise, in a system that applied a uniform subsidy formula statewide, while at the same time adapting to community diversification by providing for local taxation. The court found that the state's subsidy formula, which weighed district density, poverty, number of students, cost per student, and district wealth, bore a facially fair and substantial relation to promoting equal educational opportunity.


OUTCOME: Finding that petitioners School district of Philadelphia and parents failed to state a cause of action for violations of the state constitution, the court sustained preliminary objections filed by respondents state treasurer and state secretary of education, and dismissed petitioners' action for injunctive relief from imposition of the state's school funding system.

1107 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Concerned Taxpayers of Allegheny County v. Commonwealth


No. 2165 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


33 Pa. Commw. 518; 382 A.2d 490; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 849


November 2, 1977, Argued  
February 9, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Concerned Taxpayers of Allegheny County, a nonprofit corporation v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and Grace Sloan, State Treasurer.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Bill dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonprofit organization brought a suit in equity to enjoin defendants, state and state treasurer, from disbursing funds in accordance with the Act of June 29, 1976, 65 P.S. § 364 on the grounds that it was unconstitutional pursuant to Pa. Const. art. II, §§ 1, 8 and Pa. Const. art. III §§ 9, 24.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff nonprofit organization brought a suit in equity to enjoin defendants, state and state treasurer, from disbursing funds under the Act of June 29, 1976, 65 P.S. § 364 on the grounds that it was unconstitutional pursuant to Pa. Const. art. II, § 1, 8 and Pa. Const. art. III §§ 9, 24. Defendants alleged that the court lacked jurisdiction pursuant to Pa. Const. art. I, § 11, which permitted suits against the state only if the legislature had specifically provided for it. The court held that a suit to enjoin any state officer from enforcing a statute that was claimed to be unconstitutional was not a suit against the state and was therefore not barred by sovereign immunity. Defendants also alleged that plaintiff as a nonprofit organization, which did not pay taxes, lacked the standing to assert a taxpayer's suit on its on behalf and did not establish standing to bring suit on behalf of its member taxpayers. The court held that plaintiff did not have standing on its own or standing to assert the interest of its taxpaying members, because plaintiff had not established facts indicating a direct, immediate, and substantial injury to the taxpayers. The court dismissed the suit.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff nonprofit organization's suit in equity was dismissed, because its complaint failed to establish a direct, immediate, and substantial injury to member taxpayers, which was necessary to give the plaintiff standing to pursue its action on behalf of its member taxpayers.

 

1108 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Kavanagh v. London Grove Township


No. 594 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


33 Pa. Commw. 420; 382 A.2d 148; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 836


December 7, 1977, Argued  
February 1, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County in case of In Re: Appeal of Edward F. Kavanagh, Huston T. Adams and Robert M. Abernethy v. London Grove Township, No. 137 June Term, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania) which affirmed an order dismissing an application for a curative amendment to run a privately-owned and operated landfill on land zoned only for municipality-owned or operated landfills.


OVERVIEW: Appellants landowners applied for a curative amendment to a zoning ordinance which would allow them to establish a privately-owned and operated landfill on their property. The application was denied and appellants challenged the order arguing that it was exclusionary, discriminatory, arbitrary, and unconstitutional. On review the court found that it was not exclusionary in that the zoning ordinance allowed for landfills as long as they were municipally owned or operated. The court held that it was within the legislature's purview to establish this type of ordinance. The court also found that 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6001 et seq., the Pennsylvania Solid Waste Management Act, did not preempt the ordinance. The court further held that the ordinance only regulated uses of property, not who used the property. The court therefore found that the ordinance was valid and affirmed the order of denial.


OUTCOME: The denial of appellant landowners' application for a curative amendment allowing them to run a privately-owned and operated landfill was affirmed, because the ordinance was not exclusionary nor did was it preempted by statute, and it did not regulate property users, just property uses.

 

1109 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


County of Lawrence v. Foht


No. 961 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


33 Pa. Commw. 379; 381 A.2d 1348; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 831


October 4, 1977, Argued  
January 30, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County in case of County of Lawrence v. Robert E. Foht, County Controller of Lawrence County, No. 140 of 1975, M.D.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county controller challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County (Pennsylvania), which directed that appellant repay to appellee county the salary that was paid to him for his services as secretary of the County Retirement Board on the grounds that the salary violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 27, which prohibited post-election increases in salary, and was prohibited by Act 113 of 1971, 16 P.S. § 11011-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant county controller, in addition to his duties as controller, served as secretary of the County Retirement Board and was provided a salary for to his services as secretary pursuant to the County Pension Law of 1971, 16 P.S. § 11651 et seq. The county solicitor rendered an opinion that Act 113 of 1971, 16 P.S. § 11011-1 et seq., prohibited appellant from receiving any compensation above that fixed for the office of controller in the act. The solicitor also found that additional payments made to appellant for his duties as secretary violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 27, which prohibited post-election increases in salary. The lower court directed appellant to repay appellee county for his salary received as secretary. The court reversed and held that the intent of the legislature under 16 P.S. § 11655 was to provide compensation to appellant for his duties as secretary and that this was not inconsistent with Act 113 of 1971, because the statute could be interpreted not to prohibit compensation for a separate position with separate duties. Likewise, the constitution was not violated, because it could be interpreted to only prohibit increases in salary for the same position.


OUTCOME: The lower court order's order was reversed, because the intent of the legislature was to provide compensation to appellant county controller for his duties and position as secretary of the County Retirement Board and this was not inconsistent with Act 113 of 1971 or unconstitutional, due to the fact appellant was receiving a salary for a separate position with different responsibilities.
