January 25, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargment Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County in cases of Herbert & Irma Barness; Joseph A. & Norma J. Ciccone, his wife; John F., Jr. & Della Enders; John F. Enders, Jr. and Della E. Enders, et al.; Donald Greenberg, et al.; Claude J. Schlanger; and Robert H. Yaroschuk and K. Patricia Yaroschuk v. Board of Supervisors of Buckingham Township, Nos. 75-2561-08-5, 75-2562-08-5, 75-2563-08-5, 75-2993-08-5, 75-2994-08-5, 75-3053-08-5 and 75-4715-08-5.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Board of Supervisors of Buckingham Township, Land Use Task Force (board) and the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources, challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the zoning appeals of appellee landowners challenging the validity of the township zoning ordinance and requesting curative amendments.


OVERVIEW: Appellee landowners filed zoning appeals with appellant, the Board of Supervisors of Buckingham Township (board), which challenged an ordinance permitting only single-family construction and requested curative amendments. Appellant board dismissed the zoning appeals. The trial court sustained the appeals finding the ordinance unconstitutionally exclusionary and remanded to the board. Appellants, the board, joined by the Land Use Task Force and the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources, sought review. The court affirmed and held that the zoning ordinance's exclusion of legitimate residential uses did not bear a substantial relationship to the protection of health, safety, and the general welfare. The advertisement of amendments to the comprehensive plan was insufficient public notice of an intention to rezone and did not prevent appellees from filing zoning appeals. The court found that appellees must be issued permits to build as they proposed because 53 P.S. § 11004(2)(c) implied that grant of permits was the remedy in requests for curative amendments and landowners successful in challenging this type of zoning deserved definitive relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the unconstitutionality of a zoning ordinance permitting only single-family construction and directed appellant, the Board of Supervisors of Buckingham Township, to issue permits to appellee landowners to build as they proposed.

Singer v. Sheppard


No. 1489 C.D. 1974


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


33 Pa. Commw. 276; 381 A.2d 1007; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 803


September 15, 1977, Argued  
January 9, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Richard J. Singer, individually and on behalf of all Residents, Taxpayers, Pedestrians, Motor Vehicle Owners and Occupants of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. William J. Sheppard, Insurance Commissioner of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and J. Finton Speller, Secretary of Health of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Jacob G. Kassab, Secretary of Transportation of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Israel Packel, Attorney General of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Paul J. Smith, Secretary of Labor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Vincent X. Yakowicz, Secretary of Revenue of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Motion granted. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought declaratory judgment on constitutionality of Pennsylvania No-fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act (Act), 40 Pa. Const. Stat. § 1003 et seq, against Commonwealth officials charged with administration and implementation of Act, and argued it violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and the Act's title violated Pa. Const. Art. III, §3.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs initiated a class action, which sought to enjoin implementation and enforcement of Pennsylvania No-fault Act (Act), 40 Pa. Const. Stat. § 1003 et seq. Defendants sought dismissal on lack of standing and inappropriateness of a declaratory action. The court held that antagonistic claims clearly existed between the parties which would lead to imminent and inevitable litigation, and rights of plaintiff and class were sufficiently affected by provisions of the Act to provide standing. Declaratory Judgment Act could not be utilized to consider plaintiff's rights in anticipation of events, or for rendition of advisory opinions. The challenge as to U.S. Const. amend. XVI was meritless as the classification scheme was not arbitrary and was consistent with a stated objective, thus, constitutional. Classifications may be imperfect, but not unconstitutional, and incidental provisions of a statute needn't be enumerated in the title if they were germane to legislation as a whole.


OUTCOME: The court held the Pennsylvania No-fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act, 40 Pa. Const. Stat. § 1003 et seq, did not deny U.S. Const. amend. XVI, due process or equal protection and that its' title did not violate the Pennsylvania Constitution, defendant's motion for judgment on the pleadings was therefore granted.

Application of Friday


Nos. 158 and 303 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


33 Pa. Commw. 256; 381 A.2d 504; 1978 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 800


November 2, 1977, Argued  
January 9, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in case of In Re: Application of John A. Friday, et ux., Requesting Fox Chapel Borough Zoning Hearing Board to Hear Applicants' Challenges to the Fox Chapel Zoning Ordinance and Map and Make Findings of Fact and Divisions Based Thereon, No. S.A. 96 of 1976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and intervenors, challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) reversing a decision of the zoning hearing board that dismissed a challenge by appellee applicant to the validity of the appellant's zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city's zoning ordinance did not provide for multi-family dwelling use. Appellee applicant submitted a challenge to the constitutional validity of the use provisions. The submission included a plan for an apartment building. The zoning board concluded that the ordinance was valid and dismissed appellee's challenge. The trial court reversed the zoning board's decision. Appellants, city and intervenors, argued that the ordinance enjoyed a presumption of validity, and appellee failed to carry the burden of proving that the ordinance totally excluded apartment use. The court disagreed, holding that the presumption of validity is rebutted, as it was demonstrated that the ordinance entirely excluded a facially legitimate use. Moreover, the court declared that appellant city was required to establish that its regulation bore a relationship to the public health, safety, and welfare. The court found that appellant city failed to carry this burden. Appellants also argued that membership in a regional planning effort cured the otherwise unconstitutional nature of the ordinance. The court disagreed and held that a comprehensive plan did not have the legal effect of a zoning ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court reversing a decision of the zoning hearing board that dismissed a challenge by appellee applicant to the validity of the appellant city's zoning ordinance. The court found that appellant failed to meet its burden of proof in showing that its zoning ordinance excluding multi-family dwellings bore a relationship to the public health, safety, and welfare.

 

1113 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


In re Suspension or Revocation of the License to Practice as a Dentist


No. 61 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


32 Pa. Commw. 541; 380 A.2d 497; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1145


March 8, 1977, Argued  
December 2, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Dental Council and Examining Board in case of In the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of the License to Practice as a Dentist, No. 17028, issued July 17, 1969 to William F. Bruteyn, D.M.D.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dentist sought review of the decision of appellee State Dental Council and Examining Board (Pennsylvania), revoking his license to practice dentistry.


OVERVIEW: Appellant dentist alleged that the decision of appellee State Dental Council and Examining Board violated his due process rights in revoking his license to practice dentistry. The court remanded for a new hearing, because it found sufficient indications to warrant a conclusion that appellant was denied a fair trial. Specifically, the prosecutor who provided pre-hearing legal advice to the board also served as the prosecuting attorney, provided legal advice to the hearing body, and drafted and reviewed the final adjudication and order. Although the exigencies of modern corporate government required that one entity within a particular agency make the decision to prosecute, and another to sit as adjudicator, the same attorney could not both prosecute the case and draft the adjudication and order in which he took it upon himself to amend and supplement certain findings. The prosecutor's actions created a sufficient appearance of impropriety as to warrant a denial of due process. Therefore, the case was remanded although the court was unconvinced that any actual prejudice adhered to appellant's case.


OUTCOME: The decision revoking appellant dentist's license to practice dentistry was remanded to appellee State Dental Council and Examining Board, because appellant's due process rights were violated by the prosecutor's multiple roles in the adjudication process.

 

1114 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Bunner v. Commonwealth, Board of Probation & Parole


No. 466 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


32 Pa. Commw. 483; 379 A.2d 1368; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1144


October 14, 1977, Submitted on Briefs  
December 2, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Gary R. Bunner v. Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole.



DISPOSITION: Motion of respondent granted. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parolee filed an action in the court seeking review of the decision of respondent Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, which revoked his parole and both parties subsequently filed motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner parolee was sentenced to a term of imprisonment of from 5 years and 6 months to 12 years and was later paroled. Following respondent board of probation and parole's inability to locate him, petitioner was declared delinquent. Respondent recommitted petitioner to his original sentence, by recalculation fixed the maximum termination date, and denied petitioner credit for the time on parole during which he could not be located according to the Parole Act § 21.1(b), 61 P.S. § 331.2a(b). On appeal, the court granted respondent's motion for summary judgment, holding that petitioner possessed no right to credit for time spent on parole while in violation of the conditions of his parole. The court found that respondent's notices met constitutional due process requirements, because they accurately described the evidence relied on as petitioner's admission that he had failed to notify respondent of his whereabouts and adequately gave respondent's reason for revoking parole as his disregard for his parole obligations.


OUTCOME: The court granted respondent board of probation and parole's motion for summary judgment and dismissed petitioner parolee's petition for review. The court held that petitioner was not denied his constitutional due process rights and that his period of parole was not extended beyond the maximum term imposed by his sentence.

Hampden v. Tenny


Nos. 1441 C.D. 1976, 490 C.D. 1977


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


32 Pa. Commw. 301; 379 A.2d 635; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1100


September 13, 1977, Argued  
November 3, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County in case of Township of Hampden v. William B. Tenny and Shirley A. Tenny, No. 685 December Term, 1974.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review from two orders entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania). In one order, the lower court dismissed appellants' petition to set aside an arbitration award in favor of appellee township, and in the other, the lower court entered judgment in favor of appellee on appellants' de novo appeal from the arbitration award.


OVERVIEW: When, after getting subdivision approval, appellant landowners breached an agreement with appellee township to improve certain land, appellee sued appellants for the cost of the improvements. The case was sent to arbitration, but appellants did not attend, and appellee was granted an award. Appellants sought review, and also filed a petition to set the award aside. The lower court dismissed the petition, ruling that the direct appeal rendered it superfluous. While appellants awaited review of the order dismissing the petition, the lower court proceeded to try the de novo appeal, and a verdict was returned for appellee. Appellants' post-trial motions were denied, and appellants again sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the lower court's order dismissing the petition was not appealable, and any review thereof was cut off by appellants' direct challenge to the award. The lower court rightly proceeded to try the case de novo, because no stay was obtained. The new matters appellants had raised for the first time on appeal, even if considered, lacked any merit, and appellants were legally bound either to complete the improvements or pay the cost thereof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment in favor of appellee township for costs incurred to complete improvements which appellant landowners had agreed to make as a condition of approval of their subdivision plat. The lower court was correct in dismissing appellants' petition to set aside the award, and in hearing the case de novo on appellants' demand for review, and the resulting verdict did not invade appellants' constitutional rights.

Burchanowski v. County of Lycoming


No. 1379 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


32 Pa. Commw. 207; 378 A.2d 1025; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1077


June 8, 1977, Argued  
October 19, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County in case of Valentine P. Burchanowski and Mary H. Burchanowski v. County of Lycoming, School District of the Borough of Montoursville, Borough of Montoursville and Calvin L. Clees, Tax Collector, No. 76-0459.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants husband and wife sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County (Pennsylvania), which held that a housewife is engaged in an "occupation" within the meaning of the Local Tax Enabling Act, 53 P.S. § 6901 et seq., in appellant's action in equity against defendants borough, school district, and county.


OVERVIEW: Appellant wife, a homemaker, received a bill for occupation and per capita taxes levied by defendants borough, school district, and county pursuant to the authority granted by the Local Tax Enabling Act, 53 P.S. § 6901 et seq., the Fourth to Eighth Class County Assessment Law, 53 P.S. § 6901 et seq., and the Public School Code of 1949, 24 P.S. § 6-601 et seq. After appellant husband was notified that his wages were being attached, appellants brought an action in equity. Appellants sought review but the court dismissed their appeal as nonjusticiable, holding that they lacked standing to bring the appeal. The court found that although one issue was decided against appellants, they won their case and could not claim to have been "aggrieved" by the decision. The court concluded that appellants' concern about possible future action by the taxing authorities in amending the resolutions did not constitute a controversy appropriate for the court's review.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant husband and wife's appeal as nonjusticiable, holding that they lacked standing to bring the appeal because they had won their case.

Bovino v. Board of School Directors


No. 1335 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


32 Pa. Commw. 105; 377 A.2d 1284; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1060


June 10, 1977, Argued  
October 4, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Secretary of Education in case of In Re: Appeal of Anthony J. Bovino, dated July 6, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner professional employee appealed from a decision of the Secretary of Education (Pennsylvania), which sustained his dismissal by respondent Board of School Directors for immoral and cruel conduct, based on comments he made to a female student. Petitioner contended that the hearings before respondent were not fair, impartial, and unbiased.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Board of School Directors (board) filed charges against petitioner professional employee pursuant to 24 Pa. Cons. Stat. §1-101 et seq., based on comments he made to a female student. The student alleged that petitioner called her a slut and a prostitute. Following a hearing, respondent found that the statements were of such a nature as to constitute "immoral" and "cruel" conduct which were grounds for termination of petitioner's contract with the school district. The secretary of education (secretary) affirmed the dismissal, and petitioner sought further review. The court affirmed because the secretary made no error of law or abuse of discretion in finding that the hearings were fair, impartial, and unbiased. The court reasoned that the questions the board members asked the witnesses were not prejudicial or biased but showed a genuine desire to elicit from the witnesses all of the pertinent information surrounding petitioner's statements to the complainant student. Petitioner and his witnesses were given ample opportunity to present their version of what transpired. Further, the testimony was confined to the issues raised in the statement of charges before respondent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that affirmed petitioner professional employee's dismissal because the secretary of education made no error of law or abuse of discretion in finding that the hearings were fair, impartial, and unbiased. The court also ruled that the secretary properly found petitioner's statements to be immoral and cruel, since calling a young girl a slut offended the morals of the community and inflicted embarrassment upon her.

The court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it totally prohibited townhouse development throughout a township, and therefore, rejected contentions by appellant board and intervenors that such use was permitted in certain districts.

Nicholas, Heim & Kissinger v. Harris

Stat. § 11004.

Chmill v. Pittsburgh


No. 1047 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


31 Pa. Commw. 98; 375 A.2d 841; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 980; 15 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 447; 14 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P7745


May 4, 1977, Argued  
July 15, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in case of John S. Chmill, David Hirosky, John G. Holtz, Thomas Pflum, David J. Puciata, Lawrence T. Yakich and Paul R. Myers v. City of Pittsburgh, Pittsburgh Civil Service Commission and Stephen A. Glickman, No. GD 76-08187 and S.A. Nos. 614, 615, 661-664, 750 of 1976.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, firefighter candidates, sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which denied appellants relief in their action to enjoin appellee city and civil service commission from hiring any firefighters until their status could be ascertained with regard to their claim of reverse discrimination in hiring firefighters.


OVERVIEW: Appellant firefighter candidates were at the top of the certification list for appellee city and civil service commission when appellees decided to certify 50 percent minority candidates rather than those at the top of the competitive list for hiring as firefighters. Appellants filed a complaint in equity and appeals with the commission seeking to enjoin appellees from hiring any firefighters until appellants' status was ascertained, all of which were denied or dismissed by the trial court and the hiring of minority firefighters through the quota system was affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed and held that reasonable grounds did not exist for the denial of an injunction by the trial court. The court found that appellees violated the express terms of the Civil Service Act (CSA), 53 P.S. § 23493.1, and that the trial court erred in finding that federal and state laws took precedence over the CSA, and that no provision in the Human Relations Act, 43 P.S. § 951 et seq., or the Civil Rights Act of 1964, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000e-2(j) which allowed for such reverse discrimination. The record supported no justification for the use of quotas, especially without the direction of a court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of appellant firefighter candidates' action in equity because appellee city and civil service commission clearly violated state law by imposing an arbitrary racial quota system which was not supported by any state or federal law or constitutional principle.

Commonwealth v. Atlantic & Gulf Stevedores, Inc.


No. 246 T.D. 1970


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


30 Pa. Commw. 512; 373 A.2d 1385; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1213


March 9, 1977, Argued  
June 13, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in case of In Re: Atlantic & Gulf Stevedores, Inc., Docket No. R22232.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant stevedoring company sought review of the order of the Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which refused to review the resettlement of appellant's corporate income tax return by respondent Pennsylvania Department of Revenue.


OVERVIEW: Appellant stevedoring company was organized in Pennsylvania and owned no real property in the commonwealth. Appellee Pennsylvania Department of Revenue settled tax against appellant which appellant challenged arguing that it was a domestic corporation engaged exclusively in interstate and foreign commerce and was, therefore, not subject to tax under the Corporation Income Tax Law (CIT), 72 P.S. § 7502. On appeal, the court affirmed the order of the finance board that the settlement was proper and held that the CIT clearly applied to appellant because it applied to "every corporation," not just foreign corporations. The court found that the imposition of CIT did not violate the uniformity clause of the Pennsylvania constitution because it was applied to other domestic corporations, and where it was not, the Corporate Net Income Tax was imposed; the two taxing schemes were found to be substantially the same in application. The court also found that the CIT did not constitute an unconstitutional tax on the privilege of doing business in the commonwealth, because such taxes did not violate U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the settlement of corporate income taxes of appellant stevedoring company because it was organized in Pennsylvania and was subject to the commonwealth corporate tax statutes.

 

1123 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Rochester v. Geary


Nos. 21 T.D. and 1276 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


30 Pa. Commw. 493; 373 A.2d 1380; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 910


May 4, 1977, Argued  
June 10, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County in case of Borough of Rochester v. Roberta Geary, No. 1652 of 1975.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual on public assistance sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed her appeal from a judgment in assumpsit rendered by a lower court in appellee borough's favor in its action against appellant for unpaid per capita taxes.


OVERVIEW: Appellee borough imposed a 5-dollar per capita tax on all of its residents over the age of 18 years. Appellant individual on public assistance did not pay the tax and requested an exoneration. Appellee refused appellant's request for an exoneration and brought an action in assumpsit in a lower court, which resulted in a judgment against appellant. Appellant challenged the judgment in the trial court, which dismissed appellant's challenge. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that 72 P.S. § 5511.37 did not mandate exoneration for indigent persons. Rather, the statute placed the discretion in the hands of appellee. Therefore, the failure of appellee to grant an exoneration to appellant was not an abuse of discretion. The court also held that the Local Tax Enabling Act, 53 P.S. § 6901 et seq., did not exclude indigent persons from the payment of per capita taxes. The court also held that such taxation did not violate the Federal Aid for Dependent Children Program, 42 U.S.C.S. § 601 et seq., or the Public Welfare Code 62 P.S. § 601.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which dismissed of appellant individual on public assistance's appeal challenging the judgment in assumpsit rendered in favor of appellee borough in its action against appellant to recover unpaid per capita taxes. Appellee acted within its discretion in refusing to exonerate appellant from paying the per capita tax.

 

1124 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Appeal of GFM Associates


No. 1190 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


30 Pa. Commw. 476; 373 A.2d 1370; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 908


May 6, 1977, Argued  
June 9, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in case of In Re: Appeal of GFM Associates from Decision of Board of Commissioners of the Township of Mt. Lebanon, Nos. SA 147 of 1974 and SA 148 of 1974.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developers sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee commissioners' motion to quash appellant's appeal of a decision to deny approval to development plans for a mobile home park.


OVERVIEW: Appellant developer sought to build a mobile home park in Allegheny county. The local zoning ordinances did not allow for mobile home parks. Appellant submitted a development plan to appellee commissioners and it was denied. On appeal, the trial court granted appellees' motion to quash. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court and found that the grant of the motion to quash was proper because appellant failed to follow the correct procedure for challenging the zoning law. The court found that appellant's challenge was to the substance of the zoning ordinance, not merely the denial by appellees, thus appellant should have proceeded pursuant to 53 P.S. § 11004, which required appellant to submit the challenge either to the zoning hearing board for a report, or to the governing body with a request for a curative amendment. Appellant erred when he followed the procedures set out in 53 P.S. § 11006, which was applicable to contests to zoning decisions on the basis that they were not authorized by or contrary to the provisions of an ordinance or map.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of appellee commissioners' motion to quash in appellant developer's appeal of a zoning decision because appellant was contesting the substance of the zoning ordinance, not merely appellees' decision, and failed to follow the statutorily prescribed procedure for bringing that type of legal challenge.

Radnor Township School Dist. v. Betty


Nos. 1392 and 1393 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


30 Pa. Commw. 425; 373 A.2d 1361; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 897


April 6, 1977, Argued  
June 6, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County in cases of Radnor Township School District, Radnor Township, Delaware County and Delaware County Institutional District v. Robert K. Betty and Marion Betty, his wife, No. 75-1138; and Radnor Township School District, Radnor Township, Delaware County and Delaware County Institutional District v. Roland Massimino and Mary Jane Massimino, his wife, No. 75-3342.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lessors challenged the orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which ordered appellants, pursuant to the Administrative Code of 1929, Act of April 9, 1929, 71 P.S. §§ 512(c), (d), to make certain payments in lieu of paying taxes to appellees, various county and local governments.


OVERVIEW: Appellant lessors used property owned by the state. Appellees, various county and local governments, sought payments in lieu of taxes under 71 P.S. §§ 512(c), (d), which required that lessors of real property owned by the state for state highways make payments to the political subdivisions in which the property was situated equal to the taxes which would normally have been assessed against the property had it not been owned by the state. Appellants argued that the statute was unconstitutional. The court, on appeal, affirmed the order of the lower court and found that the classification scheme in the statute was rational and bore a legitimate relation to governmental interests. The court found that appellants enjoyed all the benefits of being within the political subdivision, such as police and fire protection, and since the state paid no taxes to appellees, appellees would have been required to provide those services to appellants for free. The court further found that because all members of the class of state lessors were treated equally, the statute did not violate Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1, which required all taxes to have been uniform, upon the same class of subjects.


OUTCOME: The court, on appeal, affirmed the lower court's orders requiring appellant lessors to make certain payments to appellees, various county and local governments, in lieu of taxes because appellants were members of the class of lessors of property owned by the state and the statute was not an unconstitutional denial of due process because it treated all members of the class equally.

Appeal of Carr


No. 84 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


30 Pa. Commw. 342; 374 A.2d 735; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 885


April 5, 1977, Argued  
May 27, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County in case of In Re: Appeal of Daniel J. Carr, Jr. and Laura G. Carr, h/w, from the Denial of a Curative Amendment Application by the Board of Supervisors of New Britain Township, No. 75-2428-07-6.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commercial property owners sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the rejection by the Board of Supervisors of a curative amendment to the township's zoning ordinance which would have allowed appellants to enlarge their now non-conforming commercial use pursuant to the Municipalities Planning Code, 53 P.S. § 11004(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Appellant commercial property owners sought a building permit, which was denied because a new rezoning plan was pending. The new zoning created a blanket prohibition against commercial use on all of appellant's property and their business became a non-conforming use. Appellants sought approval under the Municipalities Planning Code, 53 P.S. § 11004(1)(b), for a curative amendment which would have allowed them to expand their non-conforming use which was denied and the Board of Supervisors then amended the zoning ordinance to allow for 50 percent expansion. The trial court found the blanket prohibition had been invalid, but dismissed appellant's action because of the amendment. On appeal, the court reversed and held that after the trial court found the zoning ordinance unlawful it should have determined whether appellant's proposal was reasonable and disregarded the amendment of the zoning ordinance which occurred after the challenge was submitted. The municipality could not thwart a valid challenge to its zoning ordinance by adopting a curative amendment. The court remanded for a determination of the extent to which appellants could expand their business.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded appellant commercial property owners' challenge to their township's zoning ordinance under state law because the trial court was required to determine the reasonableness of their proposed use without reference to a curative amendment which was not pending at the time of the challenge.

Pennsylvania State Horse Racing Com. v. Di Santo


No. 93 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 574; 372 A.2d 487; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 817


February 3, 1977, Argued  
April 21, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania State Horse Racing Commission in case of Pennsylvania State Horse Racing Commission v. Alex Anthony DiSanto, No. 75-034.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant horse-racer sought review of an order from appellee Pennsylvania State Horse Racing Commission, which suspended appellant's license to race horses in Pennsylvania for a period of five years for violating Rule 1.11 of the Pennsylvania Rules of Racing, 15 P.S. § 2652.


OVERVIEW: After the horse of appellant horse-racer placed third in a race, it was ruled that appellant's license privileges should be suspended for violating Rule 1.11 of the Pennsylvania Rules of Racing, 15 P.S. § 2652. Appellee Pennsylvania State Horse Racing Commission affirmed this ruling and set the period of suspension for five years. Appellant sought review. The court modified appellee's order and suspended appellant's license for two years. The court found that appellant's instructions to his jockey not to ride the horse to win could have been in violation of Rule 1.11. The court determined that the language in Rule 1.11, which allowed a suspension for acting "to the detriment of racing," indicated that the rule was applicable to conduct other than that specifically mentioned in the Rules of Racing. The court concluded that Rule 1.11 contained proper standards for the exercise of discretion, and that it provided appellant with sufficient notice that his conduct was within its scope. Thus, there was substantial evidence in support of appellee's findings and conclusions. However, the court found that the revocation of appellant's license for five years was too severe.


OUTCOME: The court modified appellee Pennsylvania State Horse Racing Commission's order suspending appellant horse-racer's license for five years for violating the Pennsylvania Rules of Racing, and suspended appellant's license for two years. There was substantial evidence to support appellee's findings and conclusions where rule contained proper standards for the exercise of discretion and provided notice that appellant's conduct was within its scope.

Strokes v. Unemployment Compensation Board of Review


No. 624 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 584; 372 A.2d 485; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 810


January 31, 1977, Argued  
April 15, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of James Strokes, No. B-130211.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of an order from appellee Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant benefits under 43 P.S. § 752 for the reason that his unemployment did not result through no fault of his own.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Unemployment Compensation Board of Review denied appellant claimant benefits under 43 P.S. § 752 for the reason that his unemployment did not result through no fault of his own. Appellant's operator's license had been suspended because he had not satisfied a judgment obtained by a third party in an unrelated civil action. The court affirmed the order. The court found that the word "fault" as used in the Unemployment Compensation Law, 1937 Pa. Laws 2897 (as amended), was not such an indefinite and vague word as to be constitutionally defective.


OUTCOME: The order of appellee Unemployment Compensation Board of Review denying benefits to appellant claimant was affirmed. Appellant had adequate time to either pay the judgment that resulted in the suspension of his operator's license or make arrangements to settle his differences with the successful third party claimant.

 

1129 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. School Dist.


Nos. 1239 and 1246 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 453; 371 A.2d 1028; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 791


March 10, 1977, Argued  
April 4, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Secretary of Education in case of Appeal of Richard C. Baker, a Professional Employee, from a Decision of the Board of School Directors of the School District of the City of Allentown, Lehigh County, Pennsylvania, No. 279.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. School District appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged an order of the Secretary of Education (Pennsylvania) affirming his termination by appellee school district on the sole ground of immorality, after entering a plea of nolo contendere to operating an illegal gambling business in violation of 18 U.S.C.S. §§ 2, 1955. After a hearing, appellee terminated appellant's employment contract pursuant to 24 P.S. § 11-1122. Appellee's cross-appeal was consolidated for argument.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee entered a plea of nolo contendere in federal court to operating an illegal gambling business in violation of 18 U.S.C.S. §§ 2, 1955. Based solely on his plea and conviction, appellee school district terminated appellant's employment contract on the grounds of immorality and incompetency pursuant to 24 P.S. § 11-1122. On administrative review, the Secretary of Education affirmed appellant's dismissal on the ground of immorality only. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal, rejecting appellant's argument that the nolo contendere plea was inadmissible in a civil proceeding. The court held that in a proceeding intended to protect the rights of many, as distinguished from a proceeding involving individual civil rights, his nolo contendere plea was admissible as evidence of admission of guilt. The court also found substantial evidence in the record to support appellee's decision. Finally, the court held that the term "immorality" as used in 24 P.S. § 11-1122 was not unconstitutionally vague, having been judicially construed so as to foreclose the potential for abuse by a school board attempting to dismiss an employee merely for conduct incurring its disapproval.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Secretary of Education affirming appellant's dismissal pursuant to the applicable statute on the sole ground of immorality. The court held that it was not improper to consider appellant's nolo contendere plea in appellee school district's pretermination hearing. Nor was the statutory term "immorality" unconstitutionally vague as construed by the courts. The court dismissed appellee's cross-appeal as moot.

Commonwealth ex rel. Feflie v. Attorney Gen.


No. 186 Misc. Docket


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 473; 371 A.2d 555; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 786


March 7, 1977, Argued  
March 31, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Commonwealth ex rel. Leroy R. Feflie v. The Attorney General of Pennsylvania, The Director of the Bureau of Probation and Parole, The District Attorney of Northampton County, and The Keeper of the Prison.



DISPOSITION: Petitioner's motion denied. Respondents' motion granted. Judgment entered for respondents and against petitioner.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner youthful offender and respondent Pennsylvania Bureau of Probation and Parole filed motions for summary judgment in petitioner's action in mandamus, which alleged that the Youthful Offender Act, 61 P.S. §§ 481-486, violated his rights under U.S. Const. amend. V and XIV and that his rights were violated when respondent recomputed petitioner's sentence and failed to credit him with time spent on parol.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner youthful offender was convicted for the offenses of burglary, larceny, receiving stolen goods, and uttering a written instrument. Upon confinement, respondent Pennsylvania Bureau of Probation and Parole added one year to his sentence under §§ 6 and 13 of the Youthful Offender Act (Act), 61 P.S. §§ 485, 486. Petitioner was paroled after one year, but was returned to custody 11 months later due to a parole violation. Respondent reinstated petitioner's full sentence without crediting the time spent on parole. Petitioner instituted a mandamus action, and petitioner and respondent filed motions for summary judgment. The court granted respondent's motion and held that no constitutional infirmity existed in the Act. The court found that the Act's statutory scheme established uniformity as to youthful offenders. The sentencing judge was given discretion to decide whether to commit a youthful offender, but once he made the decision to do so, the maximum sentence was mandated by the Act. Thus, all persons committed as youthful offenders were treated equally insofar as the criteria to determine their sentences were employed.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment in favor of respondent Pennsylvania Bureau of Probation and Parole. The court found that the Youthful Offender Act (Act) was not unconstitutional because once a sentencing judgment exercised discretion to commit a person as a youthful offender, the maximum sentence was mandated by the Act. Thus, all youthful offenders were treated equally insofar as the criteria to determine their sentences were employed.

Commonwealth Dep't of State v. Schatzberg


No. 978 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 426; 371 A.2d 544; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 777


February 2, 1977, Argued  
March 28, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of State in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of State v. Irwin A. Schatzberg, D.C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chiropractor challenged the decision of appellee, the State Board of Chiropractic Examiners (Pennsylvania), which suspended appellant's license to practice his profession for a period of two days.


OVERVIEW: Appellant chiropractor stipulated in a test case that he administered acupuncture in violation of 49 Pa. Code § 5.3, which was issued by appellee, the State Board of Chiropractic Examiners (the board). On appeal, the court affirmed the suspension of appellant by the board. The court held that the equation of chiropractors and physicians was not yet realistic because of a real distinction between them in terms of required education, training, licensing, and scope of practice. Thus, the classification made by the legislature was constitutional and did not violate the equal protection clause. The court also discerned no public interest in requiring that chiropractors practice acupuncture, and there was evidence in the record that acupuncture could have caused immediate and serious medical problems that required the attention of a physician.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed by appellee, the State Board of Chiropractic Examiners', decision to suspend appellant chiropractor's license to practice his profession for a period of two days. The court held that chiropractors were different from physicians in terms of education, licensing, and scope of practice; thus, there was a reason to classify the differently. In addition, acupuncture could have cause immediate, serious medical problems.

Dumas v. Board of Finance & Revenue


No. 358 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 396; 371 A.2d 539; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1209


March 7, 1977, Argued  
March 25, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in case of In Re: Inell and Eddie Dumas, No. M-2691.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, social security recipients, challenged the order of appellee, Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellants' petition for refund of benefits paid to the Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare as reimbursement for previously granted public assistance.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, social security recipients, filed a petition with respondent Board of Finance and Revenue for a refund of benefits they had paid to the Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare (department) as reimbursement for previously granted public assistance. Respondent denied appellants' petition on the grounds that appellants had not proceeded within the two-year statute of limitations of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 503(a). The court reversed respondent's order. It held that the five-year statute of limitations provided by Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 503(a)(4) applied to appellants' action. The court concluded that the money was paid to the department pursuant to its interpretation that appellants had a legally enforceable obligation to do so under the Pennsylvania Support Law. It found that the department's interpretation was erroneous because 42 U.S.C.S. § 407 prohibited any state from using legal process in obtaining public assistance reimbursement out of a recipient's social security benefits.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the petition of appellants, social security recipients, for refund of benefits they had paid as reimbursement for previously granted public assistance, a five-year statute of limitations applied to appellants' action when the payments were based on a department's erroneous interpretation of the Pennsylvania Support Law.

Banks v. Unemployment Compensation Board of Review


No. 1910 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 307; 370 A.2d 1234; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 755


December 6, 1976, Argued  
March 17, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of Thomas C. Banks, No. B-128667.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of the decision of respondent, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his appeal from a referee's decision denying benefits. Respondent found that the appeal was not filed within the mandatory 10-day period from the date of the referee's decision as required by the Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Law, § 502, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 822.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, dismissed appellant claimant's appeal from a referee's decision denying him benefits, citing appellant's failure to file the appeal within the mandatory 10-day period from the date of the referee's decision provided by § 502 of the Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 822. The court affirmed respondent's order. It found that appellant had not met his burden to provide an adequate excuse for his delay. It rejected appellant's argument that the failure of the Bureau of Employment Security (bureau) to inform him of the decision, while he continued to sign up for benefits, was sufficient to find that his untimely appeal was the result of his having been misled by the bureau. It reasoned that the bureau had in no way acted affirmatively to mislead appellant as to his appeal rights and that the bureau's inaction could not be deemed to have misled him. The court rejected appellant's contention that providing for notification by means of regular mail did not satisfy due process rights. It found regular mail to be a reasonable means of providing for service of notice.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing appellant claimant's appeal from a referee's decision denying unemployment compensation benefits was affirmed, because appellant had not met his burden to provide an adequate excuse for his delay in filing his notice of appeal.

Commonwealth v. Meadville Co-operative Asso.


No. 1605 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 257; 370 A.2d 1225; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1208


February 1, 1977, Argued  
March 14, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in case of In Re: Meadville Co-operative Association, No. RST-229.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the order of appellee Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant's petition for refund of sales and use taxes it had paid in previous years.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer submitted a petition to the Bureau of Sales and Use Tax (bureau) for a refund of taxes that were paid in previous years. The bureau denied appellant's petition, and appellee Board of Finance and Revenue (board) affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed the determination of appellee, holding that appellant's petition for refund came within the scope the Tax Reform Code of 1971 (code), 72 P.S. § 7253(d) (1971), as the payments were made under an interpretation of the code that was subsequently declared erroneous by the final judgment of a court of competent jurisdiction. Thus, the five-year period of limitation proscribed in § 7253(d) was controlling. The court also held that appellant's voluntary payment of the taxes did not place him outside the scope of § 7253(d), as the area of involuntary payments was preempted by 72 P.S. § 7253(b), which imposed a six-month limitation period upon refund petitions involving tax paid pursuant to an assessment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellee Board of Finance and Revenue's decision denying appellant taxpayer a refund of sales and use taxes it paid. The court held that appellant was entitled to the five-year limitation period prescribed in the Tax Reform Code (code), as appellant paid the taxes under an interpretation of a provision of the code that was subsequently held erroneous by a final judgment of a court of competent jurisdiction.

Beers v. Mt. Pleasant Township


No. 873 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 64; 370 A.2d 807; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 745


October 29, 1976, Argued  
March 14, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued January 31, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Westmoreland County Court of Common Pleas in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Andrew Beers, No. 250 October Term, 1973.



DISPOSITION: Prior order vacated. Record remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant junkyard operator sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania) that affirmed the judgment of conviction sought and obtained by appellee township in summary proceedings before a justice of the peace. Appellee instigated the summary proceedings because appellant was operating his junkyard without a license, in violation of Mount Pleasant Township, Pa., Ordinance 35.


OVERVIEW: Appellee township filed a complaint with a justice of the peace alleging that appellant junkyard operator was conducting his operation without a license. On appeal, the trial court upheld the judgment of conviction. The trial court also found that the junkyard was located in a flood plain district; thus, its presence was prohibited by Mount Pleasant Township, Pa., Ordinance 55. Appellant was ordered to cease and desist operations. The trial judge substituted for the justice's fine of $ 100 a seven-day prison term. The trial judge later modified his order, and in lieu of imprisonment appellant was to pay a fine of $ 50 per day so long as he continued to operate a junkyard on the subject premises. On further appeal, the court reversed and remanded because neither a judgment of a sentence of imprisonment nor that of a daily fine was authorized by statute as a penalty for violation of the zoning ordinances. The court observed that under clause XXV, § 702 of the Second Class Township Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 65741, penalties for the violation of an ordinance could not exceed $ 300 and a sentenced of imprisonment could only be imposed in default of the payment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that affirmed the judgment of conviction appellee township had obtained against appellant junkyard operator, in summary proceedings before a justice of the peace. Although appellant had operated his junkyard without a license in a district where junkyard's were prohibited, the court remanded because neither imprisonment nor a daily fine was authorized by statute as a penalty for violation of the zoning ordinances.

Commonwealth v. Phoebe W. Haas Charitable Trust "A"


No. 993 C.D. 1974


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 214; 370 A.2d 406; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1207


February 2, 1977, Argued  
March 11, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue, in case of In Re: Phoebe W. Haas Charitable Trust "A," Docket No. CPIT 38, dated June 3, 1974.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a charitable trust, sought review of an order of appellee, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Board of Finance and Revenue, which denied appellant's petition for a refund of taxes it paid due to capital gains pursuant to § 301 of the Act of March 4, 1971, P.L. 6, added by the Act of August 31, 1971, P.L. 362, 72 P.S. § 7301.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a charitable trust, directed that all income be paid to charity for a period terminating 20 years after the death of the last of grantor's two sons; thereafter all income and principal, except for certain amounts required to be paid to charity, were to be paid to such persons or organizations as the grantor's two sons appointed by will. The trust received capital gains on the sale of principal assets, and incurred and paid taxes, for which it petitioned for refund. Appellee, the Board of Finance and Revenue, ruled that the capital gains were subject to taxation. On appeal, the court sustained appellee's ruling, and held that § 301 of the Act of March 4, 1971, P.L. 6, added by the Act of August 31, 1971, P.L. 362, 72 P.S. § 7301, defined a charitable trust as one operated exclusively for religious, charitable, scientific, literary, or educational purposes, and excluded from the meaning of "resident trust" all charitable trusts. The court held that appellant had both charitable and non-charitable purposes, and could not be declared at any point in time as being administered only for its charitable purposes. Therefore, the tax was proper.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the ruling of appellee, the Board of Finance and Revenue, which imposed a tax on appellant charitable trust's capital gains, because appellant had both charitable and non-charitable purposes and was therefore ineligible for the exemption from capital gains taxes allowed to charitable trusts.

McDaniel v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 609 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 190; 370 A.2d 417; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 739


February 3, 1977, Submitted on Briefs  
March 10, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of Public Welfare in case of In Re: Renee Carol McDaniel, Northumberland County Case 26023TC, dated March 5, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant student sought review of an order of appellee, Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare, which discontinued appellant's food stamps.


OVERVIEW: Appellant student's food stamps were discontinued because the total of her educational grants and Social Security benefits exceeded the income guidelines. Appellee, Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare, affirmed the decision. Appellant contended that the cost of books, meals, transportation, and supplies should have been deducted from her income and that the arbitrary distinction between food stamp recipients who received student grants and those who did not violated the equal protection clause. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that nothing in the Food Stamp Act of 1964, 7 U.S.C.S. § 2011 et seq., required that deductions include all necessary nonfood expenditures. The court held that the requirement in 7 U.S.C.S. § 2016(b) that the price of the stamps should not exceed 30 percent of the household's income assumed that 70 percent of that income could be expended on nonfood necessities. Thus, there was a built in allowance for necessary expenses beyond the specific deductions. There was no impropriety in not allowing the deductions from a general education grant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of appellee, Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare, which discontinued appellant student's food stamps. The court held that appellant did not have the right to deduct the cost of books, meals, transportation, and supplies from her grant for general education expenses.

 

1138 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Girard School Dist. v. Pittenger


No. 1475 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 176; 370 A.2d 420; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 733


December 7, 1976, Argued  
March 9, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Girard School District, et al. v. John C. Pittenger, as Secretary of Education and Chief Executive Officer of the State Board of Education, The State Board of Education, Grace M. Sloan, Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Robert P. Casey, Auditor General of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Regulations declared invalid. Enforcement enjoined.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, local school districts and taxpayers, sought declaratory and equitable relief, alleging that defendant state board of education (Pennsylvania), did not have the authority to promulgate and enforce statewide rules on student conduct.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, local school districts and taxpayers, brought suit against defendant state board of education to have regulations to establish statewide rules on student conduct declared invalid, claiming that defendant was without authority to promulgate and enforce such rules because the legislature delegated exclusive authority in the area of student conduct to local school boards. The court found in favor of plaintiffs and declared the regulations invalid for want of statutory authority. The court ruled that the legislature's grant of authority to defendant to adopt broad policies and standards governing the educational program of the commonwealth, Administrative Code, 71 P. S. 367(a), did not encompass the area of student discipline. The court held that defendant was not a "super school board" with general supervisory power over all local boards and over all aspects of the public school system but was limited in its authority to the areas enumerated by statute.


OUTCOME: The court found in favor of plaintiffs, local school districts and taxpayers, and declared invalid regulations adopted by defendant state board of education that established statewide rules of student conduct. The court held that local school boards had exclusive authority in the area of student conduct by delegation of the legislature.

Hoyman v. Commonwealth


No. 1063 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 131; 370 A.2d 753; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 725


February 4, 1977, Argued  
March 7, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Jesse G. Hoyman and Lillian Hoyman v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, acting through the Department of Environmental Resources.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Case transferred to the Board of Property.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners brought an action to quiet title against the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, acting by and through the Department of Environmental Resources.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff owners brought an action to quiet title against the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, acting by and through the Department of Environmental Resources. The commonwealth filed preliminary objections questioning the court's jurisdiction grounded upon sovereign immunity and the exclusive jurisdiction of the Board of Property (Board). Plaintiffs argued that the Board's jurisdiction was limited to cases arising from the operation of the Land Office and, alternatively, that the commonwealth court had concurrent jurisdiction over the matter. The court sustained the commonwealth's demurrer and transferred the action to the Board. The court held that its jurisdiction was barred the rule embodied in Pa. Const. art. I, § 11, that the commonwealth could not be sued without its consent. The court held that the fact that the commonwealth waived its immunity to quiet title actions before the Board could not be construed as a waiver of immunity in any other forum.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the commonwealth's preliminary objections to plaintiff owners' action to quiet title because the commonwealth did not consent to be sued and the commonwealth's waiver of its immunity before the Board of Property could not be construed as a waiver of immunity in any other forum.

D & B Auto Sales v. Commonwealth, Dep't of State, etc.


No. 1156 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 113; 370 A.2d 428; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 722


February 4, 1977, Argued  
March 4, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Board of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers, Dealers and Salesmen in case of In the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of a Motor Vehicle Dealer's License issued to D & B Auto Sales, License No. MVD 1202, dated June 3, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant used car dealer sought review of the decision by appellee, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of State, State Board of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers, Dealers and Salesmen, which suspended appellant's license for 90 days under 63 P.S. § 805(2)(x)(v), (xvi) of the Motor Vehicle Manufacturer's Dealer's and Salesmen's License Act. The act prohibited used car dealers from selling new cars. Appellant sold cars not previously titled.


OVERVIEW: Appellant used car dealer bought new automobiles from new car dealers for sale to the public. The vehicles had never been previously titled and appellant paid no Pennsylvania sales tax when it acquired the automobiles, but collected tax from its customers. Under 63 P.S. § 805(2)(xv), (xvi) of the Motor Vehicle Manufacturer's Dealer's and Salesmen's License Act (act), appellee, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of State, State Board of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers, Dealers and Salesmen (board), had the power to revoke licenses of used car dealers when they held out to the public that they sold new cars. Appellee suspended appellant's license for 90 days. Appellant's challenge was that there were not two used car dealers in appellee's 10-person board, as required by 63 P.S. § 803 of the act. However, the court affirmed appellee's adjudication because there was substantial evidence that appellant held itself out as a seller of new cars, which was prohibited by the act. The act was not invidious or without purpose because new car dealers and used car dealers served different needs of buyers and required different regulation and protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the adjudication made by appellee, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of State, State Board of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers, Dealers and Salesmen, which suspended appellant used car dealer's license for 90 days. The court found that there was substantial evidence that appellant engaged in the prohibited act of selling new cars, even though appellant was a used car dealer, in violation of the act.

 

1141 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Philadelphia v. MacDonald


Nos. 1593 C.D. 1975, 157 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


29 Pa. Commw. 102; 369 A.2d 1341; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 718


October 8, 1976, Argued  
March 2, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas in cases of City of Philadelphia v. Gordon MacDonald, No. 5695 April Term, 1975; and City of Philadelphia v. Lawrence Rock.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant workers sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee city's motion for judgment on the pleadings in appellee's action to collect unpaid city taxes under the Philadelphia Wage Tax, Philadelphia, Pa., Code § 19-1500 et seq. (1973), on wages earned by appellants.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city filed suit against appellant workers to collect taxes owed on appellants' wages under the Philadelphia Wage Tax, Philadelphia, Pa., Code § 19-1500 et seq. (1973). Appellee alleged that appellants were notified of, but failed to appeal, the tax assessment. In their answer, appellants denied knowledge of how the assessment was made and attempted to deny all other allegations by invoking their privilege under U.S. Const. amend V. The trial court granted appellee's motion for judgment on the pleadings. Appellants argued that they should be allowed to amend their answers and that because appellee's complaint contained conclusions of law, their refusal to answer could not be deemed an admission. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that whether appellants received notice of the assessments and whether they appealed those assessments were facts, and that because appellants failed to properly deny those factual allegations they were deemed to have admitted their failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The court held that because appellants never petitioned the trial court to amend their answers, the issue could not be raised on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of appellee city's motion for judgment on the pleadings, because appellant workers were deemed to have admitted that they received notice of appellee's wage tax assessment and that they did not appeal that assessment, as their invocation of their Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination did not adequately deny those allegations, and they could not request permission to amend for the first time on appeal.

Gilman v. Unemployment Compensation Board of Review


No. 1770 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


28 Pa. Commw. 630; 369 A.2d 895; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 708


December 6, 1976, Argued  
February 25, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of Janet S. Gilman, No. B-128244.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee challenged the decision of appellee Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a referee's decision disallowing unemployment compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former employee was employed by the Pennsylvania Department of Justice (DOJ) in Philadelphia until April 30, 1975, when, having given DOJ 30 days' notice, she terminated her employment to accompany her husband who was transferred to Harrisburg. Unable to find employment in Harrisburg, she applied for unemployment compensation benefits. It was undisputed that during a substantial part of the six-month period prior to leaving work or to filing a claim for benefits, appellant was not the sole or major support of her family. The Bureau of Employment Security disallowed her claim under the provisions of the Unemployment Compensation Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 802. The referee and appellee Unemployment Compensation Board of Review affirmed the determination. The court affirmed, holding that the distinction drawn by Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 802(b) found a rational basis in the underlying philosophy of the Unemployment Compensation Law, that the distinction involved no invidious discrimination, and that the section passed muster under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The classification created by § 802(b) was economic, not sex-based.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellee Unemployment Compensation Board of Review's decision, holding that the Unemployment Compensation Law provision governing disallowance of benefits was not unconstitutional as violative of the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution.

 

1143 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. J & R Equipment Rental Co.


Nos. 1248 and 1249 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


28 Pa. Commw. 558; 368 A.2d 1389; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1205


December 6, 1976, Argued  
February 10, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Board of Finance and Revenue in cases of Petition of J & R Equipment Rental Co., Inc. and Petition of Five-R Excavating, Inc., Nos. RST-880 and RST-881.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision of appellee Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which refused appellants' petitions for review on the basis that appellee lacked jurisdiction over the petitions because appellants did not filed them within the 60-day period set forth in § 232 of the Tax Reform Code of 1971, 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7234.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers filed petitions for review of the sales and use tax bureau's assessment of certain taxes. Appellants mailed their petitions within the 60-day period set forth in § 232 of the Tax Reform Code of 1971, 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7234, but the petitions were not received by appellee revenue board until the 61st day. Appellee refused appellants' petitions for review on the basis that appellee lacked jurisdiction over the petitions because appellants did not file them within 60 days as required by § 7234. On appeal, the court affirmed, noting that a previous decision of the court had held that simply mailing a petition for review within the 60-day period specified in § 7234 did not constitute filing and that actual receipt of the petition by appellee within the period was required. The court rejected appellants' argument that § 7234 unconstitutionally denied them equal protection of the law, ruling that it was not unreasonable that the act of mailing of notice was used as a guidepost for determining the start of the 60-day period. Thus, appellants failed to meet the heavy burden of overcoming the presumption of the statute's validity and constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellee revenue board's decision that it lacked jurisdiction over appellant taxpayers' petitions for review because appellants did not timely file their petitions. The court noted that this issue had been squarely decided in a previous case and rejected appellants' argument that the statute in question was unconstitutional.

 

1144 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Fluoro-Plastics, Inc.


No. 736 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


28 Pa. Commw. 520; 368 A.2d 1328; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1204


December 7, 1976, Argued  
February 9, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in case of Petition of Fluoro-Plastics, Inc., No. R-1421, dated March 31, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed. Settlement approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the order of appellee Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which refused the prayer of its petition for review of a settlement by the Department of Revenue of its corporate net income tax for the fiscal year.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer understated its corporate net income tax return by more than five percent. The Department of Revenue (department), pursuant to 72 P.S. § 3385(b) (1970), settled an additional tax at 10 percent of the amount of appellant's understatement. Appellee Board of Finance and Revenue refused the prayer of appellant's petition for review of the department's settlement. The court dismissed the appeal, holding that because the statute was designed to raise revenue, the legislature had wide discretion in classifying subject, and that absent capricious or arbitrary classification, the statute did not violate the uniformity and the equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1. The court held that there was nothing arbitrary or capricious in the different treatment of those who paid tentative tax in the amount provided and those who did not. The court also held that because there was nothing in the statute's failure to provide for amendment of tentative returns that demonstrated that the additional tax was adopted as a disguise for the exercise of a different and forbidden power, the statute did not offend due process.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant taxpayer's appeal from appellee Board of Finance and Revenue's refusal of the prayer of appellant's petition for review, and approved the Department of Revenue's settlement of appellant's corporate net income taxes. The court found that the statute did not violate the uniformity, equal protection, and due process clauses, and that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

Philadelphia v. Kenny


Nos. 409, 410, 411, 412, 413, 414, 653, 734, 735, 736, 738, 959, 960, 1239 and 1240 C.D. 1975

April 5, 1976, Argued  
February 8, 1977, Decided

Thomas, Percival, Kenny, Hazzard, Harvey, Jr., and Deckert, Nos. 424, 425, 428, 429, 430, 433 January Term, 1973; and City of Philadelphia v. George V. Schock and Jerome L. Newman, Nos. 2040 and 2045 November Term, 1973; City of Philadelphia v. James Sproles, Nos. 2245 November Term, 1973; City of Philadelphia v. Frederic Jennings, No. 2054 November Term, 1973, and City of Philadelphia v. Gloria T. Jones, No. 2042 November Term, 1973; City of Philadelphia v. George J. Cilona, No. 2146 November Term, 1973; City of Philadelphia v. Charles Cross, No. 2062 November Term, 1973; City of Philadelphia v. Arthur E. Cornell, No. 2087 November Term, 1973; and City of Philadelphia v. Meyer Goldstein, No. 2127 November Term, 1973.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant federal employees sought review of the orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted motions for summary judgment and motions on the pleadings filed by appellee City of Philadelphia in its assumpsit action against appellants to collect wage taxes and assess interest and penalties pursuant to the Wage and Net Profits Tax Ordinance, Philadelphia, Pa., Code § 19-1500 et seq. (1973).


OVERVIEW: Appellant federal employees were employed within the boundaries of appellee City of Philadelphia. None of them paid wage taxes pursuant to the Wage and Net Profits Tax Ordinance, Philadelphia, Pa., Code § 19-1500 et seq. (1973) (Code). Appellee brought an action in assumpsit to collect back taxes and to assess interest and penalties pursuant to Code § 19-508(1). The trial court granted appellee's motions for summary judgment or motions for judgment on the pleadings against each appellant. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that appellants' invocation of the U.S. Const. amend. V privilege against self-incrimination in their answer to appellee's complaint was not effective to deny appellee's allegations. The proceedings were civil in nature, not criminal or quasi-criminal, and appellants were not in apprehension of such proceedings being commenced against them. The court held that it had equity jurisdiction even though administrative remedies were not exhausted, as constitutional issues were raised. The court also held that the statute of limitations had not run, and the denials of appellants' requests for oral argument were within the discretion of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the motions for summary judgment and for judgment on the pleadings of appellee City of Philadelphia against appellant federal employees in appellee's action in assumpsit to collect back wage taxes, penalties, and interest, because appellants' invocation of their right against self-incrimination in a civil proceeding was insufficient to deny appellee's allegations.
