Gardner v. Sayre


No. 274 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


28 Pa. Commw. 130; 367 A.2d 814; 1977 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 627; 25 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 72


December 9, 1976, Argued  
January 10, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County in case of Whitney Gardner v. Borough of Sayre, No. 2 October Term, 1975.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County (Pennsylvania), which found in appellee borough's favor on appellant's declaratory judgment action to find an ordinance which required his involuntary retirement unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officer was retired involuntarily after having passed the age of 60 and having a total of 20 years of service as required by an ordinance of appellee borough. The trial court held the ordinance did not violate the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act, 43 P.S. § 951 et seq., or the federal or state constitutions. Appellant argued that the ordinance violated due process and equal protection guarantees. The court held that prior precedents bound the court to find that age in this case was not a suspect classification but a bona fide occupational qualification, specifically exempted from 43 P.S. § 955, and to reject any equal protection arguments arising from the distinction between those employees who had more than 20 years of service and those with less, who were allowed to work beyond their 60th year. Therefore, the court affirmed the trial court's holding in appellee's favor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which held for appellee borough and against appellant police officer on appellant's declaratory judgment action. The court held previous precedents bound the court to hold that appellant's age was a bona fide occupational qualification, which was specifically exempt from the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act.

 

1148 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Lutz Appellate Printers, Inc. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Property & Supplies


No. 1428 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


28 Pa. Commw. 7; 367 A.2d 374; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1277


February 4, 1976, Argued  
December 22, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in case of Lutz Appellate Printers, Inc., Plaintiff v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Property and Supplies; Ronald G. Lench, Secretary, Department of Property and Supplies; Milton J. Shapp, Governor, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Robert P. Casey, Auditor General, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; and Grace M. Sloan, State Treasurer, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Defendants.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants governor and secretary filed preliminary objections to plaintiff contractor's complaint, which sought to enjoin defendant governor from approving the award of a contract to any bidder other than plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: After plaintiff contractor, the lowest bidder, was not awarded a contract, plaintiff commenced an action in equity against defendant governor, secretary, and commonwealth, seeking to enjoin defendant governor from awarding the contract to any other contractor. Defendants filed preliminary objections. The court dismissed plaintiff's complaint, holding that plaintiff failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The court held that defendant secretary could have rejected any and all bids, even the lowest bid, and that the fact of bidding itself was consent to this reserved right. Absent fraud or collusion, the exercise of the reservation of the right to reject any or all bids was justifiable. Because plaintiff's complaint did not show fraud or collusion as the motivation for the rejection of his bid, plaintiff failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed plaintiff contractor's action seeking to enjoin defendant governor from approving the award of a contract to any bidder other than plaintiff. Because plaintiff's complaint did not show either fraud or collusion on the part of defendants governor and secretary as the motivation for the rejection of his bid, plaintiff's complaint did not state a claim upon which relief could be granted.

 

1149 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Appeal of Bethlehem


No. 170 Misc. Dkt.


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


27 Pa. Commw. 592; 367 A.2d 409; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1264; 94 L.R.R.M. 2055


October 8, 1976, Argued  
December 17, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the award of arbitrator in case of In the Matter of: Arbitration between City of Bethlehem and Local 735 of the International Association of Firefighters (AFL-CIO).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an award of an arbitrator. Appellant contended that it did not possess the legal authority to include a provision in the collective bargaining agreement requiring that all unresolved disputes be submitted to arbitration, and even if the arbitrator had jurisdiction to render his award, the award did not draw its essence from the basic agreement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city challenged an arbitrator's award between itself and appellee union. Appellant contended that it did not possess the legal authority to include a provision in the collective bargaining agreement requiring that all disputes be submitted to arbitration, and even if the arbitrator had jurisdiction to render his award, the award did not draw its essence from the basic agreement. On appeal the court held that appellant having agreed to, and participated in, the arbitration proceedings, without any suggestion that the proceedings were questionable, it could not seek to vacate the award on the ground that the proceedings were a nullity. The court also noted that the general assembly required arbitration. The court stated that the award of the arbitrator would be sustained so long as it drew its essence from the collective bargaining agreement, and that an award met this test if the interpretation could in any rational way be derived from the agreement, viewed in the light of its language, its context, and any other indicia of the parties' intention. The court affirmed the award because the award of the arbitrator was founded upon the agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award because a review of the record indicated that it was founded upon the collective bargaining agreement between appellant city and appellee union.

 

1150 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Shapp v. Sloan


No. 1194 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


27 Pa. Commw. 312; 367 A.2d 791; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1224


October 5, 1976, Argued  
December 3, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Milton J. Shapp, Governor, et al., Petitioners v. Grace M. Sloan, State Treasurer, Respondent, General Assembly of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Intervening Respondent.



DISPOSITION: Cross motions for summary judgment by respondent and intervening respondent sustained. Judgment entered in favor of State Treasurer and General Assembly. Petitioners' motions for summary judgment and application for modification of order denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross motions for summary judgment were filed by petitioners, governor and associated individuals, and respondent state treasurer and general assembly over fiscal control of federal funds allocated to state under sundry federal aid programs.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, governor and associated individuals, filed a petition for review directed against respondent state treasurer that challenged the constitutionality of legislation that related to the fiscal control of federal funds allocated to Pennsylvania under sundry federal aid programs. Respondent general assembly was granted leave to intervene. Cross motions for summary judgment were filed and the court granted summary judgment for respondents and denied petitioners' motions and dismissed their application for modification of the court's earlier order. The court held that money paid into the state treasury, whether derived from state taxation or any other source, was to be paid out of state treasury only by legislative action in the form of appropriate act or other statutory enactment. The court also found that there was no intent by congress to supersede the exercise of the power of the general assembly with respect to federal aid programs, and that the state interest demonstrated by the exercise of legislative power for the purpose of coordinating state fiscal policy with federal grants in aid could not be said to have impaired contracts in force.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of respondent state treasurer and general assembly and granted their motion for summary judgment and dismissed the cross-motion of petitioners, governor and associated individual, for summary judgment as well as their partial motion for summary judgment and their application for modification of the court's earlier order and held that money paid into the treasury was to be paid out only by legislative action.

Snelling v. Department of Transp.


No. 1231 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


27 Pa. Commw. 276; 366 A.2d 1298; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1218


September 9, 1976, Argued  
December 2, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania in case of Charles D. Snelling, Individual, and Allentown-Lehigh County Chamber of Commerce, and City of Allentown, Paul M. Burke, Individual, Nestor's Sporting Goods, Inc., and Rhoda E. Royer, Petitioners v. Department of Transportation of Pennsylvania, William H. Sherlock, Secretary of the Department of Transportation, and Lehigh Valley Associates, Respondents.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, individuals, chamber of commerce, city and store filed suit against respondents transportation department, department secretary and developer in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania to challenge the issuance of highway occupancy permits. Petitioners filed an amended petition for review to which respondents filed preliminary objections. The court had original jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, individuals, chamber of commerce, city and store filed a suit against respondents, transportation department, department secretary and developer, challenging respondent transportation department's issuance of highway occupancy permits to respondent developer. Petitioners filed an amended petition for review and respondents filed preliminary objections. The court held that none of petitioners had standing to sue. Municipalities did not have standing, and the other petitioners were not aggrieved, as they did not have a direct substantial interest. The court held that under 71 P.S. § 512(b) respondent transportation department was not obligated to conduct hearings on the widening of a highway and the creation of access to a shopping center. Respondent developer was obligated to buy the necessary land. The court held that sovereign immunity alone would preclude the suit because it sought to compel respondent secretary to revoke the permits. The court held that the environmental impact of the widened highway and development of access roads did not violate Pa. Const. art. I, § 27. The court dismissed petitioners' claims and sustained respondents' preliminary objections.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the preliminary objections filed by respondents transportation department, department secretary and developer because petitioners, individuals, chamber of commerce, city and store lacked standing to bring the suit. The court also held the suit was precluded by sovereign immunity because it sought to compel respondent secretary to engage in an action, to revoke the highway occupancy permits.

 

1152 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Forrest C. Gearhart, Inc. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Revenue, Bureau of Sales & Use Tax


No. 199 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


27 Pa. Commw. 70; 365 A.2d 908; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 769


September 9, 1976, Argued  
November 15, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania in case of Forrest C. Gearhart, Inc. v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Revenue, Bureau of Sales & Use Tax, and Vincent X. Yakowicz, Secretary of the Department of Revenue, for the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed for declaratory judgment in a tax case. Respondent tax bureau filed preliminary objections which argued that petitioner had not exhausted its statutory remedy and thus declaratory judgment was not a proper remedy and the court lacked jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Respondent tax bureau changed the procedure by which plaintiff corporation was to remit retail taxes. Plaintiff, incorrectly assuming that respondent exceeded its statutory authority failed to comply with the change. Subsequently, plaintiff filed a declaratory judgment action. Respondent challenged the filing and filed preliminary objections arguing that plaintiff had not exhausted its statutory remedy and therefore the court lacked jurisdiction. The court affirmed respondent's preliminary objections and dismissed the petition. The court held that if a remedy was specially provided by statute, it must be pursued. The court concluded that plaintiff had not exhausted the statutory remedies and thus the court lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court sustained respondent tax bureau's preliminary objections and dismissed plaintiff corporation's petition. The court held that plaintiff had not exhausted its statutory remedy specifically designed for tax cases, and thus, the court did not have jurisdiction.

 

1153 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


In re Quaker City Development Co.


No. 1845 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


27 Pa. Commw. 13; 365 A.2d 683; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 733


October 4, 1976, Submitted on Briefs  
October 25, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in case of In the Matter of Revocation of Hotel Liquor License No. H-4868, Amusement Permit No. AP-21216 and Sunday Sales Permit No. SS-158, issued to -- Quaker City Development Co., Inc., Penrose Avenue & Penrose Ferry Road, Philadelphia, Pa., No. 2116 October Term, 1975.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) affirming the Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board's revocation of its hotel liquor license. Appellant argued that 47 P.S. § 4-471's "upon any other sufficient cause shown" was unconstitutionally vague, indefinite, and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, holder of a hotel liquor license, leased its facilities to a charitable organization that conducted a casino night with gambling. Because appellant's liquor license had been suspended, the charitable organization provided and sold the liquor on those evenings. After a hearing, the Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board revoked appellant's license because it permitted the sale of liquor on its premises and permitted gambling. Appellant sought review after the court of common pleas affirmed the revocation. Affirming the decision, the court explained that either finding supported the revocation because a licensee could not have permitted liquor to have been sold on the premises during a suspension and permitting gambling on the premises was a violation of criminal law regardless of any charitable purpose or lack of prosecution. Rejecting appellant's argument that the "upon any other sufficient cause shown" provision of 47 P.S. § 4-471 was unconstitutionally vague, the court explained that a proceeding to revoke a license under the liquor laws had always been considered civil and administrative, and the provision was proper to accomplish the remedial purposes of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the court of common pleas upholding the Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board's revocation of appellant's hotel liquor license; the license could have been revoked for allowing liquor to have been served while the license was suspended or for permitting gambling; the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1154 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Red Cheek, Inc. v. Supervisor of Ruscombmanor


Nos. 382 and 383 C.D. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


26 Pa. Commw. 530; 364 A.2d 542; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1337


September 14, 1976, Argued  
October 12, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County in cases of Red Cheek, Inc. v. Supervisors of the Township of Ruscombmanor, No. 283 October Term, 1975; and Red Cheek, Inc. v. Supervisors of Richmond Township, No. 284 October Term, 1975.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fruit company challenged orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County (Pennsylvania) denying curative amendments to respondents', supervisors of neighboring townships, ordinances where appellant sought to construct a fruit waste facility in residential zones of respondents.


OVERVIEW: Appellant fruit company pretreated fruit waste from its operations in a primary treatment system located on its property in one Pennsylvania borough. The wastes then flowed into the borough's activated sludge plant and other sewage facilities in a manner which did not comply with environmental legislation and the state environmental department. To remedy the situation, appellant's engineers proposed construction of a fruit waste disposal system in two neighboring townships that would pump the waste to lagoons. Appellant sought a curative amendment to each county's zoning ordinances because the 26-acre site proposed for the treatment operation was located in residentially zoned districts. Respondents, supervisors of neighboring townships, denied appellant's request. The lower court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that appellant's use was accessory, and neither township imposed a total exclusion on the proposed use as an accessory use. The court affirmed each township's zoning ordinances as constitutional, permitting in their industrial zones everything appellant proposed doing in respondents' residential districts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of appellant fruit company's request for a curative amendment to respondents', supervisors of neighboring townships, zoning ordinances; each township's ordinance permitted the use sought by appellant but restricted it to industrial zones.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) that dismissed his appeal from appellee commonwealth's revocation of his driver's license for one year under the Pennsylvania Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 616(a)(4), because of drug violations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver's motor vehicle operating privileges were revoked by appellee commonwealth for one year pursuant to the Pennsylvania Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Cons. Stat. § 780-113(a)(30). When his appeal from the revocation was dismissed by the lower court, appellant sought review. The court found that the evidence, including appellant's own testimony, demonstrated that appellant had utilized a motor vehicle in the unlawful transportation of a controlled substance. Further, the statute used to justify revocation was constitutional where there was no equal protection violation inherent in the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, holding that appellant had clearly used his vehicle to transport a controlled substance illegally when he sold drugs to undercover officers in his car; further, there was no constitutional issue preventing application of the relevant statute.

Commonwealth v. Di Marco

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania

October 6, 1976, Decided

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant liquor control board and appellee bar owner each sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County (Pennsylvania), which modified appellant's order by reducing a fine imposed on appellee.


OVERVIEW: Both appellant liquor control board and appellee bar owner sought review of the order of the trial court which modified appellant's order by reducing a fine imposed by appellant against appellee from $ 1000 to $ 500. Appellant claimed the trial court capriciously ignored its evidence, and appellee claimed that § 493(10) of the Liquor Code, 47 P.S. § 4-493(10), was unconstitutional for vagueness. The court affirmed because the trial court had the power to reduce the penalty and it was not an abuse of discretion to exercise that power. The words "lewd, immoral and improper" were not unconstitutionally vague or indefinite. The court also noted that no one had a constitutional right to engage in the business of selling alcoholic beverages and that actions against licensees violating the Liquor Code were civil and administrative proceedings and not criminal in nature.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court which fined appellee bar owner $ 500 was affirmed because the court had the discretion to reduce the fine and because the words "lewd, immoral and improper" were not unconstitutionally vague or indefinite.

Commonwealth by Creamer v. Monumental Properties, Inc.

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


26 Pa. Commw. 399; 365 A.2d 442; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1312


March 1, 1976, Argued  
September 20, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Modification or, in the Alternative, Reargument, Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original jurisdiction in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, by J. Shane Creamer, Attorney General, Plaintiff v. Monumental Properties, Inc., Capital Housing Corporation, Executive House, Inc., Property Management, Inc., Samuel Elgart, Inc., Frank Stein, Albert Kaytes, Harry B. Davis, Donald Yost Real Estate Company, Miller Bros. & Company, William B. Hollinger & Son, Benjamin Volk, Marks & Company, Devon-Strafford Company, C. Pat Riley, Robert E. Plank, Griest Realty Company, Media Real Estate Company, Lori Incorporated, J.J. Gumburg Company, Washington Plaza, Inc., Penndale Towers, Inc., Saniel-Elkind Real Estate Co., Spiro Realty Company, Talenfeld Real Estate Co., John C. Clark Company, Yeo & Lukens Company, G.S. Rockey Company, and P.O. Naly Company.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand by the Pennsylvania Supreme Court, the court reviewed defendant landlords' and form sellers' preliminary objections to plaintiff commonwealth's complaint for injunctive relief from defendants' use of form leases, alleged to be in violation of the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law, 73 P.S. § 201-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The court reviewed defendant landlords' and form sellers' preliminary objections to plaintiff commonwealth's complaint for injunctive relief from their use of form leases, alleging violations of the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law (Act),73 P.S. § 201-1 et seq. The matter came before the court on remand of the Pennsylvania Supreme Court. The court overruled defendants' procedural preliminary objections and those relating to plaintiff's remedy at law because defendants abandoned them. As to their objections on whether plaintiff stated a cause of action, the court concluded that to comply with the supreme court's opinion in Monumental II a record had to be established from which it could make findings of fact and conclusions of law to determine whether the failure to notify a tenant was misleading and whether use of certain language in a form lease violated the Act. The court permitted plaintiff to amend its complaint which was confusing and lacked specificity.


OUTCOME: In plaintiff's suit for relief from defendants' use of form leases, the court granted plaintiff's motions to compel production, and for leave to discontinue, but denied leave for discovery. The court overruled defendants' abandoned preliminary objections for procedural questions and on adequacy of remedy, but sustained the rest to the extent the complaint lacked specificity. Defendant form sellers' complaint was dismissed.

County of Washington v. Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board


Nos. 8 Tr. Dkt. 1975, 17 Tr. Dkt. 1975, 35 Tr. Dkt. 1975, 8 Tr. Dkt. 1976, 9 Tr. Dkt. 1976


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


26 Pa. Commw. 315; 364 A.2d 519; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1226


June 8, 1976, Argued  
September 10, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board in the cases of In the Matter of the Employees of Washington County, PERA-R-2209-W; In the Matter of the Employees of Allegheny County, PERA-R-2104-W and PERA-R-2311-W; In the Matter of the Employees of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, PERA-R-5403-E; In the Matter of the Employees of Bucks County, PERA-R-6852-E, PERA-R-6853-E, PERA-R-6854-E and PERA-R-6855-E; In the Matter of the Employees of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, PERA-R-7138-E and PERA-7194-E; and appeals Nos. 23 Tr. Dkt. 1973 and 24 Tr. Dkt. 1973, in cases of Roger M. Fischer, Register of Wills and Clerk of the Orphans' Court Division of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Pennsylvania, Plaintiff v. Louis Rzymek, William O. Hill, Jr. and Leo P. Weir, Commissioners for the County of Erie, Pennsylvania, and American Federation of State, County and Municipal Employees, AFL-CIO, Defendants, Pennsylvania State Association of County Commissioners, Intervening Party Defendant; and Robert H. Chase, District Attorney, Erie County, Pennsylvania, Plaintiff v. Louis Rzymek, William O. Hill, Jr. and Leo P. Weir, Commissioners for [***2] the County of Erie, Pennsylvania, and American Federation of State, County and Municipal Employees, AFL-CIO, Defendants, Pennsylvania State Association of County Commissioners, Intervening Party Defendant.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part. Complaints in equity dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county employees challenged final orders of the Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board, which vacated a prior certification of a bargaining unit comprised of directly related court employees and of employees of certain county row offices for want of proper identity of the public employer of the sought for bargaining units.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner county employees challenged final orders of the Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board (PLRB), which vacated a prior certification of a bargaining unit comprised of directly related court employees and of employees of other county offices for want of proper identity of the public employer of the proposed bargaining units. The court maintained that the board of judges was empowered by statute and by the needs of judicial administration to select or discharge employees; however, the board did not enjoy exclusive control over wages and benefits. As such, the court concluded that judges enjoyed joint employer status with county commissioners for purposes of collective bargaining pursuant to the Public Employee Relations Act (Act 195). The court held that Act 195 was not an unconstitutional intrusion upon an independent judiciary as judicial review was afforded to persons challenging actions of the PLRB. Accordingly the orders were affirmed as to denial of the certifications and reversed as to the board's conclusion of law that the board of judges held sole public employer status of directly related court employees.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed as to denial of the certifications because members of proposed bargaining unit were employees of different public employers. The orders reversed as to the board's conclusion of law that the board of judges held sole public employer status of directly related court employees as judges did not enjoy exclusive control over employee wages and benefits.

Commonwealth, Ins. Dep't v. Pennsylvania Coal Mining Asso.


No. 1180 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


26 Pa. Commw. 348; 363 A.2d 823; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1195


March 1, 1976, Argued  
September 10, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Insurance Commissioner, dated July 22, 1975, in case of Coal Mine Compensation Rating Bureau of Pennsylvania, Occupational Disease Rate Filing of September 30, 1974, Docket No. R74-10-5.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a coal mining association and coal mine operators, challenged the order of the Insurance Commissioner setting occupational disease rates for mine workers pursuant to the Federal Black Lung Benefits Act, 30 U.S.C.S. § 901 et seq., and the Pennsylvania Workers' Compensation Act, 77 Pa. Con. Stat. §§ 27.1(q), 412.


OVERVIEW: The Insurance Commissioner (commissioner) approved rates for coal mine occupational disease insurance for the second year under an expanded program. Appellants, an intervenor association and coal mining companies, challenged the rate structure. The court, recognizing the commissioner's discretion in setting rates, reviewed the applicable law, and the complexity of insurance rate making, in light of the new statutory coverage. The commissioner had adopted rates, based on a proposed rate filing submitted by an actuarial firm to appellee rating bureau, after several elements were revised. The court found no showing that the actuarial firm was not equitable and impartial, or that the personnel of the firm were not qualified to prepare the rate filing. The use of data from other states was appropriate due to the absence of data under the new program. However, the court found a lack of substantial evidence to support the presumed shift in the ratio of state to federal claims in computing rates for surface and deep mine operators; thus, no deference had to be given to commissioner's findings on this issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part the order of the Insurance Commissioner and remanded the matter to take additional evidence of the propriety of the assumed state to federal claim ratio and the resulting rate structure for deep and surface mine operators. All other assumptions in setting the rates were affirmed.

Appeal of Green & White Copter, Inc.


No. 1574 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


25 Pa. Commw. 445; 360 A.2d 283; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1100


April 7, 1976, Argued  
July 12, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County in case of In Re: Appeal of Green & White Copter, Inc., from the Denial of its Curative Amendment Request by the Board of Commissioners of Radnor Township, No. 5553 of 1974.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an order of appellee zoning commission that denied appellant's application to amend a zoning ordinance to provide for private use heliports in residential districts.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner sought review of an order of the trial court that upheld a decision of appellee zoning commission, which denied appellant's application to amend a zoning ordinance to provide for private use heliports in residential districts. The court stated that some total exclusion of land uses did not shift the burden of proof to the municipality to justify the exclusion. Heliports, particularly in residential areas, embodied a land use, the total exclusion of which appeared prima facie to be designed to protect the public interest. The prohibition of heliports also related to police power goals. Thus, the zoning ordinance retained its presumption of validity, which appellant failed to overcome. Accordingly, the court affirmed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied appellant property owner's curative amendment to the township zoning ordinance to provide for private use heliports in residential districts in view of the presumed validity of the zoning ordinance. The court found that the total exclusion of heliports as a land use did not shift the burden of proof to the municipality to justify the exclusion.

Commonwealth, Human Relations Com. v. Thorp, Reed & Armstrong


No. 862 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


25 Pa. Commw. 295; 361 A.2d 497; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1170; 16 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1352; 12 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P11,058


October 29, 1975, Argued  
June 24, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission in case of Marcella Phelps Hanson v. Thorp, Reed & Armstrong, Docket No. E-8538.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed from an order of the Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission, which found that defendant had unlawfully retaliated against plaintiff employee upon learning that plaintiff employee had filed an administrative complaint against defendant employer based on age and sex discrimination.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a complaint of discrimination against her law firm employer based on sex and age pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 955(a). After learning of the administrative complaint, defendant law firm placed plaintiff on indeterminate leave of absence with pay. Defendant also took steps to reassign cases being handled by plaintiff and otherwise disassociated her from the firm. Plaintiff then filed a second complaint of discrimination based on retaliatory conduct prohibited by Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 955(d). The Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission (commission) acted on the second complaint and entered an order directing defendant law firm to restore plaintiff to the position she occupied before being placed on leave. Defendant law firm appealed and the court affirmed. The court noted that its review was limited to a determination of whether the factual findings were supported by substantial evidence, whether the adjudication was made in accordance with the law, and whether there was an abuse of discretion in the relief awarded. The court noted that the facts were largely undisputed and that defendant did not challenge the factual findings of the commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings of the commission that defendant law firm had unlawfully retaliated against plaintiff based on filing of an administrative complaint of discrimination. The court modified the order of relief to direct that defendant not be required to assign any case to plaintiff where it reasonably believed a potential conflict affecting the interest of the client would exist.

Appeal of Quaker City Development Co.


No. 1022 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


25 Pa. Commw. 190; 359 A.2d 835; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1077


April 9, 1976, Argued  
June 16, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in case of In the Matter of Revocation of Hotel Liquor License No. H-4868, Amusement Permit No. AP-21216, and Sunday Sales Permit No. SS-158, issued to Quaker City Development Co., Inc., No. 75-02-2078.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant liquor licensee sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the order of the Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board (Board) that suspended appellant's hotel liquor license for five days for permitting gambling on the licensed premises.


OVERVIEW: Appellant liquor licensee leased its premises to a church group that conducted a bingo game, the proceeds of which were to benefit the church. The liquor control board (board) suspended appellant's hotel liquor license for five days. Appellant sought review of the order that suspended appellant's hotel liquor license for permitting gambling on the licensed premises. The court affirmed the order and held that the record indicated that there was sufficient evidence to support the finding that appellant permitted gambling upon its licensed premises. The court determined that there was only required to be a preponderance of the evidence of violation of the criminal law, and not an arrest or conviction under the Crimes Code. Appellant also contended that 47 P.S. § 4-471, the provision that allowed suspension upon any other sufficient cause shown, was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that 47 P.S. § 4-471 provided an adequate standard upon which the board could have based its discretion and upon which licensees could rely in conducting their licensed activities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that suspended appellant liquor licensee's hotel liquor license for five days for permitting gambling on the licensed premises. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to support the finding that appellant permitted gambling upon its licensed premises. Only a preponderance of the evidence of violation of the criminal law was necessary.

Dakoski v. Urda


No. 1759 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


25 Pa. Commw. 77; 358 A.2d 438; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1058


April 8, 1976, Argued  
June 7, 1976, Decided

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Susquehanna County (Pennsylvania), which determined that appellant was liable for unpaid earned income tax.


OVERVIEW: A school district adopted an earned income tax resolution which levied an annual tax for general revenue purposes of one-half of one percent on all salaries, wages, commissions, and other compensation earned or received by residents of the school district. Appellant resident refused, on request of appellee tax collector, to pay the applicable earned income tax. Appellee filed a suit against appellant for collection of the claimed tax and obtained a judgment against appellant together with interest and costs. Appellant challenged the decision of the trial court because he alleged that the earned income tax was unconstitutional because his wages were taxed by the Federal Government, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and the regional school district and that the state had pre-empted this field of taxation. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court because the court held that the area was not preempted, and appellant's claim that it was unconstitutional for more than one governing body to tax his wages was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court which entered a judgment in favor of appellee tax collector because the court held that the tax was valid; the area was not pre-empted by state law nor was it unconstitutional for appellant resident's wages to be taxed by more than one governing body.

Commonwealth Dep't of Environmental Resources v. Delenick


No. 1565 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


24 Pa. Commw. 577; 357 A.2d 736; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1041


March 3, 1976, Submitted on Briefs  
May 21, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Environmental Hearing Board of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania in case of In the Matter of: Joseph C. Delenick, d/b/a St. Clair Sanitary Landfill v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources, Docket No. 75-066-D.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of the order of the Environmental Hearing Board (Pennsylvania), which required him to cease operation of his landfill and follow certain termination procedures for lack of a landfill permit as stipulated by § 7(a) of the Pennsylvania Solid Waste Management Act, 35 P.S. Ann. § 6007(a). Appellant argued that the statute unconstitutionally infringed his rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowner operated a landfill, starting before the enactment of the Pennsylvania Solid Waste Management Act, 35 P.S. § 6007(a). Appellee agency ordered him to cease such operation without a permit and to comply with closure procedures. The order was sustained by the agency hearing board. Appellant sought review, arguing that appellee's action pursuant to the statute was an unconstitutional infringement of his property rights. The court affirmed and ruled that one who challenged the constitutionality of a statute was faced with its presumptive constitutionality, that all doubt was resolved in favor of sustaining legislation, and that, given that the statute was enacted pursuant to the police power, appellant's property rights were subordinated to its proper and lawful exercise. The court found that appellant offered no evidence whatsoever that the statutory permit requirements were unduly oppressive or burdensome, nor did he offer any evidence that the operative statutory provisions constituted an unreasonable exercise of the police power on its face or as applied to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the agency hearing board decision affirming an order requiring appellant landowner to cease operation of a landfill and comply with closure procedures. The court ruled that appellant offered no evidence that the statutory requirements were unduly oppressive or burdensome or that the operative statutory provisions constituted an unreasonable exercise of the police power on its face or as applied to him.

Clearview Land Development Co. v. Kassab


No. 889 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


24 Pa. Commw. 532; 357 A.2d 732; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1040


February 4, 1976, Argued  
May 19, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Clearview Land Development Co., Inc. and Roma Associates, Inc. v. Jacob G. Kassab, Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation, and the Redevelopment Authority of the City of Philadelphia and the City of Philadelphia, and the City of Philadelphia, Department of Public Property.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections of Secretary of Transportation sustained and complaint dismissed as to that defendant. Case transferred to the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners filed a complaint in equity seeking damages from defendants, the state transportation secretary, city redevelopment authority, and city, based upon defendants' proposed taking of plaintiffs' property to widen a public street.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowners challenged an eminent domain action and sought equitable relief against defendants, the state transportation secretary, city redevelopment authority, and city, for a taking for the purpose of widening a public street. Plaintiffs argued that the street improvement project would substantially impair plaintiffs' ingress and egress to their property. Plaintiffs sought damages. Upon exercising its original jurisdiction, the court held that plaintiffs were not entitled to money damages from defendant secretary of state or an order compelling defendant secretary to file a declaration of taking because that defendant was shielded by the doctrine of sovereign immunity for affirmative acts performed within his scope of office. Defendant secretary was imbued with legislative authority to improve public streets. The remaining defendants, who were not state actors, were outside the court's original jurisdiction. The court dismissed plaintiffs' claims against defendant secretary of state and transferred the remaining claims to the appropriate court of common pleas.


OUTCOME: The court exercised its original jurisdiction and held that defendant secretary of state was immune from plaintiff landowners' suit in equity and therefore could not be ordered to pay damages or file a declaration of taking. The court transferred plaintiffs' suit against the remaining defendants, the city redevelopment authority and city, to another court of common pleas because the court lacked jurisdiction over those defendants.

Hanek v. Clairton


Nos. 1051 C.D. 1974, 221 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


24 Pa. Commw. 69; 354 A.2d 35; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 940


October 28, 1975, Argued  
March 16, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in cases of Frank Hanek v. The Cities of Clairton, et al., No. 2503 January Term, 1974; and Benjamin Lustman, individually and as representative of Members of a Class, Plaintiffs v. City of Pittsburgh, Intervenor v. West Mifflin Borough, a Municipal Corporation, and Joseph W. Schieck, Tax Collector of West Mifflin Borough, No. 1239 October Term, 1973.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed in 1051 C.D. 1974. Order reversed in 221 C.D. 1975.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual taxpayer from one action and appellee borough from a second action challenged the orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), in a dispute surrounding the alleged double taxation of appellants, individual taxpayer from one action and a class of taxpayers from a second action, by appellees, township, borough, and local taxing authorities.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, individual taxpayer from one action and a class of taxpayers from a second action, sued to challenge a new income tax. As a result of the elimination of the city tax, appellees, township, borough, and local taxing authorities, removed the credit against appellants' local tax liabilities, resulting in no reduction of appellants' tax liability. Appellee borough challenged the lower court's application of the Enabling Act, 53 P.S. § 6902(5), which automatically halved the tax rates, and appellant individual taxpayer challenged the lower court's dismissal of his action. The court held that the appellant individual taxpayer's attempt to seek a credit pursuant to 53 P.S. § 6914 was without merit. The court held that the lower court erred in holding that the automatic reduction of the tax rates, designed to lessen the tax burden on residents of the Borough and School District, also inured to the benefit of nonresidents even though no duplication of taxes existed as to them. The court affirmed the judgement in favor of appellees, township, borough, and local taxing authorities, and reversed the decision in favor of appellant individual taxpayer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the second judgement in favor of appellees, township, borough, and local taxing authorities, as the taxes imposed were constitutionally and statutorily valid. The court reversed the first decision of the trial court which applied an automatic halving of the imposed tax in favor of appellant individual taxpayer.

Commonwealth, Farview State Hospital v. Urda


No. 1318 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


23 Pa. Commw. 607; 353 A.2d 61; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 894


February 3, 1976, Argued  
March 9, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Civil Service Commission in case of Nicholas A. Urda v. Farview State Hospital, No. 1657.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged the order of the State Civil Service Commission (Pennsylvania), which upheld his removal from a position in the classified civil service with appellee state hospital based on appellant's violation of the rule that prohibited civil servants from engaging in certain political activities.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee had a classified civil service position as a psychiatric security aide at appellee state hospital. While employed in this capacity, appellant participated in his personal campaign for the office of district judge. Appellee Civil Service Commission affirmed appellant's dismissal from his position due to his participation in political activities in violation of the Civil Service Act § 904, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 741.904. On appeal, appellant asserted that the prohibition against active participation in political campaigns by civil service workers violated his rights to free speech under the federal and state constitutions. The court replied that the United States Supreme Court rejected the same argument against a similar statute. Next, the court found no merit in appellant's argument that the prohibition was unconstitutional discrimination. Finally, the court did not find the statute to be void for vagueness. The court affirmed appellee commission's decision and dismissed appellant's appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that upheld appellant employee's dismissal for his civil service employment based on his violation of the prohibition against certain campaign activities. The court rejected appellant's challenges to the constitutionality of the prohibition.

Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board v. Bethlehem Mines Corp.


No. 1161 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


23 Pa. Commw. 517; 353 A.2d 79; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 900


February 2, 1976, Argued  
March 2, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board in case of John Rastoka v. Bethlehem Mines Corporation and Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, No. A-70009.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review from an order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania), which granted a doctor's deposition fee to appellee employee in appellee's claim to recover for occupational injuries.


OVERVIEW: In appellee's workmen's compensation claim to recover for occupational injuries, appellant objected to the award of appellee's doctor's deposition fee under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 77, § 996. The reviewing court found that the award of the fee was proper. The statute was not unconstitutional because it had the legitimate goal of deterring unreasonable contests of workmen's claims and to ensure that claimants successful in litigation of their claims should receive compensation undiminished by the costs of litigation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

1169 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Barnes & Tucker Co.


No. 896-A Tr. Dkt. 1970


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


23 Pa. Commw. 496; 353 A.2d 471; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 907; 6 ELR 20466


September 10, 1975, Argued  
March 2, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Barnes & Tucker Company.



DISPOSITION: Injunction issued. Abatement procedures ordered implemented. Money judgment entered in favor of plaintiff.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pennsylvania Supreme Court reversed and remanded an action for nuisance against defendant mine owner.


OVERVIEW: A cause of action for nuisance against defendant mine owner was remanded for further proceedings by the state supreme court. In its opinion on remand the supreme court held that the discharge of acid mine drainage from defendant's mine into the waters of plaintiff commonwealth constituted a public nuisance at common law as well as under the applicable statutory law, and that relief could be granted under either theory. The absence of facts supporting concepts of negligence, foreseeability, or unlawful conduct was not fatal to a finding that a common law nuisance existed. And the doctrine of laches, waiver, or estoppel as against the plaintiff were not available to defendant nor could those who pollute streams acquire prescriptive or property rights to so pollute as against the commonwealth. The trial court found that instituting a clean up requirement of defendant as an exercise of police power was the only abatement available and that it did not constitute a taking of defendant's property without just compensation, nor was it outside of reasonable parameters. Therefore, defendant was ordered to institute a cleanup process of the acid mine drainage.


OUTCOME: The trial court issued an injunction against defendant mine owner, ordering the abatement of a nuisance caused by the discharge of acid mine drainage. The requirement that defendant implement a costly cleanup process as abatement did not constitute a taking.

 

1170 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Wolfe v. Beal


No. 1163 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


23 Pa. Commw. 475; 353 A.2d 481; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 908


February 2, 1976, Argued  
March 1, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Debra Bartholomew Wolfe v. Frank Beal, Secretary of Public Welfare of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Dr. Robert Gatski, Superintendent of Danville State Hospital.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former mental hospital patient sought an order compelling respondents Secretary of Public Welfare and superintendent of state hospital to destroy all records of said state hospital pertaining to petitioner's confinement at said hospital, after a prior finding that petitioner's confinement order had been void for lack of due process.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner former mental hospital patient had previously been committed to a state hospital. That commitment order was subsequently declared null and void for a lack of due process. Petitioner then asked the court in this action to order respondents Secretary of Public Welfare and the Superintendent of state hospital to destroy all records at state hospital that pertained to petitioner's confinement. The court denied the petition. The court held that 50 P.S. § 4602(a) mandated that the state hospital maintain such records, that there was no legislative mandate to destroy such records, and the court was therefore without power to order respondents to destroy them.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner former mental patient's petition to have her state hospital records destroyed. The court held that the state hospital had a legislative mandate to maintain such records, and there was no authority for their destruction.

 

1171 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Costopoulos v. Zoning Board of Adjustment


No. 504 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


23 Pa. Commw. 159; 351 A.2d 318; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 855; 80 A.L.R.3d 675


December 3, 1975, Argued  
February 2, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County in case of Costos C. Costopoulos, James C. Costopoulos, Thomas Costopoulos, E. L. Wiser, Frank P. Shaner, Clyde C. Millner, Richard C. Johnson, Anthony Butto, Charles Kollas, Athanasios Katsaounis, Samuel A. Miller, Melvin L. Line, Paul Cline, Sheila O. Clark, George W. Adams, Loyal Foust & Richard Zammito v. Zoning Board of Adjustment & The Borough of Carlisle, No. 2 January Term, 1974.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant merchants challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania), which found that an ordinance enacted by appellee borough, which prohibited the erection or maintenance of projecting signs over public areas and mandated the removal of like existing signs at the expense of the owner, was valid.


OVERVIEW: Appellee borough enacted an ordinance which prohibited the erection or maintenance of projecting signs over public areas and mandated the removal of like existing signs at the expense of the owner. Appellants merchants commenced suit, and the trial court issued an order staying enforcement of the ordinance pending a final determination of the case on its merits, but later ruled the contested ordinance valid. On appeal, appellants introduced evidence showing that there previously erected signs met the existing law at the time they were erected, that the signs were expensive, would be of greater expense to reproduce, and that it would cost hundreds of dollars to remove them. Appellees controverted by attempting to prove that the ordinance would eliminate hazards to motorists and pedestrians, facilitate firefighting, escalate real estate values, and would be aesthetic to the community. The court affirmed the lower court's decision finding that the ordinance was a regulation rather than a zoning law, that it regulated public rather than private property and was within appellee's authority.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed because appellant merchants cited cases pertaining to zoning ordinances, but the ordinance before the court regulated public rather than private property. Further, the court found that the ban was not a total ban on signs and was within appellee borough's authority to enact and enforce.

 

1172 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Shapp


No. 740 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


23 Pa. Commw. 153; 350 A.2d 464; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 823


January 5, 1976, Argued  
January 30, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Richard Robinson, individually and on behalf of all persons similarly situated, v. Milton J. Shapp, individually and as Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, individually and on behalf of all those similarly situated, filed a complaint in equity to set aside and to bar defendant Governor of Pennsylvania from enforcing an executive order stating executive branch policy with respect to discrimination based on sexual preference.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, individually on behalf of all persons similarly situated, invoked the court's equity jurisdiction by filing a complaint seeking injunctive relief setting aside, and barring the Governor of Pennsylvania from enforcing, an executive order which committed the executive branch to work towards ending discrimination based on affectional or sexual preferences. The court sustained defendant's preliminary objection going to justiciability, and dismissed the complaint. The court held that it lacked jurisdiction to adjudicate the propriety of an executive order which was a broad statement of public or political policy and thus within the sole discretion of the Governor; and because the doctrines of separation of powers, executive sovereignty and comity with the coordinate branches of government precluded the court from exercising its jurisdiction to inquire into the propriety of a discretionary decision of the executive branch of government.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed plaintiff's complaint seeking to enjoin enforcement of an executive order promulgated by defendant Governor of Pennsylvania. The separation of powers doctrine deprived the court of jurisdiction to inquire into, much less bar defendant from enforcing, an executive order proclaiming the policy of his administration, which was a governmental function within defendant's sole discretion.

 

1173 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth, Board of Funeral Directors v. L. Beinhauer & Son Co.


No. 696 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


23 Pa. Commw. 106; 350 A.2d 453; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 819


October 31, 1975, Argued  
January 27, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Board of Funeral Directors in case of In Re: L. Beinhauer & Son Company, dated April 16, 1975.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a decision of the State Board of Funeral Directors (Pennsylvania) that rejected appellant's application for two branch office licenses for undertaking.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation filed an application for two branch office licenses for the purpose of undertaking in the state. The application for the two branch offices was denied. When appellant received its initial license, it maintained funeral homes at three separate locations in the city. One office was subsequently moved before it closed down. Thereafter, a law was passed stating that no branch licenses would be granted to any corporation. One of the two remaining locations of the corporation was used for funerals for several years and then closed. The last location was destroyed by fire, but had been rebuilt and remained the sole place of business before being sold. Upon review, appellant asserted that its prior operation of three locations entitled it to operate three locations pursuant to a grandfather clause in the new law. The court held that a landowner's right to a nonconforming use may be forfeited upon his abandonment of that use. As appellant had discontinued funeral operations and failed to conduct branch office activities since then, it lost any rights under the grandfather clause. The decision of the state board of funeral directors was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of appellee state board of funeral directors in denying appellant corporation's application for two branch office licenses for undertaking because even though appellant had previously maintained three branch offices prior to a new law refusing licensing to corporations, appellant had abandoned undertaking and lost any rights under a grandfather clause when it failed to conduct activities for several years.

 

1174 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Redevelopment Authority of Nanticoke v. Spencer


No. 634 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


23 Pa. Commw. 77; 350 A.2d 442; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 816


October 8, 1975, Argued  
January 23, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County in case of Redevelopment Authority of the City of Nanticoke v. Theodore G. Spencer, Anna A. Spencer, his wife, and Theodore G. Spencer, Trading and Doing Business as Ted Spencer & Sons Auto Service Center, No. 272 of 1974.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Proceedings remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged an order by the Luzerne County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which upheld appellee City's taking of their property by eminent domain. Appellants claimed that the lower court erred in allowing the condemnation, and when it allowed the taking without applying the proper measure of damages compensating them for the loss.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owners were informed that their property would be condemned by appellee City after a flood and hurricane devastated the area. Appellants claimed that the court erred when it allowed condemnation because property was not taken for a public purpose, the value was improperly measured, they were denied equal protection under the law, and that 26 Pa. Stat. 1-601A et seq., was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the order by the lower court and held that appellants failed to establish that anything illegal occurred that warranted it to strike the condemnation. It found that the taking was proper, and the taking was not capricious or arbitrary. The court also held that 26 Pa. Stat. § 1-406 allowed the condemnation so long as the property was taken for a public purpose and that the owner was justly compensated for the taking. The court found no impropriety and that the assessed value for property taken was fairly calculated. The court also held that the law was constitutional and that no equal protection of the law had occurred. The court affirmed the orders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order holding that appellant property owners' land was taken by appellee City properly under the eminent domain statute. The court held that the statute was constitutional, that it had not violated equal protection laws, and that the property was properly valued.

 

1175 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Fisher


No. 459 C.D. 1975


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


23 Pa. Commw. 25; 350 A.2d 428; 1976 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 813


December 5, 1975, Argued  
January 16, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Edward H. Fisher, No. 74-10,493.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for violating an ordinance by the Lycoming County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which found him guilty, and sentenced him to fines and costs. Defendant claimed that the ordinance under which he was prosecuted was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating a land use ordinance after which he was sentenced to fines and costs. Defendant claimed that the ordinance was unconstitutional. Defendant owned two lots, he conveyed one to his son, and the son immediately reconveyed back to defendant. Defendant claimed that under 53 Pa. Stat. § 10515, he was being arbitrarily restrained from using his land in the way that he saw fit, and that the statute therefore violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court held that so long as the statute relating to land use was used to regulate heath, safety, or welfare of health of citizens, then it would have overridden any private rights held by defendant. The court said that it was satisfied that defendant had not carried the burden of proving that the ordinance was invalid. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for violating a local ordinance requiring documentation of conveyed property. The court held that a land use statute was constitutional so long as its purpose was related to the health, safety, morals and welfare of the citizens of the state.

 

1176 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Lot of Land


no. 89-01568


COMMON PLEAS COURT OF LYCOMING COUNTY, PENNSYLVANIA


1989 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 7; 8 Pa. D. & C.4th 103



November 22, 1989, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: When the Commonwealth notified defendant that it intended to physically seize his residence, pursuant to a court order permitting it to do so, defendant brought a petition for a temporary restraining order/permanent injunction to prevent the Commonwealth from taking or attempting to take possession of his residence and to allow defendant to retain possession pending further proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth sought to forfeit defendant's residence pursuant to the Pennsylvania Controlled Substances Forfeiture Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6801(a)(6)(I)(C) because an informant had purchased controlled substances from defendant at his residence. Defendant argued that he was entitled to a stay of the forfeiture proceedings pending the disposition of criminal charges against him, and that the Act itself was unconstitutional because it provided a civil penalty so punitive in purpose and effect as to negate the General Assembly's intention to provide for a civil penalty. Because the Commonwealth conceded that defendant was entitled to retain his residence pending the outcome of his criminal trial, the court granted the portion of defendant's motion that sought a stay. The court denied the remainder of the motion, however, opining that the Act was not unconstitutional. The court reasoned that the stated purpose of the Act was to remove the incentive to engage in the drug trade, and that the Act's statutory scheme was not so punitive either in purpose or effect so as to negate that intention.


OUTCOME: The court granted the portion of defendant's motion that sought a stay but denied the remainder of the motion.

Harker v. Juniata College


No. 88-0206


COMMON PLEAS COURT OF HUNTINGDON COUNTY, PENNSYLVANIA

1178 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Larrimore v. Doe


no. 3686 Equity of 1989


COMMON PLEAS COURT OF BLAIR COUNTY, PENNSYLVANIA


1989 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 117; 4 Pa. D. & C.4th 186



September 25, 1989, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a natural father and his unborn child, sought a judicial declaration holding that the Abortion Control Act (Pennsylvania) was unconstitutional. The court granted the preliminary injunction to preserve the status quo pending a final hearing.


OVERVIEW: The mother told the father that she intended to have an abortion. The father argued that the Act was unconstitutional because it failed to recognize his rights as the natural father and that a recent decision changed the status of the law about abortion. The court granted the preliminary injunction because an abortion would constitute irreparable harm. The court first determined that it had jurisdiction. Although the mother had filed an application for a stay or dissolution of the preliminary injunction with a superior court and her case was pending, the final hearing was an integral part of the proceedings, and the mother's appeal to the superior court was premature and in violation of the Pennsylvania Rules of Civil Procedure. The court then dissolved the preliminary injunction because it found that the father and the unborn child lacked standing. The father could not veto the mother's fundamental right to make the abortion decision, and the recent decision did not alter the law. The word "person" did not include the unborn child; thus, the unborn child lacked standing.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the preliminary injunction and dismissed plaintiffs' complaint for declaratory judgment. The court entered summary judgment in favor of the mother.

 

1179 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Louden


no. 87-10696


COMMON PLEAS COURT OF LEBANON COUNTY, PENNSYLVANIA


1989 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 122; 4 Pa. D. & C.4th 97



September 8, 1989, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed post-verdict motions in arrest of judgment or, in the alternative, for a new trial. Defendants were husband and wife, and they were convicted by a jury of separate counts of endangering the welfare of a child, violations of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4304.


OVERVIEW: The testimony showed that defendants operated a day-care center in their home. The home was one-half of a double home. While it operated, one defendant's sister began to hear yelling and other noises through the wall in the other home that adjoined defendants' household. The observer heard the noises on her visits to defendants' home, which occurred at least on a daily basis. The observer reported hearing obscene language, arguing over explicit sexual issues, obscenities, threats, and smacking noises followed by children crying and screaming. On appeal, defendants claimed that the trial court erred by allowing the three Commonwealth child witnesses to testify via closed-circuit television and on videotape. The trial court had determined pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5985, which permitted testimony via closed-circuit television, the witnesses could testify. The court held that defendants were entitled to a new trial because fears, anxiety, and mild trauma were not sufficient findings of particularized harm to justify removing a witness from the courtroom during the testimony. The harm was not sufficient to permit the abridgment of defendants' right of confrontation.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motions in arrest of judgment were denied, but defendants' motions for a new trial were granted.

 

1180 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Kohler v. McCrory's Stores


no. 89-SU-02443-01


COMMON PLEAS COURT OF YORK COUNTY, PENNSYLVANIA


1989 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 174; 3 Pa. D. & C.4th 191



August 21, 1989, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Preliminary objections to complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer's demurrer raised a question of lack of subject-matter jurisdiction in a negligence action brought by plaintiff employee against the employer in connection with injuries he received while on the job.


OVERVIEW: The employer employed the employee as a freight handler in a warehouse. While on the job, the employee was injured by another jack operated by a fellow employee. The employee received workers' compensation benefits pursuant to a notice of compensation. The employee then filed the present suit alleging that his employer was liable for the fellow employee's intentional or negligent conduct in failing to provide a safe workplace when the employer knew of the personal animosity between the employee and the fellow employee. The employer demurred to the allegations on three bases. The employer stated that the employee's claim was barred by his election of his workers' compensation remedy; second, that the employee was estopped from alleging that his injury did not arise in the course of his employment; and third, that the claim was barred by the doctrines of collateral estoppel and res judicata. The court held that the employee, who had received workers' compensation benefits for the injuries inflicted by the fellow employee in the course of employment, could not then also sue his employer under the "personal-animus" exception to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 77, § 411.


OUTCOME: The demurrer was sustained and the complaint was dismissed.

 

1181 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Stahl


no. 32 of 1988


COMMON PLEAS COURT OF UNION COUNTY, PENNSYLVANIA


1989 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 126; 4 Pa. D. & C.4th 321



August 11, 1989, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for arrest of judgment in challenging an order of the Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which convicted him for failing to identify himself to a game commission officer in violation of 34 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 904.


OVERVIEW: In responding to a report that shots had been fired, a gaming officer went upon defendant's property to talk to the occupants of a pick-up truck. When defendant came out of the house, the officer asked him to identify himself. The officer testified that defendant refused to do so. The officer cited defendant for violating § 904. The court held that § 904 violated the Fourteenth Amendment because identification had not been defined statutorily or by the courts. By failing to prescribe with clarity under what circumstances an individual could be stopped and asked to produce identification or what a detainee had to do to comply, § 904 vested game commission officers with unbridled discretion to interrogate whomever they choose under any circumstances they chose and left to their sole discretion whether or not the compliance was adequate. Imposing criminal sanctions on an individual who did nothing more than decline to state his name to an officer of the law and who was not the subject of any investigation was a patent violation of the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment that rendered § 904 unconstitutional as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court entered an order overturning defendant's conviction.
